'To express the quadratic \\(4x^2 + 2x - 1\\) in the form \\(a(x+b)^2 + c\\), we need to complete the square.\n\nFirst, factor out the coefficient of \\(x^2\\) from the first two terms:\n\n\\[\n4x^2 + 2x = 4(x^2 + \\frac{1}{2}x)\n\\]\n\nNext, complete the square inside the parentheses. Take half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), square it, and add and subtract it inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + \\frac{1}{2}x = \\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\left(\\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n4\\left(\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{1}{16}\\right) = 4\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{4}{16}\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n4\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{1}{4}\n\\]\n\nNow, include the constant term \\(-1\\) from the original quadratic:\n\n\\[\n4\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{1}{4} - 1 = 4\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{1}{4} - \\frac{4}{4}\n\\]\n\nCombine the constants:\n\n\\[\n4\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{5}{4}\n\\]\n\nThus, the quadratic is expressed in the form \\(a(x+b)^2 + c\\) where \\(a = 4\\), \\(b = \\frac{1}{4}\\), and \\(c = -\\frac{5}{4}\\).\n\nFinally, calculate \\(a + b + c\\):\n\n\\[\na + b + c = 4 + \\frac{1}{4} - \\frac{5}{4} = 4 + \\frac{1}{4} - \\frac{5}{4} = 4 - 1 = 3\n\\]\n\nTherefore, \\(a + b + c = \\boxed{3}\\).'
'Let the two numbers be \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), where \\( x > y \\). We are given the following system of equations:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 25\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx - y = 11\n\\]\n\nTo find the values of \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), we can add the two equations:\n\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 25 + 11\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2x = 36\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 18\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x = 18 \\) back into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n18 + y = 25\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 25 - 18\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 7\n\\]\n\nThus, the smaller of the two numbers is \\(\\boxed{7}\\).'
'To solve for \\( b \\), we start by expanding the expression \\((x+m)^2 - 63\\):\n\n\\[\n(x+m)^2 - 63 = x^2 + 2mx + m^2 - 63\n\\]\n\nThis expression must be equivalent to the original quadratic \\( x^2 + bx + 1 \\). By comparing coefficients, we have:\n\n1. The coefficient of \\( x \\) gives us \\( 2m = b \\).\n2. The constant term gives us \\( m^2 - 63 = 1 \\).\n\nFrom the second equation, we solve for \\( m \\):\n\n\\[\nm^2 - 63 = 1 \\implies m^2 = 64 \\implies m = 8 \\text{ or } m = -8\n\\]\n\nSince \\( b \\) is positive, we choose \\( m = 8 \\). Substituting \\( m = 8 \\) into the equation \\( 2m = b \\), we find:\n\n\\[\nb = 2 \\times 8 = 16\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( b \\) is \\(\\boxed{16}\\).'
"To solve for the pair \\((a, b)\\), we use Vieta's formulas, which relate the coefficients of a polynomial to sums and products of its roots. For the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + ax + b = 0\\), Vieta's formulas tell us:\n\n1. The sum of the roots \\(a + b = -a\\).\n2. The product of the roots \\(ab = b\\).\n\nFrom the first equation, \\(a + b = -a\\), we can solve for \\(b\\):\n\\[\na + b = -a \\implies b = -2a.\n\\]\n\nFrom the second equation, \\(ab = b\\), we can solve for \\(a\\):\n\\[\nab = b \\implies b(a - 1) = 0.\n\\]\n\nSince \\(b\\) is nonzero, we have \\(a - 1 = 0\\), which gives \\(a = 1\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(a = 1\\) into \\(b = -2a\\), we find:\n\\[\nb = -2(1) = -2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the pair \\((a, b)\\) is \\((1, -2)\\).\n\nTherefore, the solution is \\((a, b) = \\boxed{(1, -2)}\\)."
'To find the y-intercept of the polynomial \\( Q(x) = P(x)^2 \\), we need to evaluate \\( Q(x) \\) at \\( x = 0 \\).\n\nFirst, evaluate \\( P(x) \\) at \\( x = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\nP(0) = 4(0)^3 - 2(0)^2 + 7(0) - 1 = -1\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute this into \\( Q(x) \\):\n\n\\[\nQ(x) = P(x)^2 \\implies Q(0) = (P(0))^2 = (-1)^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the y-intercept of \\( Q(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'Let the length of the plot be \\( l \\) feet. Then the width of the plot is \\( l + 5 \\) feet. The area of the plot is given by:\n\n\\[\nl \\times (l + 5) \\geq 500\n\\]\n\nExpanding the expression, we have:\n\n\\[\nl^2 + 5l \\geq 500\n\\]\n\nTo find the minimum value of \\( l \\), we solve the equation:\n\n\\[\nl^2 + 5l - 500 = 0\n\\]\n\nUsing the quadratic formula \\( l = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 5 \\), and \\( c = -500 \\), we find:\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{5^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-500)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{25 + 2000}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{2025}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{-5 \\pm 45}{2}\n\\]\n\nThe two solutions are:\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{40}{2} = 20 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad l = \\frac{-50}{2} = -25\n\\]\n\nSince the length cannot be negative, we have \\( l = 20 \\).\n\nThus, the width of the plot is:\n\n\\[\nl + 5 = 20 + 5 = 25\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the width of the plot is \\(\\boxed{25}\\) feet.'
'The inequality \\(x^2 + bx + c > 0\\) holds only when \\(x \\in (-\\infty, -2) \\cup (3, \\infty)\\). This implies that the quadratic \\(x^2 + bx + c\\) has roots at \\(x = -2\\) and \\(x = 3\\), and the parabola opens upwards (since the coefficient of \\(x^2\\) is positive).\n\nThe roots of the quadratic are \\(-2\\) and \\(3\\). Therefore, the quadratic can be expressed in factored form as:\n\n\\[\n(x + 2)(x - 3)\n\\]\n\nExpanding this, we have:\n\n\\[\nx^2 - 3x + 2x - 6 = x^2 - x - 6\n\\]\n\nThus, comparing with the standard form \\(x^2 + bx + c\\), we identify:\n\n\\[\nb = -1 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad c = -6\n\\]\n\nWe are asked to find the value of \\(b + c\\):\n\n\\[\nb + c = -1 + (-6) = -7\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(b + c\\) is \\(\\boxed{-7}\\).'
"To find the coordinates \\((x, y)\\) given that the midpoint of the line segment between \\((x, y)\\) and \\((-9, 1)\\) is \\((3, -5)\\), we use the midpoint formula. The midpoint \\((M_x, M_y)\\) of a line segment with endpoints \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nM_x = \\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\quad M_y = \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2}\n\\]\n\nIn this problem, the midpoint is \\((3, -5)\\), and one endpoint is \\((-9, 1)\\). Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x + (-9)}{2} = 3 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad \\frac{y + 1}{2} = -5\n\\]\n\nLet's solve these equations one by one.\n\n1. Solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x - 9}{2} = 3\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 2:\n\n\\[\nx - 9 = 6\n\\]\n\nAdd 9 to both sides:\n\n\\[\nx = 15\n\\]\n\n2. Solve for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{y + 1}{2} = -5\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 2:\n\n\\[\ny + 1 = -10\n\\]\n\nSubtract 1 from both sides:\n\n\\[\ny = -11\n\\]\n\nThus, the coordinates \\((x, y)\\) are \\((15, -11)\\).\n\nThe answer is \\((15, -11)\\)."
'To calculate \\(42^2\\), Emily uses the identity for the square of a binomial:\n\n\\[\n42^2 = (40 + 2)^2 = 40^2 + 2 \\times 40 \\times 2 + 2^2 = 40^2 + 160 + 4 = 40^2 + 164\n\\]\n\nSimilarly, to calculate \\(38^2\\), we use the identity:\n\n\\[\n38^2 = (40 - 2)^2 = 40^2 - 2 \\times 40 \\times 2 + 2^2 = 40^2 - 160 + 4 = 40^2 - 156\n\\]\n\nThus, Emily subtracts \\(156\\) from \\(40^2\\) to calculate \\(38^2\\). Therefore, the number she subtracts is \\(\\boxed{156}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to find the equation of line \\( a \\), which is parallel to line \\( b \\). We know that line \\( b \\) is perpendicular to line \\( c \\), whose equation is \\( y = -2x + 3 \\).\n\nFirst, let's determine the slope of line \\( c \\). The equation \\( y = -2x + 3 \\) is in slope-intercept form \\( y = mx + b \\), where \\( m \\) is the slope. Thus, the slope of line \\( c \\) is \\(-2\\).\n\nSince line \\( b \\) is perpendicular to line \\( c \\), the slope of line \\( b \\) is the negative reciprocal of the slope of line \\( c \\). Therefore, the slope of line \\( b \\) is \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\).\n\nLine \\( a \\) is parallel to line \\( b \\), so it must have the same slope as line \\( b \\). Therefore, the slope of line \\( a \\) is also \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\).\n\nNow, we know that line \\( a \\) passes through the point \\((1, 2)\\) and has a slope of \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\). We can use the point-slope form of a line to find the equation of line \\( a \\):\n\n\\[\ny - y_1 = m(x - x_1)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the point \\((1, 2)\\) and the slope \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\) into the equation, we get:\n\n\\[\ny - 2 = \\frac{1}{2}(x - 1)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying this equation:\n\n\\[\ny - 2 = \\frac{1}{2}x - \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{1}{2}x - \\frac{1}{2} + 2\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{1}{2}x + \\frac{3}{2}\n\\]\n\nThe y-intercept of line \\( a \\) is the constant term in the equation, which is \\(\\frac{3}{2}\\).\n\nThus, the y-intercept of line \\( a \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{3}{2}}\\)."
'To solve for \\( y \\) given the equation \\(\\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{y} = \\frac{1}{z}\\), we start by substituting the given values \\( x = 25 \\) and \\( z = 24 \\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{25} + \\frac{1}{y} = \\frac{1}{24}\n\\]\n\nNext, we isolate \\(\\frac{1}{y}\\) by subtracting \\(\\frac{1}{25}\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{y} = \\frac{1}{24} - \\frac{1}{25}\n\\]\n\nTo perform the subtraction, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 24 and 25 is 600. We rewrite each fraction with this common denominator:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{24} = \\frac{25}{600}, \\quad \\frac{1}{25} = \\frac{24}{600}\n\\]\n\nNow, subtract the fractions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{y} = \\frac{25}{600} - \\frac{24}{600} = \\frac{1}{600}\n\\]\n\nTaking the reciprocal of both sides gives:\n\n\\[\ny = 600\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( y \\) is \\(\\boxed{600}\\).'
'To solve the quadratic equation \\(0 = -9x^2 - 3x + 2\\), we can use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nFor the given equation, the coefficients are \\(a = -9\\), \\(b = -3\\), and \\(c = 2\\). Plugging these into the quadratic formula gives:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-(-3) \\pm \\sqrt{(-3)^2 - 4(-9)(2)}}{2(-9)}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying inside the square root:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{3 \\pm \\sqrt{9 + 72}}{-18}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{3 \\pm \\sqrt{81}}{-18}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{3 \\pm 9}{-18}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two potential solutions:\n\n1. \\(x = \\frac{3 + 9}{-18} = \\frac{12}{-18} = -\\frac{2}{3}\\)\n\n2. \\(x = \\frac{3 - 9}{-18} = \\frac{-6}{-18} = \\frac{1}{3}\\)\n\nSince we are looking for the solution where \\(x > 0\\), we choose \\(x = \\frac{1}{3}\\).\n\nThus, the solution is \\(x = \\boxed{\\frac{1}{3}}\\).'
"According to Ohm's law, \\( V = IR \\). We are given that when \\( I = 40 \\) amperes and \\( R = 3 \\) ohms, the voltage \\( V \\) is:\n\n\\[\nV = 40 \\times 3 = 120 \\text{ volts}\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the current \\( I \\) when the resistance \\( R \\) is 20 ohms, while keeping the voltage constant at 120 volts. Using Ohm's law again:\n\n\\[\nV = IR \\implies 120 = I \\times 20\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( I \\):\n\n\\[\nI = \\frac{120}{20} = 6 \\text{ amperes}\n\\]\n\nThus, the amount of current when the resistance is 20 ohms is \\(\\boxed{6}\\) amperes."
"To solve the inequality \\(\\frac{1}{5}|9+2a| < 1\\), we first eliminate the fraction by multiplying both sides by 5:\n\n\\[\n|9 + 2a| < 5\n\\]\n\nThis inequality implies two separate inequalities:\n\n1. \\(9 + 2a < 5\\)\n2. \\(9 + 2a > -5\\)\n\nLet's solve each inequality separately.\n\n**For the first inequality:**\n\n\\[\n9 + 2a < 5\n\\]\n\nSubtract 9 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2a < 5 - 9\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2a < -4\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 2:\n\n\\[\na < -2\n\\]\n\n**For the second inequality:**\n\n\\[\n9 + 2a > -5\n\\]\n\nSubtract 9 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2a > -5 - 9\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2a > -14\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 2:\n\n\\[\na > -7\n\\]\n\nCombining these two results, we have:\n\n\\[\n-7 < a < -2\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution in interval notation is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{(-7, -2)}\n\\]"
"To find the value of \\( f(g(4)) - g(f(3)) \\), we need to evaluate each function step by step.\n\nFirst, let's evaluate \\( g(4) \\):\n\\[\ng(x) = \\sqrt{2x + 1}\n\\]\n\\[\ng(4) = \\sqrt{2(4) + 1} = \\sqrt{8 + 1} = \\sqrt{9} = 3\n\\]\n\nNext, we evaluate \\( f(g(4)) = f(3) \\):\n\\[\nf(x) = x^2 - 2x + 1\n\\]\n\\[\nf(3) = 3^2 - 2(3) + 1 = 9 - 6 + 1 = 4\n\\]\n\nNow, let's evaluate \\( f(3) \\) again for the purpose of finding \\( g(f(3)) \\):\n\\[\nf(3) = 4\n\\]\n\nThen, evaluate \\( g(f(3)) = g(4) \\):\n\\[\ng(4) = 3\n\\]\n\nFinally, calculate \\( f(g(4)) - g(f(3)) \\):\n\\[\nf(g(4)) - g(f(3)) = f(3) - g(4) = 4 - 3 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(g(4)) - g(f(3)) \\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."
'To find the value of \\( f(-2) \\) for the function \\( f(x) = 5x^2 + 3x + 4 \\), we substitute \\( x = -2 \\) into the function:\n\n\\[\nf(-2) = 5(-2)^2 + 3(-2) + 4\n\\]\n\nFirst, calculate \\( (-2)^2 \\):\n\n\\[\n(-2)^2 = 4\n\\]\n\nNow substitute this back into the expression:\n\n\\[\nf(-2) = 5 \\times 4 + 3 \\times (-2) + 4\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\n\\[\n5 \\times 4 = 20\n\\]\n\\[\n3 \\times (-2) = -6\n\\]\n\nNow add these results together:\n\n\\[\nf(-2) = 20 - 6 + 4\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\n\\[\nf(-2) = 18\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(-2) \\) is \\(\\boxed{18}\\).'
"To find the number of polynomials of the form \\(x^2 + mx + n\\) with positive integer roots and \\(n = 28\\), we start by considering the roots of the polynomial. Let the roots be \\(p\\) and \\(q\\), both positive integers. By Vieta's formulas, we have:\n\n1. \\(p + q = -m\\)\n2. \\(pq = n = 28\\)\n\nSince \\(pq = 28\\), we need to find all pairs \\((p, q)\\) of positive integers such that their product is 28. The positive integer factor pairs of 28 are:\n\n\\[\n(1, 28), (2, 14), (4, 7), (7, 4), (14, 2), (28, 1)\n\\]\n\nFor each pair \\((p, q)\\), we can determine the value of \\(m\\) using the equation \\(p + q = -m\\). However, since \\(m\\) is the coefficient of \\(x\\) in the polynomial \\(x^2 + mx + n\\), we actually have:\n\n\\[\nm = -(p + q)\n\\]\n\nLet's calculate \\(m\\) for each pair:\n\n- For \\((p, q) = (1, 28)\\), \\(p + q = 1 + 28 = 29\\), so \\(m = -29\\).\n- For \\((p, q) = (2, 14)\\), \\(p + q = 2 + 14 = 16\\), so \\(m = -16\\).\n- For \\((p, q) = (4, 7)\\), \\(p + q = 4 + 7 = 11\\), so \\(m = -11\\).\n- For \\((p, q) = (7, 4)\\), \\(p + q = 7 + 4 = 11\\), so \\(m = -11\\).\n- For \\((p, q) = (14, 2)\\), \\(p + q = 14 + 2 = 16\\), so \\(m = -16\\).\n- For \\((p, q) = (28, 1)\\), \\(p + q = 28 + 1 = 29\\), so \\(m = -29\\).\n\nEach pair \\((p, q)\\) corresponds to a unique polynomial \\(x^2 + mx + 28\\). Therefore, there are 6 such polynomials, corresponding to the 6 factor pairs of 28.\n\nThus, the number of polynomials is \\(\\boxed{6}\\)."

'To find the value of \\( b \\) such that \\( F(6, b, 4, 3) = 48 \\), we start by using the function definition:\n\n\\[\nF(a, b, c, d) = a^b + c \\times d\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values into the function, we have:\n\n\\[\nF(6, b, 4, 3) = 6^b + 4 \\times 3\n\\]\n\nWe know that:\n\n\\[\n6^b + 4 \\times 3 = 48\n\\]\n\nCalculating \\( 4 \\times 3 \\), we get:\n\n\\[\n4 \\times 3 = 12\n\\]\n\nSubstituting back, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n6^b + 12 = 48\n\\]\n\nSubtract 12 from both sides to isolate \\( 6^b \\):\n\n\\[\n6^b = 48 - 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\n6^b = 36\n\\]\n\nNow, we solve for \\( b \\) by recognizing that \\( 36 \\) is a power of 6:\n\n\\[\n6^b = 6^2\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( b = 2 \\).\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( b \\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
'To solve the problem, we need to evaluate the expression \\((3 \\star 5) - (5 \\star 3)\\) using the operation \\(\\star\\) defined by \\(a \\star b = (a + b)b\\).\n\nFirst, calculate \\(3 \\star 5\\):\n\\[\n3 \\star 5 = (3 + 5) \\cdot 5 = 8 \\cdot 5 = 40\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate \\(5 \\star 3\\):\n\\[\n5 \\star 3 = (5 + 3) \\cdot 3 = 8 \\cdot 3 = 24\n\\]\n\nNow, find the difference \\((3 \\star 5) - (5 \\star 3)\\):\n\\[\n(3 \\star 5) - (5 \\star 3) = 40 - 24 = 16\n\\]\n\nThus, the result is \\(\\boxed{16}\\).'
'To find the coordinates of the point on the line \\(5x - 9y = 42\\) where the \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) coordinates are additive inverses of each other, we set \\(y = -x\\).\n\nSubstitute \\(y = -x\\) into the equation of the line:\n\n\\[\n5x - 9(-x) = 42\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[\n5x + 9x = 42\n\\]\n\n\\[\n14x = 42\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{42}{14} = 3\n\\]\n\nSince \\(y = -x\\), we have:\n\n\\[\ny = -3\n\\]\n\nThus, the coordinates of the point are \\((3, -3)\\).\n\nThe answer is \\((3, -3)\\).'
'To solve the equation \\((17^6 - 17^5) \\div 16 = 17^x\\), we start by simplifying the expression on the left-hand side.\n\nFirst, factor out \\(17^5\\) from the terms inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\n17^6 - 17^5 = 17^5(17 - 1) = 17^5 \\cdot 16\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute this back into the original equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{17^5 \\cdot 16}{16} = 17^x\n\\]\n\nThe \\(16\\) in the numerator and denominator cancel each other out:\n\n\\[\n17^5 = 17^x\n\\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we equate the exponents:\n\n\\[\nx = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\).'
"To find the smallest distance between the origin and a point on the parabola \\( y = x^2 - 5 \\), we need to minimize the distance function from the origin to a point \\((x, y)\\) on the parabola. The distance \\( D \\) from the origin \\((0, 0)\\) to a point \\((x, y)\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{x^2 + y^2}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( y = x^2 - 5 \\), we substitute for \\( y \\) in the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{x^2 + (x^2 - 5)^2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expression inside the square root:\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{x^2 + (x^2 - 5)^2} = \\sqrt{x^2 + (x^4 - 10x^2 + 25)}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{x^4 - 9x^2 + 25}\n\\]\n\nTo find the minimum distance, we minimize the function \\( f(x) = x^4 - 9x^2 + 25 \\). We do this by finding the derivative and setting it to zero:\n\n\\[\nf'(x) = 4x^3 - 18x\n\\]\n\nSetting the derivative equal to zero:\n\n\\[\n4x^3 - 18x = 0\n\\]\n\nFactoring out \\( 2x \\):\n\n\\[\n2x(2x^2 - 9) = 0\n\\]\n\nThis gives the solutions:\n\n\\[\nx = 0 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad 2x^2 - 9 = 0\n\\]\n\nSolving \\( 2x^2 - 9 = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\n2x^2 = 9 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x^2 = \\frac{9}{2} \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = \\pm \\sqrt{\\frac{9}{2}} = \\pm \\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\n\\]\n\nWe have three critical points: \\( x = 0 \\), \\( x = \\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\), and \\( x = -\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\). We evaluate \\( f(x) \\) at these points:\n\n1. \\( x = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\nf(0) = 0^4 - 9 \\cdot 0^2 + 25 = 25\n\\]\n\n2. \\( x = \\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\):\n\n\\[\nf\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right) = \\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right)^4 - 9\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right)^2 + 25\n\\]\n\nCalculating each term:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{9 \\cdot 2}{4} = \\frac{18}{4} = \\frac{9}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right)^4 = \\left(\\frac{9}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{81}{4}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back:\n\n\\[\nf\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right) = \\frac{81}{4} - 9 \\cdot \\frac{9}{2} + 25 = \\frac{81}{4} - \\frac{81}{2} + 25\n\\]\n\nConvert to a common denominator:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{81}{4} - \\frac{162}{4} + \\frac{100}{4} = \\frac{81 - 162 + 100}{4} = \\frac{19}{4}\n\\]\n\n3. \\( x = -\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\) yields the same result as \\( x = \\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\) due to symmetry.\n\nThe minimum value of \\( f(x) \\) is \\(\\frac{19}{4}\\), so the minimum distance \\( D \\) is:\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{\\frac{19}{4}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{19}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( a = 19 \\) and \\( b = 2 \\), so \\( a + b = 19 + 2 = \\boxed{21} \\)."
"To solve the equation \\( x\\sqrt{x} - 5x - 9\\sqrt{x} = 35 \\), we start by making a substitution. Let \\( y = \\sqrt{x} \\). Then \\( x = y^2 \\), and the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\ny^2 \\cdot y - 5y^2 - 9y = 35\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\ny^3 - 5y^2 - 9y = 35\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\ny^3 - 5y^2 - 9y - 35 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe need to find integer solutions for \\( y \\). We can use the Rational Root Theorem, which suggests that any rational root, in this case an integer, is a factor of the constant term, \\(-35\\). The factors of \\(-35\\) are \\(\\pm 1, \\pm 5, \\pm 7, \\pm 35\\).\n\nLet's test these possible values for \\( y \\):\n\n1. **\\( y = 5 \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   y^3 - 5y^2 - 9y - 35 = 5^3 - 5 \\cdot 5^2 - 9 \\cdot 5 - 35\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   = 125 - 125 - 45 - 35 = 125 - 125 - 45 - 35 = 0\n   \\]\n\n   So, \\( y = 5 \\) is a root.\n\nSince \\( y = \\sqrt{x} \\), we have \\( \\sqrt{x} = 5 \\), which implies \\( x = 5^2 = 25 \\).\n\nThus, the integer value of \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{25}\\)."
'To solve for \\( x^2y \\), we start with the given equations:\n\n1. \\( x^2 + y = 4 \\)\n2. \\( x^4 + y^2 = 10 \\)\n\nFrom equation (1), we can express \\( y \\) in terms of \\( x^2 \\):\n\n\\[\ny = 4 - x^2\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( y \\) into equation (2):\n\n\\[\nx^4 + (4 - x^2)^2 = 10\n\\]\n\nExpand the square:\n\n\\[\nx^4 + (16 - 8x^2 + x^4) = 10\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n2x^4 - 8x^2 + 16 = 10\n\\]\n\nSubtract 10 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2x^4 - 8x^2 + 6 = 0\n\\]\n\nDivide the entire equation by 2:\n\n\\[\nx^4 - 4x^2 + 3 = 0\n\\]\n\nLet \\( z = x^2 \\). Then the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\nz^2 - 4z + 3 = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in \\( z \\). Solve it using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nz = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -4 \\), and \\( c = 3 \\):\n\n\\[\nz = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{(-4)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 3}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\\[\nz = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 - 12}}{2}\n\\]\n\\[\nz = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{4}}{2}\n\\]\n\\[\nz = \\frac{4 \\pm 2}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions for \\( z \\):\n\n\\[\nz = \\frac{6}{2} = 3 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad z = \\frac{2}{2} = 1\n\\]\n\nRecall that \\( z = x^2 \\), so:\n\n1. If \\( x^2 = 3 \\), then from equation (1), \\( y = 4 - 3 = 1 \\).\n2. If \\( x^2 = 1 \\), then from equation (1), \\( y = 4 - 1 = 3 \\).\n\nNow, calculate \\( x^2y \\) for each case:\n\n- If \\( x^2 = 3 \\) and \\( y = 1 \\), then \\( x^2y = 3 \\times 1 = 3 \\).\n- If \\( x^2 = 1 \\) and \\( y = 3 \\), then \\( x^2y = 1 \\times 3 = 3 \\).\n\nIn both cases, \\( x^2y = 3 \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^2y \\) is \\(\\boxed{3}\\).'
'To expand the product \\((x+1)^2 \\cdot x\\), we first expand \\((x+1)^2\\) and then multiply the result by \\(x\\).\n\nFirst, expand \\((x+1)^2\\):\n\\[\n(x+1)^2 = (x+1)(x+1) = x^2 + 2x + 1\n\\]\n\nNow, multiply this result by \\(x\\):\n\\[\n(x^2 + 2x + 1) \\cdot x = x^2 \\cdot x + 2x \\cdot x + 1 \\cdot x\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\\[\nx^2 \\cdot x = x^3\n\\]\n\\[\n2x \\cdot x = 2x^2\n\\]\n\\[\n1 \\cdot x = x\n\\]\n\nCombine these terms:\n\\[\nx^3 + 2x^2 + x\n\\]\n\nThus, the expanded form of \\((x+1)^2 \\cdot x\\) is \\(\\boxed{x^3 + 2x^2 + x}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to understand the relationship between the two arithmetic sequences.\n\nLet's denote the first sequence as \\( a_n \\) and the second sequence as \\( b_n \\).\n\nGiven:\n- The first term of the first sequence is \\( a_1 = 0 \\).\n- The second term of the first sequence is \\( a_2 = a_1 + b_1 = 0 + b_1 = b_1 \\).\n- The third term of the first sequence is \\( a_3 = a_2 + b_2 = b_1 + b_2 \\).\n- The fourth term of the first sequence is \\( a_4 = a_3 + b_3 = b_1 + b_2 + b_3 \\).\n- The fifth term of the first sequence is \\( a_5 = a_4 + b_4 = b_1 + b_2 + b_3 + b_4 \\).\n\nWe are given that the fifth term of the second sequence is \\( b_5 = 3 \\).\n\nSince the second sequence is arithmetic, we can express the terms of the second sequence as:\n- \\( b_1 = b \\)\n- \\( b_2 = b + d \\)\n- \\( b_3 = b + 2d \\)\n- \\( b_4 = b + 3d \\)\n- \\( b_5 = b + 4d = 3 \\)\n\nFrom \\( b_5 = b + 4d = 3 \\), we can express \\( b \\) in terms of \\( d \\):\n\\[ b = 3 - 4d \\]\n\nNow, let's find the fifth term of the first sequence:\n\\[ a_5 = b_1 + b_2 + b_3 + b_4 \\]\n\\[ a_5 = b + (b + d) + (b + 2d) + (b + 3d) \\]\n\\[ a_5 = 4b + 6d \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( b = 3 - 4d \\) into the expression for \\( a_5 \\):\n\\[ a_5 = 4(3 - 4d) + 6d \\]\n\\[ a_5 = 12 - 16d + 6d \\]\n\\[ a_5 = 12 - 10d \\]\n\nSince we do not have a specific value for \\( d \\), we cannot simplify further without additional information. However, the expression for the fifth term of the first sequence is:\n\\[ a_5 = 12 - 10d \\]\n\nIf we assume \\( d = 0 \\) (which is a common assumption if no other information is given), then:\n\\[ a_5 = 12 - 10 \\times 0 = 12 \\]\n\nThus, the fifth term of the first sequence is \\( \\boxed{12} \\)."
'To solve the equation \\(\\log_5(x-18) = 2\\), we need to rewrite it in exponential form. The equation \\(\\log_5(x-18) = 2\\) means that the base 5 raised to the power of 2 equals \\(x-18\\). Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\nx - 18 = 5^2\n\\]\n\nCalculating \\(5^2\\), we get:\n\n\\[\nx - 18 = 25\n\\]\n\nTo find \\(x\\), add 18 to both sides of the equation:\n\n\\[\nx = 25 + 18\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 43\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{43}\\).'
'To find the coefficient of \\( x \\) in the expression \n\n\\[\n(1+2x) - 2(1+2x+3x^2) + 3(1+2x+3x^2+4x^3) - 4(1+2x+3x^2+4x^3+5x^4),\n\\]\n\nwe first expand each term and then collect the coefficients of \\( x \\).\n\n1. The first term is \\( 1 + 2x \\). The coefficient of \\( x \\) is \\( 2 \\).\n\n2. The second term is \\( -2(1 + 2x + 3x^2) \\). Expanding this, we get:\n   \\[\n   -2 \\cdot 1 - 2 \\cdot 2x - 2 \\cdot 3x^2 = -2 - 4x - 6x^2.\n   \\]\n   The coefficient of \\( x \\) is \\( -4 \\).\n\n3. The third term is \\( 3(1 + 2x + 3x^2 + 4x^3) \\). Expanding this, we get:\n   \\[\n   3 \\cdot 1 + 3 \\cdot 2x + 3 \\cdot 3x^2 + 3 \\cdot 4x^3 = 3 + 6x + 9x^2 + 12x^3.\n   \\]\n   The coefficient of \\( x \\) is \\( 6 \\).\n\n4. The fourth term is \\( -4(1 + 2x + 3x^2 + 4x^3 + 5x^4) \\). Expanding this, we get:\n   \\[\n   -4 \\cdot 1 - 4 \\cdot 2x - 4 \\cdot 3x^2 - 4 \\cdot 4x^3 - 4 \\cdot 5x^4 = -4 - 8x - 12x^2 - 16x^3 - 20x^4.\n   \\]\n   The coefficient of \\( x \\) is \\( -8 \\).\n\nNow, we sum the coefficients of \\( x \\) from each term:\n\n\\[\n2 + (-4) + 6 + (-8) = 2 - 4 + 6 - 8 = -4.\n\\]\n\nThus, the coefficient of \\( x \\) in the simplified expression is \\(\\boxed{-4}\\).'
"Let's denote John's age as \\(10a + b\\), where \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) are the digits of John's age. Then, his father's age, which is the reverse of John's age, is \\(10b + a\\).\n\nWe are given two conditions:\n1. The positive difference between their ages is 27 years:\n   \\[\n   |(10a + b) - (10b + a)| = 27\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we have:\n   \\[\n   |9a - 9b| = 27 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad |a - b| = 3\n   \\]\n\n2. The sum of the digits in each age is 5:\n   \\[\n   a + b = 5\n   \\]\n\nWe need to solve these equations simultaneously. Let's consider the two cases for \\(|a - b| = 3\\):\n\n**Case 1:** \\(a - b = 3\\)\n\nFrom \\(a + b = 5\\), we can solve for \\(a\\) and \\(b\\):\n\\[\na + b = 5 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad a - b = 3\n\\]\nAdding these equations, we get:\n\\[\n2a = 8 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad a = 4\n\\]\nSubstituting \\(a = 4\\) into \\(a + b = 5\\):\n\\[\n4 + b = 5 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad b = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, John's age is \\(10a + b = 10 \\times 4 + 1 = 41\\), and his father's age is \\(10b + a = 10 \\times 1 + 4 = 14\\).\n\n**Case 2:** \\(b - a = 3\\)\n\nFrom \\(a + b = 5\\), we can solve for \\(a\\) and \\(b\\):\n\\[\na + b = 5 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad b - a = 3\n\\]\nAdding these equations, we get:\n\\[\n2b = 8 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad b = 4\n\\]\nSubstituting \\(b = 4\\) into \\(a + b = 5\\):\n\\[\na + 4 = 5 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad a = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, John's age is \\(10a + b = 10 \\times 1 + 4 = 14\\), and his father's age is \\(10b + a = 10 \\times 4 + 1 = 41\\).\n\nIn both cases, the father's age is 41. Therefore, the number of years in John's father's age is \\(\\boxed{41}\\)."
'To solve this problem, we need to consider the process of recycling the cans iteratively. We start with 125 aluminum cans and recycle them to make new cans. Each new can requires 5 old cans.\n\n1. **First Iteration:**\n   - We have 125 cans.\n   - We can make \\( \\left\\lfloor \\frac{125}{5} \\right\\rfloor = 25 \\) new cans.\n   - After making these 25 new cans, we have \\( 125 - 25 \\times 5 = 0 \\) leftover cans.\n\n2. **Second Iteration:**\n   - We now have 25 new cans from the first iteration.\n   - We can recycle these to make \\( \\left\\lfloor \\frac{25}{5} \\right\\rfloor = 5 \\) new cans.\n   - After making these 5 new cans, we have \\( 25 - 5 \\times 5 = 0 \\) leftover cans.\n\n3. **Third Iteration:**\n   - We now have 5 new cans from the second iteration.\n   - We can recycle these to make \\( \\left\\lfloor \\frac{5}{5} \\right\\rfloor = 1 \\) new can.\n   - After making this 1 new can, we have \\( 5 - 1 \\times 5 = 0 \\) leftover cans.\n\n4. **Fourth Iteration:**\n   - We now have 1 new can from the third iteration.\n   - We cannot recycle this into a new can because \\( \\left\\lfloor \\frac{1}{5} \\right\\rfloor = 0 \\).\n\nAdding up all the new cans made in each iteration, we have:\n- 25 new cans from the first iteration,\n- 5 new cans from the second iteration,\n- 1 new can from the third iteration.\n\nThus, the total number of new cans that can eventually be made is \\( 25 + 5 + 1 = 31 \\).\n\nTherefore, the number of new cans that can eventually be made from 125 aluminum cans is \\(\\boxed{31}\\).'
'To solve the problem, we need to calculate \\(50\\%\\) of \\(200\\%\\) of \\(10\\).\n\nFirst, calculate \\(200\\%\\) of \\(10\\):\n\\[\n200\\% \\text{ of } 10 = \\left(\\frac{200}{100}\\right) \\times 10 = 2 \\times 10 = 20\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate \\(50\\%\\) of the result from the previous step:\n\\[\n50\\% \\text{ of } 20 = \\left(\\frac{50}{100}\\right) \\times 20 = 0.5 \\times 20 = 10\n\\]\n\nTherefore, \\(50\\%\\) of \\(200\\%\\) of \\(10\\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
'To rewrite the quadratic \\(3x^2 - 24x + 72\\) in the form \\(a(x+b)^2 + c\\), we first complete the square.\n\n1. **Factor out the leading coefficient from the quadratic and linear terms:**\n\n   \\[\n   3(x^2 - 8x) + 72\n   \\]\n\n2. **Complete the square inside the parentheses:**\n\n   - Take half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), which is \\(-8\\), and square it: \\(\\left(\\frac{-8}{2}\\right)^2 = 16\\).\n   - Add and subtract this square inside the parentheses:\n\n   \\[\n   3(x^2 - 8x + 16 - 16) + 72\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   = 3((x-4)^2 - 16) + 72\n   \\]\n\n3. **Distribute the 3 and simplify:**\n\n   \\[\n   = 3(x-4)^2 - 48 + 72\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   = 3(x-4)^2 + 24\n   \\]\n\nNow, the quadratic is in the form \\(a(x+b)^2 + c\\) where \\(a = 3\\), \\(b = -4\\), and \\(c = 24\\).\n\n4. **Calculate \\(a + b + c\\):**\n\n   \\[\n   a + b + c = 3 + (-4) + 24 = 3 - 4 + 24 = 23\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(a + b + c\\) is \\(\\boxed{23}\\).'
'Given that \\(a, b, c, d\\) form an increasing arithmetic sequence, we can express them as:\n\\[\nb = a + k, \\quad c = a + 2k, \\quad d = a + 3k\n\\]\nfor some positive \\(k\\).\n\nAdditionally, since \\(a, b, d\\) form a geometric sequence, we have:\n\\[\n\\frac{b}{a} = \\frac{d}{b}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the expressions for \\(b\\) and \\(d\\), we get:\n\\[\n\\frac{a+k}{a} = \\frac{a+3k}{a+k}\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\\[\n(a+k)^2 = a(a+3k)\n\\]\n\nExpanding both sides, we have:\n\\[\na^2 + 2ak + k^2 = a^2 + 3ak\n\\]\n\nSubtracting \\(a^2\\) from both sides, we obtain:\n\\[\n2ak + k^2 = 3ak\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms, we find:\n\\[\nk^2 = ak\n\\]\n\nSince \\(k\\) is positive, we can divide both sides by \\(k\\):\n\\[\nk = a\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(k = a\\) back into the expressions for \\(b\\), \\(c\\), and \\(d\\), we have:\n\\[\nb = a + a = 2a, \\quad c = a + 2a = 3a, \\quad d = a + 3a = 4a\n\\]\n\nThus, the sequence is \\(a, 2a, 3a, 4a\\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\):\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{d} = \\frac{a}{4a} = \\frac{1}{4}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{4}}\\).'
'To solve for \\( w \\) in the equation \\(\\frac{1\\frac{1}{6}}{w} = \\frac{42}{3}\\), we first simplify both sides of the equation.\n\nFirst, convert the mixed number \\(1\\frac{1}{6}\\) to an improper fraction:\n\\[\n1\\frac{1}{6} = \\frac{6}{6} + \\frac{1}{6} = \\frac{7}{6}\n\\]\n\nNow, the equation becomes:\n\\[\n\\frac{\\frac{7}{6}}{w} = \\frac{42}{3}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the right side of the equation:\n\\[\n\\frac{42}{3} = 14\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation is:\n\\[\n\\frac{7}{6w} = 14\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( w \\), multiply both sides by \\( w \\) to eliminate the fraction:\n\\[\n\\frac{7}{6} = 14w\n\\]\n\nNext, solve for \\( w \\) by dividing both sides by 14:\n\\[\nw = \\frac{7}{6 \\times 14}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\\[\nw = \\frac{7}{84}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction by dividing the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 7:\n\\[\nw = \\frac{1}{12}\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is:\n\\[\nw = \\boxed{\\frac{1}{12}}\n\\]'
'To solve the equation \\(\\lceil x \\rceil + x = \\frac{23}{7}\\), we start by letting \\(\\lceil x \\rceil = n\\), where \\(n\\) is an integer. This implies that \\(n - 1 < x \\leq n\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(n\\) for \\(\\lceil x \\rceil\\) in the equation, we have:\n\n\\[\nn + x = \\frac{23}{7}\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(x\\), we get:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{23}{7} - n\n\\]\n\nSince \\(n - 1 < x \\leq n\\), we substitute \\(x = \\frac{23}{7} - n\\) into this inequality:\n\n\\[\nn - 1 < \\frac{23}{7} - n \\leq n\n\\]\n\nWe will solve each part of the inequality separately.\n\n1. Solving \\(n - 1 < \\frac{23}{7} - n\\):\n\n\\[\nn - 1 < \\frac{23}{7} - n\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2n < \\frac{23}{7} + 1\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2n < \\frac{23}{7} + \\frac{7}{7}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2n < \\frac{30}{7}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn < \\frac{15}{7}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(n\\) is an integer, \\(n \\leq 2\\).\n\n2. Solving \\(\\frac{23}{7} - n \\leq n\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{23}{7} - n \\leq n\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{23}{7} \\leq 2n\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{23}{14} \\leq n\n\\]\n\nSince \\(n\\) is an integer, \\(n \\geq 2\\).\n\nCombining both results, we find \\(n = 2\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(n = 2\\) back into the expression for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{23}{7} - 2 = \\frac{23}{7} - \\frac{14}{7} = \\frac{9}{7}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{9}{7}}\\).'
'February typically has 28 days, except in a leap year when it has 29 days. Since Suzanne walks every third day, we need to determine how many days she walks in February.\n\n1. **For a non-leap year (28 days):**\n   - The sequence of days Suzanne walks is: 3, 6, 9, 12, 15, 18, 21, 24, 27.\n   - This is a total of 9 days.\n\n2. **For a leap year (29 days):**\n   - The sequence of days Suzanne walks is: 3, 6, 9, 12, 15, 18, 21, 24, 27.\n   - This is still a total of 9 days, as the 30th day would be the next walking day.\n\nIn both cases, Suzanne walks 9 times in February. Since she walks 4 miles each time, the total number of miles she walks is:\n\n\\[ 9 \\times 4 = 36 \\text{ miles}. \\]\n\nTherefore, the fewest number of miles Suzanne can walk in February is \\(\\boxed{36}\\).'
'To simplify and rationalize the expression \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{160}}{\\sqrt{252}} \\times \\frac{\\sqrt{245}}{\\sqrt{108}}\\), we start by simplifying each square root individually.\n\n1. Simplify \\(\\sqrt{160}\\):\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{160} = \\sqrt{16 \\times 10} = \\sqrt{16} \\times \\sqrt{10} = 4\\sqrt{10}\n   \\]\n\n2. Simplify \\(\\sqrt{252}\\):\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{252} = \\sqrt{36 \\times 7} = \\sqrt{36} \\times \\sqrt{7} = 6\\sqrt{7}\n   \\]\n\n3. Simplify \\(\\sqrt{245}\\):\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{245} = \\sqrt{49 \\times 5} = \\sqrt{49} \\times \\sqrt{5} = 7\\sqrt{5}\n   \\]\n\n4. Simplify \\(\\sqrt{108}\\):\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{108} = \\sqrt{36 \\times 3} = \\sqrt{36} \\times \\sqrt{3} = 6\\sqrt{3}\n   \\]\n\nNow substitute these simplified forms back into the original expression:\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{160}}{\\sqrt{252}} \\times \\frac{\\sqrt{245}}{\\sqrt{108}} = \\frac{4\\sqrt{10}}{6\\sqrt{7}} \\times \\frac{7\\sqrt{5}}{6\\sqrt{3}}\n\\]\n\nCombine the fractions:\n\\[\n= \\frac{4\\sqrt{10} \\times 7\\sqrt{5}}{6\\sqrt{7} \\times 6\\sqrt{3}}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the numerator and the denominator:\n- Numerator: \\(4 \\times 7 \\times \\sqrt{10} \\times \\sqrt{5} = 28 \\times \\sqrt{50} = 28 \\times \\sqrt{25 \\times 2} = 28 \\times 5\\sqrt{2} = 140\\sqrt{2}\\)\n- Denominator: \\(6 \\times 6 \\times \\sqrt{7} \\times \\sqrt{3} = 36 \\times \\sqrt{21}\\)\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\\[\n= \\frac{140\\sqrt{2}}{36\\sqrt{21}}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction:\n\\[\n= \\frac{140}{36} \\times \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{\\sqrt{21}}\n\\]\n\nSimplify \\(\\frac{140}{36}\\):\n\\[\n= \\frac{35}{9}\n\\]\n\nNow, rationalize the denominator \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{\\sqrt{21}}\\):\n\\[\n= \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{\\sqrt{21}} \\times \\frac{\\sqrt{21}}{\\sqrt{21}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{42}}{21}\n\\]\n\nCombine the simplified fraction:\n\\[\n= \\frac{35}{9} \\times \\frac{\\sqrt{42}}{21} = \\frac{35\\sqrt{42}}{189}\n\\]\n\nSimplify \\(\\frac{35}{189}\\):\n- The greatest common divisor of 35 and 189 is 7.\n- \\(\\frac{35}{189} = \\frac{5}{27}\\)\n\nThus, the completely simplified and rationalized expression is:\n\\[\n\\boxed{\\frac{5\\sqrt{42}}{27}}\n\\]'
'To find the value of \\( b \\) in the quadratic equation \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\), given that the vertex is \\( (p, p) \\) and the \\( y \\)-intercept is \\( (0, -p) \\), we can use the properties of the vertex and the \\( y \\)-intercept.\n\n1. **Vertex Form**: The vertex form of a parabola is given by \\( y = a(x-h)^2 + k \\), where \\( (h, k) \\) is the vertex. Since the vertex is \\( (p, p) \\), we can write:\n   \\[\n   y = a(x-p)^2 + p\n   \\]\n\n2. **Convert to Standard Form**: Expanding the vertex form:\n   \\[\n   y = a(x^2 - 2px + p^2) + p = ax^2 - 2apx + ap^2 + p\n   \\]\n   Comparing this with the standard form \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\), we have:\n   \\[\n   b = -2ap\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   c = ap^2 + p\n   \\]\n\n3. **\\( y \\)-Intercept**: The \\( y \\)-intercept is given as \\( (0, -p) \\), which means when \\( x = 0 \\), \\( y = -p \\). Substituting \\( x = 0 \\) in the standard form:\n   \\[\n   y = a(0)^2 + b(0) + c = c = -p\n   \\]\n   From the expression for \\( c \\) obtained earlier:\n   \\[\n   ap^2 + p = -p\n   \\]\n   Solving for \\( a \\):\n   \\[\n   ap^2 = -2p\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   a = -\\frac{2}{p}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Substitute \\( a \\) into \\( b \\)**: Now substitute \\( a = -\\frac{2}{p} \\) into the expression for \\( b \\):\n   \\[\n   b = -2ap = -2\\left(-\\frac{2}{p}\\right)p = 4\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( b \\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To find the coefficient of \\(x^3\\) in the product of the polynomials \\(7x^4 - 3x^3 - 3x^2 - 8x + 1\\) and \\(8x^4 + 2x^3 - 7x^2 + 3x + 4\\), we need to consider the terms from each polynomial that can multiply together to produce a term with \\(x^3\\).\n\nThe possible combinations of terms from each polynomial that result in an \\(x^3\\) term are:\n\n1. The constant term from the first polynomial and the \\(x^3\\) term from the second polynomial:\n   \\[\n   1 \\cdot 2x^3 = 2x^3\n   \\]\n\n2. The \\(x\\) term from the first polynomial and the \\(x^2\\) term from the second polynomial:\n   \\[\n   -8x \\cdot (-7x^2) = 56x^3\n   \\]\n\n3. The \\(x^2\\) term from the first polynomial and the \\(x\\) term from the second polynomial:\n   \\[\n   -3x^2 \\cdot 3x = -9x^3\n   \\]\n\n4. The \\(x^3\\) term from the first polynomial and the constant term from the second polynomial:\n   \\[\n   -3x^3 \\cdot 4 = -12x^3\n   \\]\n\nNow, we add these contributions together to find the total coefficient of \\(x^3\\):\n\\[\n2 + 56 - 9 - 12 = 37\n\\]\n\nThus, the coefficient of \\(x^3\\) in the product of the two polynomials is \\(\\boxed{37}\\).'
'To find the sum of all values of \\( x \\) such that \\( f(x) = 0 \\), we need to consider both cases of the piecewise function.\n\n**Case 1:** \\( x \\leq 3 \\)\n\nFor this case, the function is given by:\n\\[\nf(x) = 2x + 1\n\\]\nSetting \\( f(x) = 0 \\), we have:\n\\[\n2x + 1 = 0\n\\]\nSolving for \\( x \\), we subtract 1 from both sides:\n\\[\n2x = -1\n\\]\nThen divide by 2:\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\nSince \\(-\\frac{1}{2} \\leq 3\\), this solution is valid for this case.\n\n**Case 2:** \\( x > 3 \\)\n\nFor this case, the function is given by:\n\\[\nf(x) = 8 - 4x\n\\]\nSetting \\( f(x) = 0 \\), we have:\n\\[\n8 - 4x = 0\n\\]\nSolving for \\( x \\), we subtract 8 from both sides:\n\\[\n-4x = -8\n\\]\nThen divide by -4:\n\\[\nx = 2\n\\]\nHowever, \\( x = 2 \\) does not satisfy the condition \\( x > 3 \\), so this solution is not valid for this case.\n\nThus, the only valid solution is \\( x = -\\frac{1}{2} \\).\n\nThe sum of all values of \\( x \\) such that \\( f(x) = 0 \\) is:\n\\[\n\\boxed{-\\frac{1}{2}}\n\\]'
'To determine the domain of the function \\( f(x) = \\frac{2x-7}{\\sqrt{x^2-5x+6}} \\), we need to ensure that the expression under the square root is positive, as the square root of a negative number is not defined in the real numbers, and the denominator cannot be zero.\n\nThe expression under the square root is \\( x^2 - 5x + 6 \\). We first find the values of \\( x \\) for which this expression is zero by solving the equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 - 5x + 6 = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation that can be factored as:\n\n\\[\n(x-2)(x-3) = 0\n\\]\n\nThe solutions to this equation are \\( x = 2 \\) and \\( x = 3 \\). These are the points where the expression under the square root is zero, which would make the denominator zero, and thus the function undefined.\n\nNext, we determine the intervals where \\( x^2 - 5x + 6 > 0 \\). We test intervals around the roots \\( x = 2 \\) and \\( x = 3 \\):\n\n1. For \\( x < 2 \\), choose \\( x = 1 \\):\n   \\[\n   1^2 - 5 \\cdot 1 + 6 = 1 - 5 + 6 = 2 > 0\n   \\]\n   So, \\( x^2 - 5x + 6 > 0 \\) for \\( x < 2 \\).\n\n2. For \\( 2 < x < 3 \\), choose \\( x = 2.5 \\):\n   \\[\n   (2.5)^2 - 5 \\cdot 2.5 + 6 = 6.25 - 12.5 + 6 = -0.25 < 0\n   \\]\n   So, \\( x^2 - 5x + 6 < 0 \\) for \\( 2 < x < 3 \\).\n\n3. For \\( x > 3 \\), choose \\( x = 4 \\):\n   \\[\n   4^2 - 5 \\cdot 4 + 6 = 16 - 20 + 6 = 2 > 0\n   \\]\n   So, \\( x^2 - 5x + 6 > 0 \\) for \\( x > 3 \\).\n\nCombining these results, the expression \\( x^2 - 5x + 6 \\) is positive for \\( x < 2 \\) and \\( x > 3 \\).\n\nTherefore, the domain of the function \\( f(x) \\) is:\n\n\\[\n(-\\infty, 2) \\cup (3, \\infty)\n\\]\n\nThus, the domain of the function is \\(\\boxed{(-\\infty, 2) \\cup (3, \\infty)}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\sqrt{x + \\sqrt{x + \\sqrt{x + \\ldots}}} = 5\\), we first recognize that the expression inside the square root is self-similar. This means we can set:\n\n\\[\ny = \\sqrt{x + y}\n\\]\n\nGiven that \\(y = 5\\), we substitute into the equation:\n\n\\[\n5 = \\sqrt{x + 5}\n\\]\n\nNext, we square both sides to eliminate the square root:\n\n\\[\n25 = x + 5\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(x\\), we subtract 5 from both sides:\n\n\\[\nx = 25 - 5 = 20\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{20}\\).'
'To find the price that results in maximum revenue, we first need to express the revenue as a function of the price. Let \\( x \\) be the number of $5 decreases in price. Then the new price of the smartphone is \\( 450 - 5x \\) dollars, and the number of smartphones sold is \\( 500 + 10x \\).\n\nThe revenue \\( R \\) as a function of \\( x \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nR(x) = (450 - 5x)(500 + 10x)\n\\]\n\nExpanding this expression, we have:\n\n\\[\nR(x) = 450 \\times 500 + 450 \\times 10x - 5x \\times 500 - 5x \\times 10x\n\\]\n\n\\[\nR(x) = 225000 + 4500x - 2500x - 50x^2\n\\]\n\n\\[\nR(x) = 225000 + 2000x - 50x^2\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic function in the form \\( R(x) = -50x^2 + 2000x + 225000 \\). The maximum revenue occurs at the vertex of this parabola. The \\( x \\)-coordinate of the vertex of a parabola \\( ax^2 + bx + c \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{b}{2a}\n\\]\n\nHere, \\( a = -50 \\) and \\( b = 2000 \\), so:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{2000}{2 \\times -50} = \\frac{2000}{100} = 20\n\\]\n\nThus, the maximum revenue occurs when \\( x = 20 \\). The corresponding price is:\n\n\\[\n450 - 5 \\times 20 = 450 - 100 = 350\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the price that results in maximum revenue is \\(\\boxed{350}\\) dollars.'
'To find the sum of all possible values of \\( s \\) such that the roots of the quadratic expression \\(\\frac{1}{2}x^2 + sx - \\frac{1}{2}\\) are integers, we start by considering the quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2}x^2 + sx - \\frac{1}{2} = 0\n\\]\n\nMultiplying the entire equation by 2 to eliminate the fractions, we get:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 2sx - 1 = 0\n\\]\n\nFor the roots to be integers, the discriminant of this quadratic equation must be a perfect square. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = (2s)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-1) = 4s^2 + 4\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = 4(s^2 + 1)\n\\]\n\nFor \\(\\Delta\\) to be a perfect square, \\(s^2 + 1\\) must be a perfect square. Let \\(s^2 + 1 = k^2\\) for some integer \\(k\\). Then:\n\n\\[\nk^2 - s^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nThis is a difference of squares, which can be factored as:\n\n\\[\n(k-s)(k+s) = 1\n\\]\n\nThe integer solutions to this equation are \\((k-s, k+s) = (1, 1)\\) and \\((-1, -1)\\).\n\n1. For \\((k-s, k+s) = (1, 1)\\):\n   - Solving \\(k-s = 1\\) and \\(k+s = 1\\), we add the equations to get \\(2k = 2\\), so \\(k = 1\\).\n   - Substituting \\(k = 1\\) into \\(k-s = 1\\), we find \\(s = 0\\).\n\n2. For \\((k-s, k+s) = (-1, -1)\\):\n   - Solving \\(k-s = -1\\) and \\(k+s = -1\\), we add the equations to get \\(2k = -2\\), so \\(k = -1\\).\n   - Substituting \\(k = -1\\) into \\(k-s = -1\\), we find \\(s = 0\\).\n\nThus, the only possible value for \\(s\\) is \\(s = 0\\).\n\nTherefore, the sum of all possible values of \\(s\\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
'To find the value of \\(-a-b^2+3ab\\) given \\(a=-1\\) and \\(b=5\\), we substitute these values into the expression:\n\n\\[\n-a-b^2+3ab = -(-1) - (5)^2 + 3(-1)(5)\n\\]\n\nFirst, calculate each term separately:\n\n1. \\(-(-1) = 1\\)\n2. \\((5)^2 = 25\\)\n3. \\(3(-1)(5) = -15\\)\n\nNow substitute these values back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n1 - 25 - 15\n\\]\n\nCombine the terms:\n\n\\[\n1 - 25 = -24\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-24 - 15 = -39\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{-39}\\).'
'To find the slope of the line containing the midpoints of the given segments, we first need to determine the coordinates of these midpoints.\n\n1. **Midpoint of the segment with endpoints \\((2, 4)\\) and \\((0, -2)\\):**\n\n   The formula for the midpoint \\((x_m, y_m)\\) of a segment with endpoints \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is:\n   \\[\n   (x_m, y_m) = \\left( \\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2} \\right)\n   \\]\n\n   Applying this formula:\n   \\[\n   \\left( \\frac{2 + 0}{2}, \\frac{4 + (-2)}{2} \\right) = \\left( \\frac{2}{2}, \\frac{2}{2} \\right) = (1, 1)\n   \\]\n\n2. **Midpoint of the segment with endpoints \\((5, 1)\\) and \\((1, 5)\\):**\n\n   Again, using the midpoint formula:\n   \\[\n   \\left( \\frac{5 + 1}{2}, \\frac{1 + 5}{2} \\right) = \\left( \\frac{6}{2}, \\frac{6}{2} \\right) = (3, 3)\n   \\]\n\nNow, we have the midpoints \\((1, 1)\\) and \\((3, 3)\\).\n\n3. **Calculate the slope of the line through these midpoints:**\n\n   The formula for the slope \\(m\\) of a line through two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is:\n   \\[\n   m = \\frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}\n   \\]\n\n   Applying this formula to the points \\((1, 1)\\) and \\((3, 3)\\):\n   \\[\n   m = \\frac{3 - 1}{3 - 1} = \\frac{2}{2} = 1\n   \\]\n\nThus, the slope of the line containing the midpoints of the given segments is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To calculate the future value of Paula's investment with quarterly compounding interest, we use the formula for compound interest:\n\n\\[\nA = P \\left(1 + \\frac{r}{n}\\right)^{nt}\n\\]\n\nwhere:\n- \\( A \\) is the amount of money accumulated after \\( n \\) years, including interest.\n- \\( P \\) is the principal amount (initial investment), which is \\$10,000.\n- \\( r \\) is the annual interest rate (decimal), which is 0.10 for 10%.\n- \\( n \\) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year, which is 4 for quarterly compounding.\n- \\( t \\) is the time the money is invested for in years, which is 5 years.\n\nSubstituting the given values into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nA = 10000 \\left(1 + \\frac{0.10}{4}\\right)^{4 \\times 5}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\nA = 10000 \\left(1 + 0.025\\right)^{20}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nA = 10000 \\left(1.025\\right)^{20}\n\\]\n\nNow, we calculate \\( (1.025)^{20} \\):\n\n\\[\n(1.025)^{20} \\approx 1.638616\n\\]\n\nThus, the future value \\( A \\) is:\n\n\\[\nA = 10000 \\times 1.638616 \\approx 16386.16\n\\]\n\nTherefore, Paula's investment is worth approximately \\(\\$16,386.16\\) at the end of 5 years. The answer, rounded to the nearest cent, is \\(\\boxed{16,386.16}\\)."
"To find the value of \\( x \\) that satisfies both equations \\( 18x^2 + 25x - 3 = 0 \\) and \\( 4x^2 + 8x + 3 = 0 \\), we need to find a common solution to both quadratic equations.\n\nFirst, let's solve the first equation:\n\n\\[ 18x^2 + 25x - 3 = 0. \\]\n\nUsing the quadratic formula \\( x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 18 \\), \\( b = 25 \\), and \\( c = -3 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-25 \\pm \\sqrt{25^2 - 4 \\cdot 18 \\cdot (-3)}}{2 \\cdot 18}.\n\\]\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = 25^2 - 4 \\cdot 18 \\cdot (-3) = 625 + 216 = 841.\n\\]\n\nSince \\( \\sqrt{841} = 29 \\), the solutions are:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-25 \\pm 29}{36}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-25 + 29}{36} = \\frac{4}{36} = \\frac{1}{9},\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-25 - 29}{36} = \\frac{-54}{36} = -\\frac{3}{2}.\n\\]\n\nNext, solve the second equation:\n\n\\[ 4x^2 + 8x + 3 = 0. \\]\n\nUsing the quadratic formula with \\( a = 4 \\), \\( b = 8 \\), and \\( c = 3 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-8 \\pm \\sqrt{8^2 - 4 \\cdot 4 \\cdot 3}}{2 \\cdot 4}.\n\\]\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = 8^2 - 4 \\cdot 4 \\cdot 3 = 64 - 48 = 16.\n\\]\n\nSince \\( \\sqrt{16} = 4 \\), the solutions are:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-8 \\pm 4}{8}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-8 + 4}{8} = \\frac{-4}{8} = -\\frac{1}{2},\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-8 - 4}{8} = \\frac{-12}{8} = -\\frac{3}{2}.\n\\]\n\nThe common solution to both equations is \\( x = -\\frac{3}{2} \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( x \\) that satisfies both equations is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{3}{2}}\\)."
'To solve for the value of \\((p-1)(q-1)\\) given that \\(\\frac{1}{p} + \\frac{1}{q} = 1\\), we start by manipulating the given equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{p} + \\frac{1}{q} = 1\n\\]\n\nCombine the fractions on the left-hand side:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{q + p}{pq} = 1\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nq + p = pq\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation:\n\n\\[\npq - p - q = 0\n\\]\n\nAdd 1 to both sides:\n\n\\[\npq - p - q + 1 = 1\n\\]\n\nNotice that the left-hand side can be factored:\n\n\\[\n(p-1)(q-1) = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\((p-1)(q-1)\\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'To find \\(24x - 14y\\), we start by solving the system of equations:\n\n\\[\n5x - 2y = 7\n\\]\n\\[\n3x + y = 2\n\\]\n\nFirst, solve the second equation for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\ny = 2 - 3x\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\(y = 2 - 3x\\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n5x - 2(2 - 3x) = 7\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n5x - 4 + 6x = 7\n\\]\n\\[\n11x - 4 = 7\n\\]\n\\[\n11x = 11\n\\]\n\\[\nx = 1\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\(x = 1\\) back into the expression for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\ny = 2 - 3(1) = 2 - 3 = -1\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\(x = 1\\) and \\(y = -1\\), compute \\(24x - 14y\\):\n\n\\[\n24x - 14y = 24(1) - 14(-1)\n\\]\n\\[\n= 24 + 14\n\\]\n\\[\n= 38\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(24x - 14y\\) is \\(\\boxed{38}\\).'
'To simplify \\(\\frac{3}{\\sqrt[5]{16}} + \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\) and express it in the form \\(\\frac{a^2\\sqrt[5]{b} + b\\sqrt{a}}{ab}\\), we need to rationalize the denominators of each term separately.\n\nFirst, consider \\(\\frac{3}{\\sqrt[5]{16}}\\). We can rationalize the denominator by multiplying the numerator and the denominator by \\(\\sqrt[5]{16^4}\\), which is \\(\\sqrt[5]{65536}\\), to make the denominator a perfect fifth power:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{\\sqrt[5]{16}} \\cdot \\frac{\\sqrt[5]{65536}}{\\sqrt[5]{65536}} = \\frac{3\\sqrt[5]{65536}}{16}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(16 = 2^4\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[5]{65536} = \\sqrt[5]{(2^4)^4} = \\sqrt[5]{2^{16}} = 2^{16/5}\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{16/5}}{16}\n\\]\n\nNext, consider \\(\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\). We rationalize the denominator by multiplying the numerator and the denominator by \\(\\sqrt{3}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{\\sqrt{3}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{3}\n\\]\n\nNow, we combine the two rationalized terms:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{16/5}}{16} + \\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{3}\n\\]\n\nTo express this in the form \\(\\frac{a^2\\sqrt[5]{b} + b\\sqrt{a}}{ab}\\), we need to find a common denominator, which is \\(48\\) (the least common multiple of \\(16\\) and \\(3\\)):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{16/5}}{16} = \\frac{9 \\cdot 2^{16/5}}{48}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{3} = \\frac{16\\sqrt{3}}{48}\n\\]\n\nCombining these, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{9 \\cdot 2^{16/5} + 16\\sqrt{3}}{48}\n\\]\n\nMatching this with the form \\(\\frac{a^2\\sqrt[5]{b} + b\\sqrt{a}}{ab}\\), we identify:\n\n- \\(a^2 = 9\\), so \\(a = 3\\)\n- \\(b = 2\\), since \\(2^{16/5}\\) corresponds to \\(\\sqrt[5]{b}\\)\n- The term \\(16\\sqrt{3}\\) corresponds to \\(b\\sqrt{a}\\), confirming \\(b = 2\\) and \\(a = 3\\)\n\nThus, \\(a = 3\\) and \\(b = 2\\), and the sum \\(a + b = 3 + 2 = \\boxed{5}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( y \\) when \\( x = 6 \\) for the parabola \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\) with vertex \\((2, 3)\\) and passing through the point \\((4, 4)\\), we start by using the vertex form of a parabola:\n\n\\[\ny = a(x - h)^2 + k\n\\]\n\nwhere \\((h, k)\\) is the vertex. Here, \\((h, k) = (2, 3)\\), so the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\ny = a(x - 2)^2 + 3\n\\]\n\nWe know the parabola passes through the point \\((4, 4)\\). Substituting \\(x = 4\\) and \\(y = 4\\) into the equation, we can solve for \\(a\\):\n\n\\[\n4 = a(4 - 2)^2 + 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\n4 = a(2)^2 + 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\n4 = 4a + 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1 = 4a\n\\]\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{1}{4}\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\(a = \\frac{1}{4}\\), the equation of the parabola is:\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{1}{4}(x - 2)^2 + 3\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the value of \\(y\\) when \\(x = 6\\):\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{1}{4}(6 - 2)^2 + 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{1}{4}(4)^2 + 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{1}{4} \\times 16 + 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 4 + 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 7\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(y\\) when \\(x = 6\\) is \\(\\boxed{7}\\).'
'To find point \\( T \\) such that \\( Q \\) is the midpoint of segment \\(\\overline{PT}\\), we use the midpoint formula. The midpoint \\( M \\) of a segment with endpoints \\( (x_1, y_1) \\) and \\( (x_2, y_2) \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nM = \\left( \\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2} \\right)\n\\]\n\nGiven that \\( P = (5, 3) \\) and \\( Q = (-3, 6) \\) is the midpoint, we set:\n\n\\[\nQ = \\left( \\frac{5 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{3 + y_2}{2} \\right) = (-3, 6)\n\\]\n\nWe equate the coordinates:\n\n1. 'To find the equation of the circle, we need to determine its center and radius. The circle is centered at \\((-1, 1)\\) and passes through the point \\((1, 2)\\).\n\nFirst, calculate the radius of the circle. The radius \\(r\\) is the distance between the center \\((-1, 1)\\) and the point \\((1, 2)\\):\n\n\\[\nr = \\sqrt{(1 - (-1))^2 + (2 - 1)^2} = \\sqrt{(1 + 1)^2 + (2 - 1)^2} = \\sqrt{2^2 + 1^2} = \\sqrt{4 + 1} = \\sqrt{5}\n\\]\n\nThe standard form of the equation of a circle with center \\((h, k)\\) and radius \\(r\\) is:\n\n\\[\n(x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the center \\((-1, 1)\\) and radius \\(\\sqrt{5}\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n(x + 1)^2 + (y - 1)^2 = 5\n\\]\n\nExpanding this equation:\n\n\\[\n(x + 1)^2 = x^2 + 2x + 1\n\\]\n\\[\n(y - 1)^2 = y^2 - 2y + 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 2x + 1 + y^2 - 2y + 1 = 5\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + 2x - 2y + 2 = 5\n\\]\n\nSubtract 5 from both sides to set the equation to zero:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + 2x - 2y + 2 - 5 = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + 2x - 2y - 3 = 0\n\\]\n\nNow, we identify the coefficients \\(A\\), \\(B\\), \\(C\\), and \\(D\\) from the equation \\(x^2 + Ay^2 + Bx + Cy + D = 0\\):\n\n- \\(A = 1\\)\n- \\(B = 2\\)\n- \\(C = -2\\)\n- \\(D = -3\\)\n\nFinally, calculate \\(A + B + C + D\\):\n\n\\[\nA + B + C + D = 1 + 2 - 2 - 3 = -2\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(A + B + C + D\\) is \\(\\boxed{-2}\\).'
'To find the maximum value of \\( f^{-1}(x) \\), we need to understand the relationship between the function \\( f(x) \\) and its inverse \\( f^{-1}(x) \\). "To find Ben's minimum height, we need to determine the minimum value of the quadratic function \\( h(t) = 2t^2 - 5t + 29 \\).\n\nThe function \\( h(t) = 2t^2 - 5t + 29 \\) is a quadratic function in the standard form \\( at^2 + bt + c \\), where \\( a = 2 \\), \\( b = -5 \\), and \\( c = 29 \\). 'To determine the largest value of \\( a \\) such that the graph of \\( y = f(x) \\) intersects every horizontal line at least once, we need to ensure that for every \\( y \\in \\mathbb{R} \\), there exists an \\( x \\) such that \\( f(x) = y \\).\n\nThe function \\( f(x) \\) is defined piecewise as follows:\n\\[\nf(x) =\n\\begin{cases}\nax^2 & \\text{if } x \\geq a,\\\\\nax + 2a & \\text{if } x < a.\n\\end{cases}\n\\]\n\n**Step 1: Analyze the quadratic part \\( ax^2 \\) for \\( x \\geq a \\).**\n\nThe quadratic function \\( ax^2 \\) is a parabola opening upwards (since \\( a > 0 \\) for the parabola to open upwards). The minimum value of \\( ax^2 \\) occurs at \\( x = a \\), which is \\( f(a) = aa^2 = a^3 \\).\n\n**Step 2: Analyze the linear part \\( ax + 2a \\) for \\( x < a \\).**\n\nThe linear function \\( ax + 2a \\) is a line with slope \\( a \\). As \\( x \\to -\\infty \\), \\( ax + 2a \\to -\\infty \\). Therefore, the range of the linear part is \\((-\\infty, 3a)\\), where \\( 3a \\) is the value of the linear function at \\( x = a \\).\n\n**Step 3: Ensure the entire function covers all real numbers.**\n\nFor the graph of \\( y = f(x) \\) to intersect every horizontal line at least once, the ranges of the two parts must cover all real numbers. Specifically, the minimum value of the quadratic part \\( a^3 \\) must be less than or equal to the maximum value of the linear part \\( 3a \\).\n\nThus, we require:\n\\[\na^3 \\leq 3a.\n\\]\n\n**Step 4: Solve the inequality \\( a^3 \\leq 3a \\).**\n\nDivide both sides by \\( a \\) (assuming \\( a \\neq 0 \\)):\n\\[\na^2 \\leq 3.\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we get:\n\\[\na \\leq \\sqrt{3}.\n\\]\n\nSince \\( a \\) must be positive for the parabola to open upwards, the largest possible value of \\( a \\) is \\( \\sqrt{3} \\).\n\nTherefore, the largest value of \\( a \\) such that the graph of \\( y = f(x) \\) intersects every horizontal line at least once is \\(\\boxed{\\sqrt{3}}\\).'

"To solve this problem, we need to use the properties of quadratic equations and the given conditions. The equation is \\(x^2 - mx + n = 0\\) with roots \\(k\\) and \\(t\\). By Vieta's formulas, we know:\n\n1. \\(k + t = m\\)\n2. \\(kt = n\\)\n\nSince \\(m\\) and \\(n\\) are both prime numbers, and \\(k\\) and \\(t\\) are positive integers, we need to find values for \\(k\\), \\(t\\), \\(m\\), and \\(n\\) that satisfy these conditions.\n\nLet's consider the possible values for \\(n\\), which is the product of \\(k\\) and \\(t\\). Since \\(n\\) is a prime number, one of the roots must be 1 (because the only way to express a prime number as a product of two positive integers is \\(1 \\times n\\)). Therefore, we can assume without loss of generality that \\(t = 1\\) and \\(k = n\\).\n\nNow, substituting \\(t = 1\\) and \\(k = n\\) into the equations from Vieta's formulas:\n\n- \\(k + t = m\\) becomes \\(n + 1 = m\\)\n- \\(kt = n\\) becomes \\(n \\times 1 = n\\)\n\nSince \\(m\\) is also a prime number, and \\(m = n + 1\\), we need to find two consecutive numbers where one is prime and the other is also prime. The only such pair is \\(n = 2\\) and \\(m = 3\\).\n\nThus, we have:\n- \\(n = 2\\)\n- \\(m = 3\\)\n- \\(k = 2\\)\n- \\(t = 1\\)\n\nNow, we need to calculate \\(m^n + n^m + k^t + t^k\\):\n\n\\[\nm^n = 3^2 = 9\n\\]\n\\[\nn^m = 2^3 = 8\n\\]\n\\[\nk^t = 2^1 = 2\n\\]\n\\[\nt^k = 1^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nAdding these together:\n\n\\[\nm^n + n^m + k^t + t^k = 9 + 8 + 2 + 1 = 20\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(m^n + n^m + k^t + t^k\\) is \\(\\boxed{20}\\)."

'To solve the equation \\( x = 1 + \\frac{x}{1 + \\frac{x}{1 + \\frac{x}{1 + \\cdots}}} \\), we first recognize that the expression is self-referential. 'To find the distance between the points \\((-5, 5)\\) and \\((5, -5)\\), we use the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given coordinates \\((-5, 5)\\) and \\((5, -5)\\) into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nx_1 = -5, \\quad y_1 = 5, \\quad x_2 = 5, \\quad y_2 = -5\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(5 - (-5))^2 + (-5 - 5)^2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(5 + 5)^2 + (-5 - 5)^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{10^2 + (-10)^2}\n\\]\n\nCalculating the squares:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{100 + 100}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{200}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying \\(\\sqrt{200}\\):\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{100 \\times 2} = \\sqrt{100} \\times \\sqrt{2} = 10\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the distance between the points is \\(\\boxed{10\\sqrt{2}}\\).'
'The expression \\(36 - 4x^2\\) is a difference of squares. We can factor it using the difference of squares formula, which states that \\(a^2 - b^2 = (a - b)(a + b)\\).\n\nFirst, we identify \\(a^2\\) and \\(b^2\\) in the expression:\n\n\\[\n36 = (6)^2 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad 4x^2 = (2x)^2\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n36 - 4x^2 = (6)^2 - (2x)^2\n\\]\n\nApplying the difference of squares formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n(6)^2 - (2x)^2 = (6 - 2x)(6 + 2x)\n\\]\n\nWe can further factor each term if possible. Notice that both terms have a common factor of 2:\n\n\\[\n6 - 2x = 2(3 - x) \\quad \\text{and} \\quad 6 + 2x = 2(3 + x)\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n(6 - 2x)(6 + 2x) = 2(3 - x) \\cdot 2(3 + x) = 4(3 - x)(3 + x)\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the completely factored form of \\(36 - 4x^2\\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{4(3 - x)(3 + x)}\n\\]'
'To find the value of \\( g(g(-1)) \\), we first need to determine \\( g(-1) \\) from the graph of the function \\( y = g(x) \\).\n\nFrom the graph, we observe that the function is a sinusoidal wave, specifically \\( y = -6 \\sin\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{6} x\\right) \\).\n\n1. **Find \\( g(-1) \\):**\n\n   Substitute \\( x = -1 \\) into the function:\n   \\[\n   g(-1) = -6 \\sin\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{6} \\times (-1)\\right) = -6 \\sin\\left(-\\frac{\\pi}{6}\\right)\n   \\]\n\n   Using the property of sine, \\( \\sin(-\\theta) = -\\sin(\\theta) \\), we have:\n   \\[\n   \\sin\\left(-\\frac{\\pi}{6}\\right) = -\\sin\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{6}\\right) = -\\frac{1}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   Therefore:\n   \\[\n   g(-1) = -6 \\times \\left(-\\frac{1}{2}\\right) = 3\n   \\]\n\n2. **Find \\( g(g(-1)) = g(3) \\):**\n\n   Now, substitute \\( x = 3 \\) into the function:\n   \\[\n   g(3) = -6 \\sin\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{6} \\times 3\\right) = -6 \\sin\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{2}\\right)\n   \\]\n\n   We know that:\n   \\[\n   \\sin\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{2}\\right) = 1\n   \\]\n\n   Therefore:\n   \\[\n   g(3) = -6 \\times 1 = -6\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( g(g(-1)) \\) is \\(\\boxed{-6}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(c) \\) for the given function \\( f(c) = \\frac{3}{2c-3} \\), and then evaluate the expression \\( f^{-1}(c) \\times c \\times f(c) \\).\n\n### Step 1: Find the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(c) \\)\n\nStart by setting \\( y = f(c) = \\frac{3}{2c-3} \\). To find the inverse, solve for \\( c \\) in terms of \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{3}{2c-3}\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by \\( 2c - 3 \\):\n\n\\[\ny(2c - 3) = 3\n\\]\n\nDistribute \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\n2yc - 3y = 3\n\\]\n\nAdd \\( 3y \\) to both sides:\n\n\\[\n2yc = 3 + 3y\n\\]\n\nDivide by \\( 2y \\):\n\n\\[\nc = \\frac{3 + 3y}{2y}\n\\]\n\nThus, the inverse function is:\n\n\\[\nf^{-1}(c) = \\frac{3 + 3c}{2c}\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Evaluate \\( f^{-1}(c) \\times c \\times f(c) \\)\n\nSubstitute \\( f^{-1}(c) \\) and \\( f(c) \\) into the expression:\n\n\\[\nf^{-1}(c) = \\frac{3 + 3c}{2c}, \\quad f(c) = \\frac{3}{2c-3}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the product:\n\n\\[\nf^{-1}(c) \\times c \\times f(c) = \\left(\\frac{3 + 3c}{2c}\\right) \\times c \\times \\left(\\frac{3}{2c-3}\\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{3 + 3c}{2c} \\times \\frac{3c}{2c-3}\n\\]\n\nCancel \\( c \\) in the numerator and denominator:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{(3 + 3c) \\times 3}{2(2c-3)}\n\\]\n\nDistribute the 3 in the numerator:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{9 + 9c}{4c - 6}\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Express in the form \\(\\frac{kc+l}{mc+n}\\)\n\nThe expression \\(\\frac{9 + 9c}{4c - 6}\\) is already in the form \\(\\frac{kc+l}{mc+n}\\) with:\n\n- \\( k = 9 \\)\n- \\( l = 9 \\)\n- \\( m = 4 \\)\n- \\( n = -6 \\)\n\n### Step 4: Calculate \\(\\frac{kn^2}{lm}\\)\n\nSubstitute the values:\n\n\\[\nk = 9, \\quad l = 9, \\quad m = 4, \\quad n = -6\n\\]\n\nCalculate:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{kn^2}{lm} = \\frac{9 \\times (-6)^2}{9 \\times 4}\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{9 \\times 36}{36}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 9\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{kn^2}{lm}\\) is \\(\\boxed{9}\\).'

'To find the value of \\(2x - xy\\), we first need to solve for \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) using the given equations:\n\n1. \\(x + y = 12\\)\n2. \\(x - y = 8\\)\n\nWe can solve these equations simultaneously. By adding the two equations, we eliminate \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 12 + 8\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2x = 20\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 10\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\(x = 10\\) back into one of the original equations to find \\(y\\). 'Let \\( r \\) be the number of rows and \\( s \\) be the number of seats per row in the original seating arrangement. We know that the total number of seats is given by:\n\n\\[\nr \\times s = 450\n\\]\n\nIn the new arrangement, there are three fewer seats per row and five extra rows, so the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n(r + 5)(s - 3) = 450\n\\]\n\nWe now have two equations:\n\n1. \\( rs = 450 \\)\n2. \\( (r + 5)(s - 3) = 450 \\)\n\nExpanding the second equation, we have:\n\n\\[\n(r + 5)(s - 3) = rs - 3r + 5s - 15 = 450\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( rs = 450 \\) from the first equation into the expanded form:\n\n\\[\n450 - 3r + 5s - 15 = 450\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n-3r + 5s - 15 = 0\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\n5s = 3r + 15\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( s \\), we have:\n\n\\[\ns = \\frac{3r + 15}{5}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( s \\) back into the first equation \\( rs = 450 \\):\n\n\\[\nr \\left(\\frac{3r + 15}{5}\\right) = 450\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by 5 to clear the fraction:\n\n\\[\nr(3r + 15) = 2250\n\\]\n\nExpanding gives:\n\n\\[\n3r^2 + 15r = 2250\n\\]\n\nDivide the entire equation by 3:\n\n\\[\nr^2 + 5r = 750\n\\]\n\nRearrange to form a quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\nr^2 + 5r - 750 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula \\( r = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 5 \\), and \\( c = -750 \\):\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{5^2 - 4 \\times 1 \\times (-750)}}{2 \\times 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{25 + 3000}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{3025}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{-5 \\pm 55}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives two possible solutions for \\( r \\):\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{50}{2} = 25 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad r = \\frac{-60}{2} = -30\n\\]\n\nSince the number of rows cannot be negative, we have \\( r = 25 \\).\n\nThus, the auditorium originally has \\(\\boxed{25}\\) rows.'

'To find the \\( y \\)-intercepts of the parabola given by the equation \\( x = -y^2 + 4y - 4 \\), we need to determine the values of \\( y \\) for which \\( x = 0 \\).\n\nSet \\( x = 0 \\) in the equation:\n\n\\[\n0 = -y^2 + 4y - 4\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\ny^2 - 4y + 4 = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in \\( y \\). We can solve it using the quadratic formula, \\( y = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -4 \\), and \\( c = 4 \\).\n\nFirst, calculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = (-4)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 4 = 16 - 16 = 0\n\\]\n\nSince the discriminant is zero, there is exactly one solution for \\( y \\). 'To solve the equation \\(\\sqrt{5x} \\cdot \\sqrt{10x} \\cdot \\sqrt{18x} = 30\\), we start by simplifying the left-hand side. 'To solve the problem, we need to simplify each fraction separately and then combine them.\n\nFirst, consider the fraction \\(\\frac{2}{1 + 2\\sqrt{3}}\\). We rationalize the denominator by multiplying the numerator and the denominator by the conjugate of the denominator, \\(1 - 2\\sqrt{3}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2}{1 + 2\\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{1 - 2\\sqrt{3}}{1 - 2\\sqrt{3}} = \\frac{2(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}{(1 + 2\\sqrt{3})(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}\n\\]\n\nThe denominator simplifies as follows:\n\n\\[\n(1 + 2\\sqrt{3})(1 - 2\\sqrt{3}) = 1^2 - (2\\sqrt{3})^2 = 1 - 4 \\cdot 3 = 1 - 12 = -11\n\\]\n\nThus, the fraction becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}{-11} = \\frac{2 - 4\\sqrt{3}}{-11} = \\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\nNext, consider the fraction \\(\\frac{3}{2 - \\sqrt{3}}\\). We rationalize the denominator by multiplying the numerator and the denominator by the conjugate of the denominator, \\(2 + \\sqrt{3}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2 - \\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{2 + \\sqrt{3}}{2 + \\sqrt{3}} = \\frac{3(2 + \\sqrt{3})}{(2 - \\sqrt{3})(2 + \\sqrt{3})}\n\\]\n\nThe denominator simplifies as follows:\n\n\\[\n(2 - \\sqrt{3})(2 + \\sqrt{3}) = 2^2 - (\\sqrt{3})^2 = 4 - 3 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the fraction becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3(2 + \\sqrt{3})}{1} = 6 + 3\\sqrt{3}\n\\]\n\nNow, we add the two simplified fractions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11} + (6 + 3\\sqrt{3})\n\\]\n\nTo combine these, we express \\(6 + 3\\sqrt{3}\\) with a common denominator of 11:\n\n\\[\n6 + 3\\sqrt{3} = \\frac{66 + 33\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\nAdding the two fractions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11} + \\frac{66 + 33\\sqrt{3}}{11} = \\frac{-2 + 66 + (4\\sqrt{3} + 33\\sqrt{3})}{11}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the numerator:\n\n\\[\n-2 + 66 = 64 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad 4\\sqrt{3} + 33\\sqrt{3} = 37\\sqrt{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the combined fraction is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{64 + 37\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\nIn the form \\(\\frac{A + B\\sqrt{3}}{C}\\), we have \\(A = 64\\), \\(B = 37\\), and \\(C = 11\\). Therefore, \\(A + B + C = 64 + 37 + 11 = 112\\).\n\nThe answer is \\(\\boxed{112}\\).'

Then the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n(a-b)^2 = (531 - 530)^2 = 1^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"Given the conditions \\( p + q = pq \\) and \\( p - q = 7 \\), we need to find the value of \\(\\frac{1}{\\frac{1}{p^2} + \\frac{1}{q^2}}\\).\n\nFirst, let's solve for \\( p \\) and \\( q \\). From the equation \\( p + q = pq \\), we can express \\( q \\) in terms of \\( p \\):\n\n\\[\nq = \\frac{p}{p-1}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting this into the second equation \\( p - q = 7 \\):\n\n\\[\np - \\frac{p}{p-1} = 7\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by \\( p-1 \\) to clear the fraction:\n\n\\[\np(p-1) - p = 7(p-1)\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\np^2 - p - p = 7p - 7\n\\]\n\n\\[\np^2 - 8p + 7 = 0\n\\]\n\nSolve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\np = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -8 \\), and \\( c = 7 \\):\n\n\\[\np = \\frac{8 \\pm \\sqrt{64 - 28}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\np = \\frac{8 \\pm \\sqrt{36}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\np = \\frac{8 \\pm 6}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[\np = \\frac{14}{2} = 7 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad p = \\frac{2}{2} = 1\n\\]\n\nSince \\( p - q = 7 \\), \\( p = 7 \\) and \\( q = 0 \\) is not possible because \\( q \\) must be positive. Thus, \\( p = 8 \\) and \\( q = 1 \\).\n\nNow, calculate \\(\\frac{1}{\\frac{1}{p^2} + \\frac{1}{q^2}}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{\\frac{1}{8^2} + \\frac{1}{1^2}} = \\frac{1}{\\frac{1}{64} + 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{1}{\\frac{1}{64} + \\frac{64}{64}} = \\frac{1}{\\frac{65}{64}}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{64}{65}\n\\]\n\nThe expression is \\(\\frac{64}{65}\\), which is already in the form \\(\\frac{a+b\\sqrt{c}}{d}\\) with \\( a = 64 \\), \\( b = 0 \\), \\( c = 1 \\), and \\( d = 65 \\).\n\nThus, \\( a + b + c + d = 64 + 0 + 1 + 65 = \\boxed{130} \\)."
'The car travels 45 feet in the first second, and each subsequent second it travels 5 feet less than the previous second. This forms an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\( a = 45 \\) and the common difference \\( d = -5 \\).\n\nThe sequence of distances traveled each second is: 45, 40, 35, 30, ..., until the car stops. We need to find the total distance traveled, which is the sum of this arithmetic sequence.\n\nFirst, we determine the number of terms in the sequence. The car stops when the distance traveled in a second is 0 feet. We set the \\( n \\)-th term of the sequence to 0:\n\n\\[\na_n = a + (n-1)d = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n45 + (n-1)(-5) = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n45 - 5(n-1) = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n45 - 5n + 5 = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n50 = 5n\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = 10\n\\]\n\nThere are 10 terms in the sequence. The sum \\( S_n \\) of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\n\\[\nS_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (a + l)\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( l \\) is the last term. Here, \\( l = 0 \\), so:\n\n\\[\nS_{10} = \\frac{10}{2} \\times (45 + 0) = 5 \\times 45 = 225\n\\]\n\nThus, the car travels a total of \\(\\boxed{225}\\) feet from the time the brakes are applied to the time the car stops.'
"To solve this problem, we need to calculate the distance traveled by each horse and then determine how many revolutions the second horse must make to travel the same distance as the first horse.\n\nFirst, let's calculate the distance traveled by the horse 64 feet from the center. The circumference of the circle that this horse travels is given by the formula \\( C = 2\\pi r \\), where \\( r \\) is the radius of the circle. For the first horse, \\( r = 64 \\) feet, so the circumference is:\n\n\\[\nC_1 = 2\\pi \\times 64 = 128\\pi \\text{ feet}\n\\]\n\nThe horse makes 27 revolutions, so the total distance traveled by the first horse is:\n\n\\[\nD_1 = 27 \\times 128\\pi = 3456\\pi \\text{ feet}\n\\]\n\nNext, we need to find out how many revolutions the second horse, which is 16 feet from the center, must make to travel the same distance. The circumference of the circle for the second horse is:\n\n\\[\nC_2 = 2\\pi \\times 16 = 32\\pi \\text{ feet}\n\\]\n\nLet \\( n \\) be the number of revolutions the second horse needs to make. The total distance traveled by the second horse is:\n\n\\[\nD_2 = n \\times 32\\pi\n\\]\n\nWe want this distance to be equal to the distance traveled by the first horse:\n\n\\[\nn \\times 32\\pi = 3456\\pi\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by \\( 32\\pi \\), we get:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{3456\\pi}{32\\pi} = \\frac{3456}{32} = 108\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the horse 16 feet from the center would need to make \\(\\boxed{108}\\) revolutions to travel the same distance as the horse 64 feet from the center."
'To determine the value of \\( K \\) such that no pair of real numbers \\((x, y)\\) satisfies the system of equations:\n\n\\[\n6x + 4y = 7\n\\]\n\\[\nKx + 8y = 7\n\\]\n\nwe need the system to be inconsistent. This occurs when the two lines represented by the equations are parallel, which means they have the same slope but different intercepts.\n\nFirst, we find the slope of the line given by the first equation. Rewriting the equation in slope-intercept form \\( y = mx + c \\):\n\n\\[\n4y = -6x + 7 \\implies y = -\\frac{3}{2}x + \\frac{7}{4}\n\\]\n\nThe slope of this line is \\(-\\frac{3}{2}\\).\n\nNext, we find the slope of the line given by the second equation. Rewriting it in slope-intercept form:\n\n\\[\nKx + 8y = 7 \\implies 8y = -Kx + 7 \\implies y = -\\frac{K}{8}x + \\frac{7}{8}\n\\]\n\nThe slope of this line is \\(-\\frac{K}{8}\\).\n\nFor the lines to be parallel, their slopes must be equal:\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{3}{2} = -\\frac{K}{8}\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( K \\), we multiply both sides by \\(-1\\) and then by 8:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2} = \\frac{K}{8}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nK = 8 \\times \\frac{3}{2} = 12\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( K \\) that makes the system of equations inconsistent is \\(\\boxed{12}\\).'

We want to find the number of calories, \\( x \\), in 12 fluid ounces.\n\nThe proportion is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{125 \\text{ calories}}{8 \\text{ fluid ounces}} = \\frac{x \\text{ calories}}{12 \\text{ fluid ounces}}\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( x \\), we cross-multiply:\n\n\\[\n125 \\times 12 = 8 \\times x\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1500 = 8x\n\\]\n\nNow, divide both sides by 8 to solve for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{1500}{8} = 187.5\n\\]\n\nTherefore, a 12 fluid ounce bottle of Vitamin Water contains \\( \\boxed{187.5} \\) calories.'

Start with the innermost expression: \\(\\sqrt{x}\\).\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{x} = x^{1/2}\n   \\]\n\n2. Next, consider the expression \\(\\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}\\).\n   \\[\n   x \\sqrt{x} = x \\cdot x^{1/2} = x^{1 + 1/2} = x^{3/2}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\root 3 \\of {x^{3/2}} = (x^{3/2})^{1/3} = x^{(3/2) \\cdot (1/3)} = x^{1/2}\n   \\]\n\n3.
