"Let's denote the number of free hours each person gets as \\( f \\) and the cost per extra hour as \\( c \\) cents. We need to find the value of \\( c \\).\n\nFirst, let's consider Wells and Ted together. They used a total of 105 hours and paid $10, which is 1000 cents. Since they both used all their free hours, the total number of extra hours they used is \\( 105 - 2f \\). Therefore, the equation for Wells and Ted is:\n\n\\[\nc(105 - 2f) = 1000\n\\]\n\nNext, consider Vino, who used 105 hours and paid $26, which is 2600 cents. The number of extra hours Vino used is \\( 105 - f \\). Therefore, the equation for Vino is:\n\n\\[\nc(105 - f) = 2600\n\\]\n\nNow we have two equations:\n\n1. \\( c(105 - 2f) = 1000 \\)\n2. \\( c(105 - f) = 2600 \\)\n\nWe can solve these equations simultaneously. First, solve the second equation for \\( c \\):\n\n\\[\nc = \\frac{2600}{105 - f}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( c \\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2600}{105 - f}(105 - 2f) = 1000\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( f \\):\n\n\\[\n2600(105 - 2f) = 1000(105 - f)\n\\]\n\nExpanding both sides:\n\n\\[\n273000 - 5200f = 105000 - 1000f\n\\]\n\nRearrange to solve for \\( f \\):\n\n\\[\n273000 - 105000 = 5200f - 1000f\n\\]\n\n\\[\n168000 = 4200f\n\\]\n\n\\[\nf = \\frac{168000}{4200} = 40\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\( f = 40 \\), substitute back to find \\( c \\) using the second equation:\n\n\\[\nc = \\frac{2600}{105 - 40} = \\frac{2600}{65} = 40\n\\]\n\nThus, the number of cents charged for each extra hour is \\(\\boxed{40}\\)."
'To find the value of \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\), we need to combine the given ratios:\n\n1. \\(\\frac{a}{b} = \\frac{3}{5}\\)\n2. \\(\\frac{b}{c} = \\frac{15}{6}\\)\n3. \\(\\frac{c}{d} = 6\\)\n\nFirst, simplify \\(\\frac{b}{c} = \\frac{15}{6}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{b}{c} = \\frac{15}{6} = \\frac{5}{2}\n\\]\n\nNow, we want to find \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\). We can do this by multiplying the ratios:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{d} = \\frac{a}{b} \\times \\frac{b}{c} \\times \\frac{c}{d}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the values:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{d} = \\frac{3}{5} \\times \\frac{5}{2} \\times 6\n\\]\n\nSimplify step by step:\n\nFirst, multiply \\(\\frac{3}{5}\\) and \\(\\frac{5}{2}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{5} \\times \\frac{5}{2} = \\frac{3 \\times 5}{5 \\times 2} = \\frac{15}{10} = \\frac{3}{2}\n\\]\n\nNext, multiply \\(\\frac{3}{2}\\) by 6:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2} \\times 6 = \\frac{3 \\times 6}{2} = \\frac{18}{2} = 9\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\) is \\(\\boxed{9}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( c \\) such that \\( x^2 + 25x + c \\) is the square of a binomial, we need to express it in the form \\( (x + a)^2 \\).\n\nThe expansion of \\( (x + a)^2 \\) is:\n\n\\[\n(x + a)^2 = x^2 + 2ax + a^2\n\\]\n\nBy comparing this with \\( x^2 + 25x + c \\), we can see that:\n\n1. The coefficient of \\( x \\) gives us \\( 2a = 25 \\).\n2. 'To find the shortest distance between the two circles, we first need to determine the distance between their centers and then subtract the sum of their radii.\n\nThe first circle is given by the equation \\((x-9)^2 + (y-5)^2 = 6.25\\). The center of this circle is \\((9, 5)\\) and its radius is \\(\\sqrt{6.25} = 2.5\\).\n\nThe second circle is given by the equation \\((x+6)^2 + (y+3)^2 = 49\\). The center of this circle is \\((-6, -3)\\) and its radius is \\(\\sqrt{49} = 7\\).\n\nNext, we calculate the distance between the centers of the two circles. The distance \\(d\\) between the points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is given by the formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the coordinates of the centers, we have:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{((-6) - 9)^2 + ((-3) - 5)^2} = \\sqrt{(-15)^2 + (-8)^2} = \\sqrt{225 + 64} = \\sqrt{289} = 17\n\\]\n\nThe shortest distance between the two circles is the distance between their centers minus the sum of their radii. The sum of the radii is:\n\n\\[\n2.5 + 7 = 9.5\n\\]\n\nThus, the shortest distance between the circles is:\n\n\\[\n17 - 9.5 = 7.5\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the shortest distance between the two circles is \\(\\boxed{7.5}\\) units.'
'To find the value of \\((4^3 + 2^3) - (3^3 + 1^3)\\), we first calculate each of the individual powers:\n\n1. Calculate \\(4^3\\):\n   \\[\n   4^3 = 4 \\times 4 \\times 4 = 16 \\times 4 = 64\n   \\]\n\n2. Calculate \\(2^3\\):\n   \\[\n   2^3 = 2 \\times 2 \\times 2 = 4 \\times 2 = 8\n   \\]\n\n3. Calculate \\(3^3\\):\n   \\[\n   3^3 = 3 \\times 3 \\times 3 = 9 \\times 3 = 27\n   \\]\n\n4. Calculate \\(1^3\\):\n   \\[\n   1^3 = 1 \\times 1 \\times 1 = 1\n   \\]\n\nNow, substitute these values back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n(4^3 + 2^3) - (3^3 + 1^3) = (64 + 8) - (27 + 1)\n\\]\n\nCalculate the sums inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\n64 + 8 = 72\n\\]\n\\[\n27 + 1 = 28\n\\]\n\nSubtract the second sum from the first:\n\n\\[\n72 - 28 = 44\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\((4^3 + 2^3) - (3^3 + 1^3)\\) is \\(\\boxed{44}\\).'
'To find \\( x^3 - y^3 \\), we can use the identity for the difference of cubes:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = (x-y)(x^2 + xy + y^2)\n\\]\n\nWe are given that \\( x-y = 1 \\). Therefore, we need to find \\( x^2 + xy + y^2 \\).\n\nWe are also given that \\( x^2 + y^2 = 7 \\).\n\nTo find \\( xy \\), we can use the identity:\n\n\\[\n(x-y)^2 = x^2 - 2xy + y^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values:\n\n\\[\n1^2 = x^2 - 2xy + y^2\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1 = 7 - 2xy\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( xy \\):\n\n\\[\n2xy = 7 - 1 = 6\n\\]\n\n\\[\nxy = 3\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x^2 + y^2 = 7 \\) and \\( xy = 3 \\) into the expression for \\( x^2 + xy + y^2 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 + xy + y^2 = x^2 + y^2 + xy = 7 + 3 = 10\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute back into the expression for \\( x^3 - y^3 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = (x-y)(x^2 + xy + y^2) = 1 \\cdot 10 = 10\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^3 - y^3 \\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
"To solve the equation \\( x \\cdot \\lfloor x \\rfloor = 27 \\) where \\( x \\) is positive, we need to find a positive \\( x \\) such that the product of \\( x \\) and the greatest integer less than or equal to \\( x \\) equals 27.\n\nLet's denote \\( \\lfloor x \\rfloor = n \\), where \\( n \\) is an integer. Then, we have:\n\n\\[\nx \\cdot n = 27\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{27}{n}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( \\lfloor x \\rfloor = n \\), it follows that:\n\n\\[\nn \\leq x < n+1\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( x = \\frac{27}{n} \\) into the inequality, we get:\n\n\\[\nn \\leq \\frac{27}{n} < n+1\n\\]\n\nWe will solve these inequalities separately.\n\n1. **First inequality:**\n\n   \\[\n   n \\leq \\frac{27}{n}\n   \\]\n\n   Multiplying both sides by \\( n \\) (assuming \\( n > 0 \\)) gives:\n\n   \\[\n   n^2 \\leq 27\n   \\]\n\n   Solving for \\( n \\), we find:\n\n   \\[\n   n \\leq \\sqrt{27} \\approx 5.196\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\( n \\) is an integer, \\( n \\leq 5 \\).\n\n2. **Second inequality:**\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{27}{n} < n+1\n   \\]\n\n   Multiplying both sides by \\( n \\) gives:\n\n   \\[\n   27 < n^2 + n\n   \\]\n\n   Rearranging terms, we have:\n\n   \\[\n   n^2 + n - 27 > 0\n   \\]\n\n   Solving the quadratic equation \\( n^2 + n - 27 = 0 \\) using the quadratic formula:\n\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{1 + 4 \\times 27}}{2} = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{109}}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   Approximating the roots:\n\n   \\[\n   n \\approx \\frac{-1 \\pm 10.44}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   This gives approximate solutions \\( n \\approx 4.72 \\) and \\( n \\approx -5.72 \\). Since \\( n \\) must be a positive integer, we consider \\( n \\geq 5 \\).\n\nCombining both inequalities, \\( n \\leq 5 \\) and \\( n \\geq 5 \\), we find \\( n = 5 \\).\n\nSubstituting \\( n = 5 \\) back into the expression for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{27}{5} = 5.4\n\\]\n\nThus, the positive value of \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{5.4}\\)."
"To find the least possible value of the sum \\( |x - 1| + |x - 1.5| + |x - 2| \\), we need to consider the behavior of the expression as \\( x \\) varies. The expression consists of three absolute value terms, each of which changes its behavior at the points 1, 1.5, and 2. These points are the critical points where the expression can change its form.\n\nLet's evaluate the expression in the intervals determined by these critical points:\n\n1. **Interval \\( x < 1 \\):**\n\n   In this interval, all terms are negative inside the absolute values:\n   \\[\n   |x - 1| = 1 - x, \\quad |x - 1.5| = 1.5 - x, \\quad |x - 2| = 2 - x\n   \\]\n   The sum is:\n   \\[\n   (1 - x) + (1.5 - x) + (2 - x) = 4.5 - 3x\n   \\]\n\n2. **Interval \\( 1 \\leq x < 1.5 \\):**\n\n   Here, the first term is non-negative, while the other two are negative:\n   \\[\n   |x - 1| = x - 1, \\quad |x - 1.5| = 1.5 - x, \\quad |x - 2| = 2 - x\n   \\]\n   The sum is:\n   \\[\n   (x - 1) + (1.5 - x) + (2 - x) = 2.5 - x\n   \\]\n\n3. **Interval \\( 1.5 \\leq x < 2 \\):**\n\n   In this interval, the first two terms are non-negative, and the last term is negative:\n   \\[\n   |x - 1| = x - 1, \\quad |x - 1.5| = x - 1.5, \\quad |x - 2| = 2 - x\n   \\]\n   The sum is:\n   \\[\n   (x - 1) + (x - 1.5) + (2 - x) = x - 1 + x - 1.5 + 2 - x = x - 0.5\n   \\]\n\n4. **Interval \\( x \\geq 2 \\):**\n\n   In this interval, all terms are non-negative:\n   \\[\n   |x - 1| = x - 1, \\quad |x - 1.5| = x - 1.5, \\quad |x - 2| = x - 2\n   \\]\n   The sum is:\n   \\[\n   (x - 1) + (x - 1.5) + (x - 2) = 3x - 4.5\n   \\]\n\nNow, we find the minimum value of the expression in each interval:\n\n- For \\( x < 1 \\), the expression is \\( 4.5 - 3x \\), which decreases as \\( x \\) increases.\n- For \\( 1 \\leq x < 1.5 \\), the expression is \\( 2.5 - x \\), which decreases as \\( x \\) increases.\n- For \\( 1.5 \\leq x < 2 \\), the expression is \\( x - 0.5 \\), which increases as \\( x \\) increases.\n- For \\( x \\geq 2 \\), the expression is \\( 3x - 4.5 \\), which increases as \\( x \\) increases.\n\nThe minimum value occurs at the transition point between decreasing and increasing behavior, which is at \\( x = 1.5 \\). Substituting \\( x = 1.5 \\) into the expression for the interval \\( 1.5 \\leq x < 2 \\), we get:\n\\[\n1.5 - 0.5 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the least possible value of the sum is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."

Then, Josh rode for \\( 2t \\) hours at a speed of \\( \\frac{4}{5}r \\) miles per hour.\n\nThe distance Josh rode is given by:\n\\[\n\\text{Distance Josh rode} = \\left(\\frac{4}{5}r\\right)(2t) = \\frac{8}{5}rt\n\\]\n\nThe distance Mike rode is:\n\\[\n\\text{Distance Mike rode} = rt\n\\]\n\nSince they meet after covering a total distance of 13 miles, we have:\n\\[\n\\frac{8}{5}rt + rt = 13\n\\]\n\nCombining the terms, we get:\n\\[\n\\frac{8}{5}rt + \\frac{5}{5}rt = \\frac{13}{5}rt = 13\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( rt \\), we multiply both sides by 5:\n\\[\n13rt = 65\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by 13 gives:\n\\[\nrt = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, Mike rode 5 miles when they met. 'To solve for \\( f(f(9)) \\), we need to understand the relationship between \\( f \\) and its inverse \\( g \\). Given that \\( g(x) = f^{-1}(x) \\), it follows that:\n\n\\[ f(g(x)) = x \\]\nand\n\\[ g(f(x)) = x. \\]\n\nWe are given several values for \\( g \\):\n\n- \\( g(-15) = 0 \\)\n- \\( g(0) = 3 \\)\n- \\( g(3) = 9 \\)\n- \\( g(9) = 20 \\)\n\nFrom these, we can deduce the corresponding values for \\( f \\):\n\n- Since \\( g(-15) = 0 \\), it follows that \\( f(0) = -15 \\).\n- Since \\( g(0) = 3 \\), it follows that \\( f(3) = 0 \\).\n- Since \\( g(3) = 9 \\), it follows that \\( f(9) = 3 \\).\n- Since \\( g(9) = 20 \\), it follows that \\( f(20) = 9 \\).\n\nWe need to find \\( f(f(9)) \\). From the values above, we know:\n\n\\[ f(9) = 3. \\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\( f(3) \\):\n\n\\[ f(3) = 0. \\]\n\nThus, \\( f(f(9)) = f(3) = 0 \\).\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( f(f(9)) \\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
'To expand the product \\((x-2)^2(x+2)^2\\), we start by expanding each binomial squared:\n\n\\[\n(x-2)^2 = (x-2)(x-2) = x^2 - 4x + 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\n(x+2)^2 = (x+2)(x+2) = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to multiply these two results together:\n\n\\[\n(x^2 - 4x + 4)(x^2 + 4x + 4)\n\\]\n\nWe will use the distributive property (also known as the FOIL method for binomials) to expand this product:\n\n1. Multiply \\(x^2\\) by each term in the second polynomial:\n   \\[\n   x^2 \\cdot (x^2 + 4x + 4) = x^4 + 4x^3 + 4x^2\n   \\]\n\n2. Multiply \\(-4x\\) by each term in the second polynomial:\n   \\[\n   -4x \\cdot (x^2 + 4x + 4) = -4x^3 - 16x^2 - 16x\n   \\]\n\n3. Multiply \\(4\\) by each term in the second polynomial:\n   \\[\n   4 \\cdot (x^2 + 4x + 4) = 4x^2 + 16x + 16\n   \\]\n\nNow, add all these results together:\n\n\\[\nx^4 + 4x^3 + 4x^2 - 4x^3 - 16x^2 - 16x + 4x^2 + 16x + 16\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n- \\(x^4\\) term: \\(x^4\\)\n- \\(x^3\\) terms: \\(4x^3 - 4x^3 = 0\\)\n- \\(x^2\\) terms: \\(4x^2 - 16x^2 + 4x^2 = -8x^2\\)\n- \\(x\\) terms: \\(-16x + 16x = 0\\)\n- Constant term: \\(16\\)\n\nThus, the expanded expression is:\n\n\\[\nx^4 - 8x^2 + 16\n\\]\n\nThe nonzero coefficients in this expression are \\(1\\) (for \\(x^4\\)), \\(-8\\) (for \\(x^2\\)), and \\(16\\) (the constant term). The product of these coefficients is:\n\n\\[\n1 \\times (-8) \\times 16 = -128\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the product of the nonzero coefficients is \\(\\boxed{-128}\\).'
'Let the three consecutive positive even numbers be \\( x-2 \\), \\( x \\), and \\( x+2 \\). The sum of their squares is given by:\n\n\\[\n(x-2)^2 + x^2 + (x+2)^2 = 12296\n\\]\n\nExpanding each square, we have:\n\n\\[\n(x-2)^2 = x^2 - 4x + 4\n\\]\n\\[\nx^2 = x^2\n\\]\n\\[\n(x+2)^2 = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nAdding these expressions together:\n\n\\[\n(x^2 - 4x + 4) + x^2 + (x^2 + 4x + 4) = 12296\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the left side:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 + 8 = 12296\n\\]\n\nSubtract 8 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 = 12288\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 3:\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 4096\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides:\n\n\\[\nx = 64\n\\]\n\nThus, the three consecutive even numbers are \\( 62 \\), \\( 64 \\), and \\( 66 \\).\n\nNext, we find the product of these numbers:\n\n\\[\n62 \\times 64 \\times 66\n\\]\n\nTo simplify the calculation, note that:\n\n\\[\n62 \\times 66 = (64-2)(64+2) = 64^2 - 2^2 = 4096 - 4 = 4092\n\\]\n\nNow, multiply by 64:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 64\n\\]\n\nBreaking it down:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 64 = (4092 \\times 60) + (4092 \\times 4)\n\\]\n\nCalculate each part:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 60 = 245520\n\\]\n\\[\n4092 \\times 4 = 16368\n\\]\n\nAdding these results:\n\n\\[\n245520 + 16368 = 261888\n\\]\n\nFinally, divide the product by 8:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{261888}{8} = 32736\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the three numbers divided by 8 is \\(\\boxed{32736}\\).'
'To find the number of positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which the sum \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 \\) is less than 20, we start by setting up the inequality:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 < 20\n\\]\n\nSubtract 20 from both sides to simplify:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 - 20 < 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x - 16 < 0\n\\]\n\nNext, we solve the quadratic equation \\( x^2 + 4x - 16 = 0 \\) to find the critical points. We use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 4 \\), and \\( c = -16 \\). Plugging in these values, we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{4^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-16)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 + 64}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{80}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 \\cdot 5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm 4\\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = -2 \\pm 2\\sqrt{5}\n\\]\n\nThe roots are \\( x = -2 + 2\\sqrt{5} \\) and \\( x = -2 - 2\\sqrt{5} \\). Since we are interested in positive integer values of \\( x \\), we consider the interval between these roots where the quadratic is negative. The approximate value of \\( \\sqrt{5} \\) is about 2.236, so:\n\n\\[\nx = -2 + 2 \\times 2.236 \\approx -2 + 4.472 \\approx 2.472\n\\]\n\nThus, the inequality \\( x^2 + 4x - 16 < 0 \\) holds for \\( x \\) in the interval \\( (-2 - 2\\sqrt{5}, -2 + 2\\sqrt{5}) \\), which approximately translates to \\( (-6.472, 2.472) \\).\n\nThe positive integer values of \\( x \\) within this interval are \\( x = 1 \\) and \\( x = 2 \\).\n\nTherefore, there are \\(\\boxed{2}\\) positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 < 20 \\).'
'To find the value of \\(255^2 - 245^2\\), we can use the difference of squares formula, which states:\n\n\\[\na^2 - b^2 = (a-b)(a+b)\n\\]\n\nIn this case, \\(a = 255\\) and \\(b = 245\\). Applying the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n255^2 - 245^2 = (255 - 245)(255 + 245)\n\\]\n\nCalculating each part:\n\n\\[\n255 - 245 = 10\n\\]\n\n\\[\n255 + 245 = 500\n\\]\n\nSubstituting these values back into the expression, we get:\n\n\\[\n255^2 - 245^2 = 10 \\times 500 = 5000\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(255^2 - 245^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{5000}\\).'
'To find the minimum possible slope of the line, we need to consider the line passing through the point \\((4, 365)\\) and having a \\(y\\)-intercept between 1 and 9. The equation of a line in slope-intercept form is given by:\n\n\\[ y = mx + c \\]\n\nwhere \\(m\\) is the slope and \\(c\\) is the \\(y\\)-intercept. Since the line passes through the point \\((4, 365)\\), we can substitute these values into the equation:\n\n\\[ 365 = m \\cdot 4 + c \\]\n\nRearranging this equation gives:\n\n\\[ m = \\frac{365 - c}{4} \\]\n\nTo find the minimum possible slope, we need to maximize the value of \\(c\\) within the given range. Since \\(c\\) is between 1 and 9, the maximum value of \\(c\\) is 9. Substituting \\(c = 9\\) into the equation for \\(m\\), we get:\n\n\\[ m = \\frac{365 - 9}{4} = \\frac{356}{4} = 89 \\]\n\nTherefore, the minimum possible slope of the line is \\(\\boxed{89}\\).'
'To solve for \\( x - y \\), we have the system of equations:\n\n\\[\n725x + 727y = 1500\n\\]\n\n\\[\n729x + 731y = 1508\n\\]\n\nWe can use the method of elimination to find \\( x - y \\). First, subtract the first equation from the second:\n\n\\[\n(729x + 731y) - (725x + 727y) = 1508 - 1500\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n4x + 4y = 8\n\\]\n\nDividing the entire equation by 4:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 2\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\( x - y \\). We can express \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y \\) using the equation \\( x + y = 2 \\):\n\n\\[\nx = 2 - y\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( x = 2 - y \\) into one of the original equations, say \\( 725x + 727y = 1500 \\):\n\n\\[\n725(2 - y) + 727y = 1500\n\\]\n\nExpanding and simplifying:\n\n\\[\n1450 - 725y + 727y = 1500\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1450 + 2y = 1500\n\\]\n\nSubtract 1450 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2y = 50\n\\]\n\nDivide by 2:\n\n\\[\ny = 25\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( y = 25 \\) back into \\( x = 2 - y \\):\n\n\\[\nx = 2 - 25 = -23\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\( x - y \\):\n\n\\[\nx - y = -23 - 25 = -48\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x - y \\) is \\(\\boxed{-48}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\log_2 8\\sqrt{2}\\), we start by expressing \\(8\\sqrt{2}\\) in terms of powers of 2.\n\nFirst, note that:\n\\[ 8 = 2^3 \\]\nand\n\\[ \\sqrt{2} = 2^{1/2}. \\]\n\nThus, we can write:\n\\[ 8\\sqrt{2} = 2^3 \\cdot 2^{1/2} = 2^{3 + 1/2} = 2^{3.5} = 2^{7/2}. \\]\n\nNow, we need to evaluate:\n\\[ \\log_2 (2^{7/2}). \\]\n\nUsing the property of logarithms that \\(\\log_b (b^x) = x\\), we have:\n\\[ \\log_2 (2^{7/2}) = \\frac{7}{2}. \\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\log_2 8\\sqrt{2}\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{7}{2}}\\).'
'To find the positive difference between the sum and the product of \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\) and \\(\\frac{1}{3}\\), we first calculate each separately.\n\nFirst, calculate the sum:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2} + \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{3}{6} + \\frac{2}{6} = \\frac{5}{6}\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate the product:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2} \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{1 \\times 1}{2 \\times 3} = \\frac{1}{6}\n\\]\n\nNow, find the positive difference between the sum and the product:\n\\[\n\\frac{5}{6} - \\frac{1}{6} = \\frac{5 - 1}{6} = \\frac{4}{6} = \\frac{2}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the positive difference is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{2}{3}}\\).'
'To find the smallest positive four-digit integer that is the product of two consecutive integers, we need to find integers \\( n \\) and \\( n+1 \\) such that their product \\( n(n+1) \\) is a four-digit number, i.e., \\( 1000 \\leq n(n+1) < 10000 \\).\n\nFirst, we approximate \\( n \\) by solving the inequality:\n\n\\[\nn^2 \\leq n(n+1) < 10000\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of the upper bound:\n\n\\[\nn^2 < 10000 \\implies n < \\sqrt{10000} = 100\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of the lower bound:\n\n\\[\nn^2 \\geq 1000 \\implies n \\geq \\sqrt{1000} \\approx 31.62\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( n \\) must be an integer such that \\( 32 \\leq n < 100 \\).\n\nWe will test values of \\( n \\) starting from 32 to find the smallest product that is a four-digit number:\n\n- For \\( n = 32 \\):\n  \\[\n  n(n+1) = 32 \\times 33 = 1056\n  \\]\n\n- For \\( n = 31 \\):\n  \\[\n  n(n+1) = 31 \\times 32 = 992\n  \\]\n\nSince 992 is not a four-digit number, we confirm that the smallest four-digit product is obtained when \\( n = 32 \\).\n\nTherefore, the smallest positive four-digit integer that is the product of two consecutive integers is \\(\\boxed{1056}\\).'
"Given that \\( f \\) is an invertible function and \\( f(f(x)) = x \\), we need to find \\( f(x) - f^{-1}(x) \\).\n\nFirst, let's analyze the condition \\( f(f(x)) = x \\). This implies that applying the function \\( f \\) twice returns the original input \\( x \\). This is a characteristic of an involution, meaning \\( f \\) is its own inverse. Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\nf^{-1}(x) = f(x)\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\( f(x) - f^{-1}(x) \\). Since \\( f^{-1}(x) = f(x) \\), we have:\n\n\\[\nf(x) - f^{-1}(x) = f(x) - f(x) = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(x) - f^{-1}(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\)."
'To find the value of \\(\\frac{7}{30} @ \\frac{10}{21}\\), we use the operation defined as:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{m}{n} @ \\frac{p}{q} = (m)(p)\\left(\\frac{q}{n}\\right)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given fractions \\(\\frac{7}{30}\\) and \\(\\frac{10}{21}\\) into the operation, we have:\n\n- \\(m = 7\\), \\(n = 30\\)\n- \\(p = 10\\), \\(q = 21\\)\n\nNow, apply the operation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{7}{30} @ \\frac{10}{21} = (7)(10)\\left(\\frac{21}{30}\\right)\n\\]\n\nCalculate each part:\n\n1. Multiply \\(m\\) and \\(p\\):\n\n\\[\n7 \\times 10 = 70\n\\]\n\n2. Simplify \\(\\frac{21}{30}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{21}{30} = \\frac{7}{10} \\quad \\text{(dividing both numerator and denominator by 3)}\n\\]\n\n3. Multiply the results:\n\n\\[\n70 \\times \\frac{7}{10} = 70 \\times 0.7 = 49\n\\]\n\nThus, the simplified value of \\(\\frac{7}{30} @ \\frac{10}{21}\\) is \\(\\boxed{49}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 125\\sqrt{5}\\), we start by expressing everything in terms of powers of 5. \n\nFirst, note that:\n\\[\n\\sqrt{5} = 5^{1/2}\n\\]\nand\n\\[\n125 = 5^3.\n\\]\nThus, we can write:\n\\[\n125\\sqrt{5} = 5^3 \\cdot 5^{1/2} = 5^{3 + 1/2} = 5^{7/2}.\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to evaluate:\n\\[\n\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} (5^{7/2}).\n\\]\n\nUsing the change of base formula, we have:\n\\[\n\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} (5^{7/2}) = \\frac{\\log_{5^{1/2}} (5^{7/2})}{\\log_{5^{1/2}} 5}.\n\\]\n\nThe expression \\(\\log_{5^{1/2}} 5\\) can be simplified as follows:\n\\[\n\\log_{5^{1/2}} 5 = \\frac{\\log_5 5}{\\log_5 5^{1/2}} = \\frac{1}{1/2} = 2.\n\\]\n\nNow, consider \\(\\log_{5^{1/2}} (5^{7/2})\\):\n\\[\n\\log_{5^{1/2}} (5^{7/2}) = \\frac{\\log_5 (5^{7/2})}{\\log_5 5^{1/2}} = \\frac{7/2}{1/2} = 7.\n\\]\n\nThus, the original expression simplifies to:\n\\[\n\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} (5^{7/2}) = \\frac{7}{2} = 7.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 125\\sqrt{5}\\) is \\(\\boxed{7}\\).'
'To find the numerical value of the expression \\((b-c)^2 + a(b+c)\\) given \\(a = 2\\), \\(b = 3\\), and \\(c = 4\\), we can substitute these values into the expression and simplify:\n\n1. Substitute the values:\n   \\[\n   (b-c)^2 + a(b+c) = (3-4)^2 + 2(3+4)\n   \\]\n\n2. Simplify each part:\n   - Calculate \\(b-c\\):\n     \\[\n     3 - 4 = -1\n     \\]\n   - Calculate \\((b-c)^2\\):\n     \\[\n     (-1)^2 = 1\n     \\]\n   - Calculate \\(b+c\\):\n     \\[\n     3 + 4 = 7\n     \\]\n   - Calculate \\(a(b+c)\\):\n     \\[\n     2 \\times 7 = 14\n     \\]\n\n3. Add the results:\n   \\[\n   (b-c)^2 + a(b+c) = 1 + 14 = 15\n   \\]\n\nThus, the numerical value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{15}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to understand the properties of an arithmetic sequence. An arithmetic sequence is defined by a first term \\( a_1 \\) and a common difference \\( d \\). The general term of the sequence can be expressed as:\n\n\\[\na_n = a_1 + (n-1)d\n\\]\n\nGiven that \\(\\frac{a_4}{a_2} = 3\\), we can express \\(a_4\\) and \\(a_2\\) in terms of \\(a_1\\) and \\(d\\):\n\n\\[\na_4 = a_1 + 3d\n\\]\n\\[\na_2 = a_1 + d\n\\]\n\nSubstituting these into the given ratio:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a_4}{a_2} = \\frac{a_1 + 3d}{a_1 + d} = 3\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\n\\[\na_1 + 3d = 3(a_1 + d)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\n\\[\na_1 + 3d = 3a_1 + 3d\n\\]\n\nSubtracting \\(3d\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\na_1 = 3a_1\n\\]\n\nSubtracting \\(a_1\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\n0 = 2a_1\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(a_1 = 0\\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\(\\frac{a_5}{a_3}\\). Using the general term formula:\n\n\\[\na_5 = a_1 + 4d = 0 + 4d = 4d\n\\]\n\\[\na_3 = a_1 + 2d = 0 + 2d = 2d\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the ratio is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a_5}{a_3} = \\frac{4d}{2d} = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{a_5}{a_3}\\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
'The function \\( f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\) is an exponential function with base \\(\\frac{3}{7}\\), which is a positive number less than 1. The domain of \\( f(x) \\) is \\([0, \\infty)\\).\n\nTo determine the range of \\( f(x) \\), we analyze the behavior of the function as \\( x \\) varies over its domain:\n\n1. **As \\( x \\to 0 \\):** \n   \\[\n   f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\to \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^0 = 1.\n   \\]\n   So, \\( f(x) \\) approaches 1 from below as \\( x \\) approaches 0.\n\n2. **As \\( x \\to \\infty \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\to 0.\n   \\]\n   Since \\(\\frac{3}{7} < 1\\), raising it to a larger and larger power makes the value approach 0.\n\nSince \\( f(x) \\) is a continuous function that decreases from 1 to 0 as \\( x \\) increases from 0 to \\(\\infty\\), the range of \\( f(x) \\) is all positive real numbers less than or equal to 1. Therefore, the range of the function is:\n\n\\[\n(0, 1].\n\\]\n\nThus, the range of the function \\( f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\) is \\((0, 1]\\).'
'To find the sum of the areas of all the circles, we first need to determine the area of each circle. The diameter of the circles forms a geometric sequence: 16 inches, 8 inches, 4 inches, and so on. The radius of each circle is half of its diameter, so the radii are 8 inches, 4 inches, 2 inches, and so on.\n\nThe area \\( A \\) of a circle with radius \\( r \\) is given by the formula:\n\n\\[\nA = \\pi r^2\n\\]\n\nThus, the areas of the circles are:\n\n- First circle: \\( \\pi \\times 8^2 = 64\\pi \\)\n- Second circle: \\( \\pi \\times 4^2 = 16\\pi \\)\n- Third circle: \\( \\pi \\times 2^2 = 4\\pi \\)\n- Fourth circle: \\( \\pi \\times 1^2 = \\pi \\)\n\nThe areas form a geometric series with the first term \\( a = 64\\pi \\) and common ratio \\( r = \\frac{1}{4} \\).\n\nThe sum \\( S \\) of an infinite geometric series is given by:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{a}{1 - r}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values we have:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{64\\pi}{1 - \\frac{1}{4}} = \\frac{64\\pi}{\\frac{3}{4}} = \\frac{64\\pi \\times 4}{3} = \\frac{256\\pi}{3}\n\\]\n\nTo express this sum to the nearest whole number, we approximate \\(\\pi \\approx 3.14159\\):\n\n\\[\nS \\approx \\frac{256 \\times 3.14159}{3} \\approx \\frac{804.24704}{3} \\approx 268.08235\n\\]\n\nRounding to the nearest whole number, the sum of the areas of all the circles is approximately:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{268}\n\\]'
'To find the difference between the sum of the first 2003 even counting numbers and the sum of the first 2003 odd counting numbers, we start by calculating each sum separately.\n\nThe first 2003 even counting numbers are: \n\\[ 2, 4, 6, \\ldots, 2 \\times 2003. \\]\nThis sequence is an arithmetic series with the first term \\( a = 2 \\) and the last term \\( l = 2 \\times 2003 = 4006 \\). The number of terms \\( n \\) is 2003. The sum \\( S_{\\text{even}} \\) of an arithmetic series is given by:\n\\[\nS_{\\text{even}} = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (a + l) = \\frac{2003}{2} \\times (2 + 4006) = 2003 \\times 2004.\n\\]\n\nThe first 2003 odd counting numbers are:\n\\[ 1, 3, 5, \\ldots, 2 \\times 2003 - 1. \\]\nThis sequence is also an arithmetic series with the first term \\( a = 1 \\) and the last term \\( l = 2 \\times 2003 - 1 = 4005 \\). The number of terms \\( n \\) is 2003. The sum \\( S_{\\text{odd}} \\) of this arithmetic series is:\n\\[\nS_{\\text{odd}} = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (a + l) = \\frac{2003}{2} \\times (1 + 4005) = 2003 \\times 2003.\n\\]\n\nNow, we find the difference between these two sums:\n\\[\nS_{\\text{even}} - S_{\\text{odd}} = 2003 \\times 2004 - 2003 \\times 2003.\n\\]\nFactoring out the common term 2003, we have:\n\\[\nS_{\\text{even}} - S_{\\text{odd}} = 2003 \\times (2004 - 2003) = 2003 \\times 1 = 2003.\n\\]\n\nThus, the difference between the sum of the first 2003 even counting numbers and the sum of the first 2003 odd counting numbers is \\(\\boxed{2003}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8})\\), we start by expressing both the base and the argument in terms of powers of 2.\n\nFirst, note that:\n\\[\n\\sqrt{8} = 8^{1/2} = (2^3)^{1/2} = 2^{3/2}\n\\]\nThus, the base \\(\\sqrt{8}\\) can be rewritten as \\(2^{3/2}\\).\n\nNext, express \\(64\\sqrt{8}\\) in terms of powers of 2:\n\\[\n64 = 2^6\n\\]\n\\[\n64\\sqrt{8} = 2^6 \\cdot 2^{3/2} = 2^{6 + 3/2} = 2^{6 + 1.5} = 2^{7.5}\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to evaluate:\n\\[\n\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8}) = \\log_{2^{3/2}}(2^{7.5})\n\\]\n\nUsing the change of base formula for logarithms, we have:\n\\[\n\\log_{2^{3/2}}(2^{7.5}) = \\frac{\\log_2(2^{7.5})}{\\log_2(2^{3/2})}\n\\]\n\nCalculate each logarithm:\n\\[\n\\log_2(2^{7.5}) = 7.5\n\\]\n\\[\n\\log_2(2^{3/2}) = \\frac{3}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\\[\n\\frac{7.5}{3/2} = 7.5 \\times \\frac{2}{3} = \\frac{15}{2} \\times \\frac{2}{3} = 5\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8})\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\).'
'Since \\( c \\) and \\( d \\) are inversely proportional, we have the relationship \\( c \\cdot d = k \\) for some constant \\( k \\).\n\nGiven that \\( c = 9 \\) when \\( d = 8 \\), we can find \\( k \\) as follows:\n\n\\[\n9 \\cdot 8 = k \\implies k = 72\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find the value of \\( d \\) when \\( c = 6 \\). Using the relationship \\( c \\cdot d = k \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n6 \\cdot d = 72\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( d \\), we divide both sides by 6:\n\n\\[\nd = \\frac{72}{6} = 12\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( d \\) when \\( c = 6 \\) is \\(\\boxed{12}\\).'
"In an arithmetic sequence, the difference between consecutive terms is constant. Let's denote the first term as \\( a_1 = 3^2 = 9 \\), the second term as \\( a_2 = x \\), and the third term as \\( a_3 = 3^4 = 81 \\).\n\nThe common difference \\( d \\) can be expressed as:\n\\[\nd = a_2 - a_1 = x - 9\n\\]\n\\[\nd = a_3 - a_2 = 81 - x\n\\]\n\nSince the common difference is the same, we equate the two expressions for \\( d \\):\n\\[\nx - 9 = 81 - x\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( x \\), we add \\( x \\) to both sides:\n\\[\n2x - 9 = 81\n\\]\n\nNext, add 9 to both sides:\n\\[\n2x = 90\n\\]\n\nFinally, divide by 2:\n\\[\nx = 45\n\\]\n\nThus, the integer value of \\( x \\) in the arithmetic sequence is \\(\\boxed{45}\\)."
"Heisenberg's Uncertainty Principle can be expressed mathematically as:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta p \\cdot \\Delta x \\geq \\frac{h}{4\\pi}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(\\Delta p\\) is the error in the measurement of momentum, \\(\\Delta x\\) is the error in the measurement of position, and \\(h\\) is Planck's constant.\n\nInitially, let's denote the original error in momentum as \\(\\Delta p_0\\) and the original error in position as \\(\\Delta x_0\\). According to the principle, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta p_0 \\cdot \\Delta x_0 = \\frac{h}{4\\pi}\n\\]\n\nNow, suppose the error in the measurement of momentum is halved, so the new error in momentum is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta p = \\frac{\\Delta p_0}{2}\n\\]\n\nTo satisfy the uncertainty principle, the new error in position \\(\\Delta x\\) must satisfy:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta p \\cdot \\Delta x \\geq \\frac{h}{4\\pi}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the new \\(\\Delta p\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\Delta p_0}{2} \\cdot \\Delta x = \\frac{h}{4\\pi}\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(\\Delta x\\), we get:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta x = \\frac{h}{4\\pi} \\cdot \\frac{2}{\\Delta p_0} = 2 \\cdot \\Delta x_0\n\\]\n\nThis means the new error in position \\(\\Delta x\\) is twice the original error \\(\\Delta x_0\\).\n\nTo find the percentage increase in the error of position, we calculate:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Percentage Increase} = \\left(\\frac{\\Delta x - \\Delta x_0}{\\Delta x_0}\\right) \\times 100\\%\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(\\Delta x = 2 \\cdot \\Delta x_0\\):\n\n\\[\n\\text{Percentage Increase} = \\left(\\frac{2 \\cdot \\Delta x_0 - \\Delta x_0}{\\Delta x_0}\\right) \\times 100\\% = \\left(\\frac{\\Delta x_0}{\\Delta x_0}\\right) \\times 100\\% = 100\\%\n\\]\n\nThus, the minimum error in the measurement of its position increases by \\(\\boxed{100\\%}\\)."
'To find the integer values of \\( x \\) for which \\( |x^2 - 16| \\) is a prime number, we need to consider two cases: when \\( x^2 - 16 \\) is positive and when it is negative.\n\n**Case 1:** \\( x^2 - 16 \\) is positive.\n\nIn this case, \\( x^2 - 16 = p \\), where \\( p \\) is a prime number. Thus, we have:\n\n\\[\nx^2 = p + 16\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x^2 \\) must be a perfect square, we need to check small values of \\( p \\) to see if \\( p + 16 \\) is a perfect square.\n\n- If \\( p = 2 \\), then \\( x^2 = 18 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 3 \\), then \\( x^2 = 19 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 5 \\), then \\( x^2 = 21 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 7 \\), then \\( x^2 = 23 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 11 \\), then \\( x^2 = 27 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 13 \\), then \\( x^2 = 29 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 17 \\), then \\( x^2 = 33 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n\nNone of these values work, so we move to the next case.\n\n**Case 2:** \\( x^2 - 16 \\) is negative.\n\nIn this case, \\( 16 - x^2 = p \\), where \\( p \\) is a prime number. Thus, we have:\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 16 - p\n\\]\n\nAgain, \\( x^2 \\) must be a perfect square, so we check small values of \\( p \\) to see if \\( 16 - p \\) is a perfect square.\n\n- If \\( p = 2 \\), then \\( x^2 = 14 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 3 \\), then \\( x^2 = 13 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 5 \\), then \\( x^2 = 11 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 7 \\), then \\( x^2 = 9 \\), which is a perfect square. Thus, \\( x = \\pm 3 \\).\n- If \\( p = 11 \\), then \\( x^2 = 5 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 13 \\), then \\( x^2 = 3 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n\nThe only values of \\( x \\) that work are \\( x = 3 \\) and \\( x = -3 \\).\n\nThe product of these integer values is:\n\n\\[\n3 \\times (-3) = -9\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the two integer values for \\( x \\) for which \\( |x^2 - 16| \\) is a prime number is \\(\\boxed{-9}\\).'
'To find \\( f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) \\), we first need to determine the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) of \\( f(x) = \\frac{2}{x+1} \\).\n\n1. Start by setting \\( y = f(x) = \\frac{2}{x+1} \\).\n2. Solve for \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y \\):\n   \\[\n   y = \\frac{2}{x+1}\n   \\]\n   Multiply both sides by \\( x+1 \\):\n   \\[\n   y(x+1) = 2\n   \\]\n   Expand and rearrange:\n   \\[\n   yx + y = 2\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   yx = 2 - y\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{2-y}{y}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the inverse function is \\( f^{-1}(x) = \\frac{2-x}{x} \\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\( f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) \\):\n\\[\nf^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) = \\frac{2 - \\frac{1}{5}}{\\frac{1}{5}}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the numerator:\n\\[\n2 - \\frac{1}{5} = \\frac{10}{5} - \\frac{1}{5} = \\frac{9}{5}\n\\]\n\nNow divide by \\(\\frac{1}{5}\\):\n\\[\n\\frac{\\frac{9}{5}}{\\frac{1}{5}} = \\frac{9}{5} \\times \\frac{5}{1} = 9\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) \\) is \\(\\boxed{9}\\).'
'To find the distance between the vertex of the parabola given by the equation \\( y = x^2 + 2x - 6 \\) and the point \\( (4, 5) \\), we first need to determine the vertex of the parabola.\n\nThe equation of the parabola is in the form \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 2 \\), and \\( c = -6 \\). The vertex of a parabola in this form is given by the formula:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{b}{2a}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values of \\( a \\) and \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{2}{2 \\times 1} = -1\n\\]\n\nNow, we substitute \\( x = -1 \\) back into the equation to find the \\( y \\)-coordinate of the vertex:\n\n\\[\ny = (-1)^2 + 2(-1) - 6 = 1 - 2 - 6 = -7\n\\]\n\nThus, the vertex of the parabola is at the point \\( (-1, -7) \\).\n\nNext, we calculate the distance between the vertex \\( (-1, -7) \\) and the point \\( (4, 5) \\) using the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the coordinates of the two points:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(4 - (-1))^2 + (5 - (-7))^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(4 + 1)^2 + (5 + 7)^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{5^2 + 12^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{25 + 144}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{169}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = 13\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the distance between the vertex of the parabola and the point \\( (4, 5) \\) is \\(\\boxed{13}\\).'

'To find the product of \\(x\\) and \\(y\\), we first need to solve the system of equations:\n\n\\[\n2x - 3y = 8\n\\]\n\\[\n4x + 3y = -2\n\\]\n\nWe can add these two equations to eliminate \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\n(2x - 3y) + (4x + 3y) = 8 + (-2)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n6x = 6\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by 6, we find:\n\n\\[\nx = 1\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\(x = 1\\) back into the first equation to solve for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\n2(1) - 3y = 8\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n2 - 3y = 8\n\\]\n\nSubtract 2 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n-3y = 6\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by -3:\n\n\\[\ny = -2\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\(x = 1\\) and \\(y = -2\\), the product \\(xy\\) is:\n\n\\[\nxy = 1 \\times (-2) = -2\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) is \\(\\boxed{-2}\\).'
'Let the two numbers be \\( x \\) and \\( y \\). We are given the equations:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\nxy = 35\n\\]\n\nWe want to find the positive difference between the numbers, which is \\( |x - y| \\).\n\nTo find \\( x - y \\), we can use the identity:\n\n\\[\n(x - y)^2 = (x + y)^2 - 4xy\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values:\n\n\\[\n(x - y)^2 = 12^2 - 4 \\times 35\n\\]\n\n\\[\n(x - y)^2 = 144 - 140\n\\]\n\n\\[\n(x - y)^2 = 4\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we find:\n\n\\[\n|x - y| = \\sqrt{4} = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the positive difference between the numbers is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
'To find the positive difference between the sum of the first 20 positive multiples of 5 and the sum of the first 20 positive even integers, we need to calculate each sum separately and then find their difference.\n\n**Step 1: Sum of the first 20 positive multiples of 5**\n\nThe first 20 positive multiples of 5 are: \n\\[ 5, 10, 15, \\ldots, 100. \\]\n\nThis is an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\( a = 5 \\) and the common difference \\( d = 5 \\). The number of terms \\( n = 20 \\).\n\nThe formula for the sum of an arithmetic sequence is:\n\\[ S_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (a + l), \\]\nwhere \\( l \\) is the last term.\n\nThe last term \\( l \\) can be calculated as:\n\\[ l = a + (n-1) \\times d = 5 + (20-1) \\times 5 = 5 + 95 = 100. \\]\n\nThus, the sum is:\n\\[ S_{20} = \\frac{20}{2} \\times (5 + 100) = 10 \\times 105 = 1050. \\]\n\n**Step 2: Sum of the first 20 positive even integers**\n\nThe first 20 positive even integers are:\n\\[ 2, 4, 6, \\ldots, 40. \\]\n\nThis is also an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\( a = 2 \\) and the common difference \\( d = 2 \\). The number of terms \\( n = 20 \\).\n\nThe last term \\( l \\) is:\n\\[ l = a + (n-1) \\times d = 2 + (20-1) \\times 2 = 2 + 38 = 40. \\]\n\nThus, the sum is:\n\\[ S_{20} = \\frac{20}{2} \\times (2 + 40) = 10 \\times 42 = 420. \\]\n\n**Step 3: Calculate the positive difference**\n\nThe positive difference between the two sums is:\n\\[ 1050 - 420 = 630. \\]\n\nTherefore, the positive difference is \\(\\boxed{630}\\).'

We take half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), which is \\(-8\\), divide it by 2 to get \\(-4\\), and then square it to get \\(16\\).\n\n   \\[\n   x^2 - 8x = (x - 4)^2 - 16\n   \\]\n\n2. **Rewrite the original equation:**\n\n   Substitute the completed square back into the original equation:\n\n   \\[\n   (x - 4)^2 - 16 - 49 = 0\n   \\]\n\n   Simplify the constant terms:\n\n   \\[\n   (x - 4)^2 - 65 = 0\n   \\]\n\n3. **Express in the form \\((ax + b)^2 + c\\):**\n\n   The equation \\((x - 4)^2 - 65 = 0\\) is already in the form \\((ax + b)^2 + c\\), where \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = -4\\), and \\(c = -65\\).\n\n4. **Calculate \\(ab\\):**\n\n   \\[\n   ab = 1 \\times (-4) = -4\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(ab\\) is \\(\\boxed{-4}\\).'
'To solve the problem, we need to evaluate the function \\( f(x) \\) for each given value and then sum the results.\n\n1. **Evaluate \\( f(\\sqrt[3]{-8}) \\):**\n\n   \\(\\sqrt[3]{-8} = -2\\), which is a rational number. Therefore, we use the first case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(\\sqrt[3]{-8}) = |\\lfloor -2 \\rfloor| = |-2| = 2.\n   \\]\n\n2. **Evaluate \\( f(-\\pi) \\):**\n\n   \\(-\\pi\\) is an irrational number. Therefore, we use the second case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(-\\pi) = \\lceil -\\pi \\rceil^2.\n   \\]\n   Since \\(-\\pi \\approx -3.14\\), we have \\(\\lceil -\\pi \\rceil = -3\\). This inequality describes the set of \\(x\\) values that are within or on the boundary of the interval defined by the solutions to the equation. "To find the function \\( k(x) \\) such that \\( f(x) \\) is its own inverse, we need to ensure that \\( f(f(x)) = x \\) for all \\( x \\).\n\nGiven the piecewise function:\n\\[\nf(x) =\n\\begin{cases}\nk(x) & \\text{if } x > 0, \\\\\n-\\frac{1}{2x} & \\text{if } x < 0, \\\\\n0 & \\text{if } x = 0.\n\\end{cases}\n\\]\n\nWe need to consider the cases for \\( x > 0 \\) and \\( x < 0 \\) separately.\n\n**Case 1: \\( x > 0 \\)**\n\nFor \\( x > 0 \\), \\( f(x) = k(x) \\). Since \\( f \\) is its own inverse, we have:\n\\[\nf(f(x)) = f(k(x)) = x.\n\\]\nSince \\( k(x) > 0 \\), we have \\( f(k(x)) = k(k(x)) \\). Therefore, we need:\n\\[\nk(k(x)) = x.\n\\]\n\n**Case 2: \\( x < 0 \\)**\n\nFor \\( x < 0 \\), \\( f(x) = -\\frac{1}{2x} \\). We need:\n\\[\nf(f(x)) = f\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = x.\n\\]\nSince \\(-\\frac{1}{2x} > 0\\), we use \\( f(x) = k(x) \\) for positive inputs:\n\\[\nk\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = x.\n\\]\n\n**Finding \\( k(x) \\):**\n\nFrom the requirement \\( k(k(x)) = x \\), we can try a function of the form \\( k(x) = \\frac{1}{2x} \\). Let's verify:\n\n1. **Check \\( k(k(x)) = x \\):**\n   \\[\n   k(k(x)) = k\\left(\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = \\frac{1}{2\\left(\\frac{1}{2x}\\right)} = x.\n   \\]\n\n2. **Check \\( f(f(x)) = x \\) for \\( x < 0 \\):**\n   \\[\n   f\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = k\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = \\frac{1}{2\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right)} = x.\n   \\]\n\nThus, the function \\( k(x) = \\frac{1}{2x} \\) satisfies all conditions for \\( f(x) \\) to be its own inverse. Therefore, the function \\( k(x) \\) is:\n\\[\nk(x) = \\frac{1}{2x}.\n\\]"
'To solve for \\( f(g(f(g(f(8))))) \\), we need to evaluate the expression step by step using the given functions \\( f(x) = \\sqrt{x} \\) and \\( g(x) = x^2 \\).\n\n1. **Calculate \\( f(8) \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(8) = \\sqrt{8} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Calculate \\( g(f(8)) = g(2\\sqrt{2}) \\):**\n   \\[\n   g(2\\sqrt{2}) = (2\\sqrt{2})^2 = 4 \\times 2 = 8\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate \\( f(g(f(8))) = f(8) \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(8) = \\sqrt{8} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate \\( g(f(g(f(8)))) = g(2\\sqrt{2}) \\):**\n   \\[\n   g(2\\sqrt{2}) = (2\\sqrt{2})^2 = 8\n   \\]\n\n5. **Calculate \\( f(g(f(g(f(8))))) = f(8) \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(8) = \\sqrt{8} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the final result is:\n\\[\nf(g(f(g(f(8))))) = 2\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{2\\sqrt{2}}\\).'
'To find the least value of \\( b \\) such that \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 \\le 0 \\), we first need to solve the quadratic inequality. We start by finding the roots of the corresponding quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\nb^2 + 2b - 15 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe can solve this using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-B \\pm \\sqrt{B^2 - 4AC}}{2A}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( A = 1 \\), \\( B = 2 \\), and \\( C = -15 \\). Plugging in these values, we have:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{2^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-15)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{4 + 60}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{64}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 \\pm 8}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us the roots:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 + 8}{2} = 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 - 8}{2} = -5\n\\]\n\nThe roots of the equation are \\( b = 3 \\) and \\( b = -5 \\). The quadratic \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 \\) is a parabola that opens upwards (since the coefficient of \\( b^2 \\) is positive). Therefore, the inequality \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 \\le 0 \\) holds between the roots \\( b = -5 \\) and \\( b = 3 \\).\n\nThus, the solution to the inequality is:\n\n\\[\n-5 \\le b \\le 3\n\\]\n\nThe least value of \\( b \\) that satisfies the inequality is \\( b = -5 \\).\n\nTherefore, the least value of \\( b \\) is \\(\\boxed{-5}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to account for the time difference between New York and Denver and the duration of the train journey.\n\n1. **Time Difference**: When it is noon in New York, it is 10 a.m. in Denver. This means Denver is 2 hours behind New York.\n\n2. **Departure Time**: The train leaves New York at 2 p.m. New York time. In Denver time, this would be 2 p.m. - 2 hours = 12 p.m. (noon).\n\n3. **Travel Duration**: The train journey takes 45 hours.\n\n4. **Arrival Time in Denver**: We add the 45-hour travel duration to the departure time in Denver time (12 p.m.):\n   - 12 p.m. + 24 hours = 12 p.m. (next day)\n   - 12 p.m. + 21 hours = 9 a.m.\n\nTherefore, the train arrives in Denver at 9 a.m. Denver time. The answer is \\(\\boxed{9 \\text{ a.m.}}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to understand the transformations applied to the function \\( f(x) \\) and how they relate to the original function.\n\nThe problem states that when the graph of \\( f(x) \\) is shifted 2 units to the right and stretched vertically by a factor of 2, the resulting graph is identical to the original graph. This means that for every \\( x \\), the following relationship holds:\n\n\\[\n2f(x-2) = f(x)\n\\]\n\nWe are also given that \\( f(0) = 0.1 \\).\n\nLet's use this information to find \\( f(10) \\).\n\n1. Start with \\( f(0) = 0.1 \\).\n2. Use the relationship \\( 2f(x-2) = f(x) \\) to find \\( f(2) \\):\n   \\[\n   2f(0) = f(2) \\implies 2 \\times 0.1 = f(2) \\implies f(2) = 0.2\n   \\]\n3. Use the relationship again to find \\( f(4) \\):\n   \\[\n   2f(2) = f(4) \\implies 2 \\times 0.2 = f(4) \\implies f(4) = 0.4\n   \\]\n4. Continue this process to find \\( f(6) \\):\n   \\[\n   2f(4) = f(6) \\implies 2 \\times 0.4 = f(6) \\implies f(6) = 0.8\n   \\]\n5. Next, find \\( f(8) \\):\n   \\[\n   2f(6) = f(8) \\implies 2 \\times 0.8 = f(8) \\implies f(8) = 1.6\n   \\]\n6. Finally, find \\( f(10) \\):\n   \\[\n   2f(8) = f(10) \\implies 2 \\times 1.6 = f(10) \\implies f(10) = 3.2\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(10) \\) is \\(\\boxed{3.2}\\)."
"To solve this problem, we first need to determine Alice's speed. We know that Beatrice takes 25 seconds to complete the 100-meter race. Therefore, Beatrice's speed is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Beatrice's speed} = \\frac{100 \\text{ meters}}{25 \\text{ seconds}} = 4 \\text{ meters per second}\n\\]\n\nAlice finishes the race 5 seconds before Beatrice, so it takes Alice:\n\n\\[\n25 \\text{ seconds} - 5 \\text{ seconds} = 20 \\text{ seconds}\n\\]\n\nto complete the 100-meter race. Therefore, Alice's speed is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Alice's speed} = \\frac{100 \\text{ meters}}{20 \\text{ seconds}} = 5 \\text{ meters per second}\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find out how long it takes Alice to run 50 meters at her speed of 5 meters per second. The time it takes is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Time} = \\frac{\\text{Distance}}{\\text{Speed}} = \\frac{50 \\text{ meters}}{5 \\text{ meters per second}} = 10 \\text{ seconds}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, it would take Alice \\(\\boxed{10}\\) seconds to run 50 meters."
'For the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + mx + (m+n) = 0\\) to have one real solution, the discriminant must be zero. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) of a quadratic equation \\(ax^2 + bx + c = 0\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = b^2 - 4ac\n\\]\n\nIn this case, \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = m\\), and \\(c = m+n\\). Therefore, the discriminant is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = m^2 - 4(1)(m+n) = m^2 - 4m - 4n\n\\]\n\nSetting the discriminant equal to zero for the quadratic to have one real solution, we have:\n\n\\[\nm^2 - 4m - 4n = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in terms of \\(m\\). For there to be a unique value of \\(m\\), the discriminant of this quadratic equation must also be zero. The discriminant of \\(m^2 - 4m - 4n = 0\\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta_m = (-4)^2 - 4(1)(-4n) = 16 + 16n\n\\]\n\nSetting this discriminant to zero gives:\n\n\\[\n16 + 16n = 0\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(n\\), we find:\n\n\\[\n16n = -16 \\\\\nn = -1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(n\\) is \\(\\boxed{-1}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we first need to find the sum of the first ten positive integers and then determine which integer Marsha did not include to make the sum a square number.\n\nThe sum of the first ten positive integers is given by the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{n(n+1)}{2}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( n = 10 \\). Thus, the sum is:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{10 \\times 11}{2} = 55\n\\]\n\nMarsha's sum is a square number, so we need to find a number \\( x \\) such that \\( 55 - x \\) is a perfect square. We will check each integer from 1 to 10 to see which one, when removed, results in a perfect square.\n\nLet's check each possibility:\n\n- If \\( x = 1 \\), then \\( 55 - 1 = 54 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 2 \\), then \\( 55 - 2 = 53 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 3 \\), then \\( 55 - 3 = 52 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 4 \\), then \\( 55 - 4 = 51 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 5 \\), then \\( 55 - 5 = 50 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 6 \\), then \\( 55 - 6 = 49 \\), which is \\( 7^2 \\) (a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 7 \\), then \\( 55 - 7 = 48 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 8 \\), then \\( 55 - 8 = 47 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 9 \\), then \\( 55 - 9 = 46 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 10 \\), then \\( 55 - 10 = 45 \\) (not a perfect square).\n\nThe only integer that, when removed, results in a perfect square is 6. Therefore, Marsha did not include the number \\(\\boxed{6}\\)."
'To solve the equation \\(\\log_{64^{\\frac{1}{3}}}4^x = 1\\), we start by simplifying the base of the logarithm. \n\nFirst, note that:\n\\[\n64 = 4^3\n\\]\nThus:\n\\[\n64^{\\frac{1}{3}} = (4^3)^{\\frac{1}{3}} = 4^{3 \\cdot \\frac{1}{3}} = 4^1 = 4\n\\]\n\nThis means the equation simplifies to:\n\\[\n\\log_{4} 4^x = 1\n\\]\n\nThe property of logarithms \\(\\log_b b^y = y\\) allows us to simplify further:\n\\[\nx = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'To solve for \\( f^{-1}(f^{-1}(6)) \\), we first need to determine the inverse function values based on the given information about \\( f \\).\n\nGiven:\n- \\( f(1) = 2 \\)\n- \\( f(2) = 6 \\)\n- \\( f(3) = 5 \\)\n\nThe inverse function \\( f^{-1} \\) will reverse these mappings:\n- Since \\( f(2) = 6 \\), it follows that \\( f^{-1}(6) = 2 \\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\( f^{-1}(f^{-1}(6)) \\):\n- We already found that \\( f^{-1}(6) = 2 \\).\n- Next, we need to find \\( f^{-1}(2) \\). Since \\( f(1) = 2 \\), it follows that \\( f^{-1}(2) = 1 \\).\n\nTherefore, \\( f^{-1}(f^{-1}(6)) = f^{-1}(2) = 1 \\).\n\nThe answer is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To find \\( a + b \\), we start by using the fact that the roots of the polynomial \\( p(x) = x^2 + ax + b \\) are given as \\( 2a \\) and \\( b \\).\n\nBy Vieta's formulas, the sum of the roots of the polynomial is equal to the negation of the coefficient of \\( x \\) divided by the leading coefficient. Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\n2a + b = -a\n\\]\n\nRearranging this equation gives:\n\n\\[\n3a + b = 0 \\quad \\text{(Equation 1)}\n\\]\n\nAlso, by Vieta's formulas, the product of the roots is equal to the constant term divided by the leading coefficient. Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\n2a \\cdot b = b\n\\]\n\nAssuming \\( b \\neq 0 \\) (since the roots are distinct), we can divide both sides by \\( b \\) to obtain:\n\n\\[\n2a = 1\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( a \\), we find:\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( a = \\frac{1}{2} \\) into Equation 1:\n\n\\[\n3\\left(\\frac{1}{2}\\right) + b = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2} + b = 0\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( b \\), we find:\n\n\\[\nb = -\\frac{3}{2}\n\\]\n\nFinally, we calculate \\( a + b \\):\n\n\\[\na + b = \\frac{1}{2} - \\frac{3}{2} = -1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( a + b \\) is \\(\\boxed{-1}\\)."
"To solve this problem, we need to establish relationships between the weights of treeks, squigs, and goolees. Let's denote the weight of a treek as \\( T \\), the weight of a squig as \\( S \\), and the weight of a goolee as \\( G \\).\n\nFrom the problem, we have the following equations:\n\n1. \\( 10T = 3S + G \\)\n2. \\( 2T + G = S \\)\n\nWe want to find the number of treeks that equal the weight of one squig, i.e., we want to express \\( S \\) in terms of \\( T \\).\n\nFirst, solve the second equation for \\( G \\):\n\n\\[ G = S - 2T \\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( G \\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[ 10T = 3S + (S - 2T) \\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[ 10T = 4S - 2T \\]\n\nAdd \\( 2T \\) to both sides:\n\n\\[ 12T = 4S \\]\n\nDivide both sides by 4:\n\n\\[ 3T = S \\]\n\nThus, the weight of one squig is equivalent to the weight of 3 treeks. Therefore, the combined weight of \\(\\boxed{3}\\) treeks equals the weight of one squig."
"Let's denote the number of clowns as \\( c \\) and the number of horses as \\( h \\).\n\nWe know that:\n- Each clown has 2 legs and 1 head.\n- Each horse has 4 legs and 1 head.\n\nFrom the problem, we have the following equations based on the number of heads and legs:\n\n1. The total number of heads is 10:\n   \\[\n   c + h = 10\n   \\]\n\n2. The total number of legs is 30:\n   \\[\n   2c + 4h = 30\n   \\]\n\nWe can solve this system of equations to find the values of \\( c \\) and \\( h \\).\n\nFirst, solve the first equation for \\( c \\):\n\\[\nc = 10 - h\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( c = 10 - h \\) into the second equation:\n\\[\n2(10 - h) + 4h = 30\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( h \\):\n\\[\n20 - 2h + 4h = 30\n\\]\n\\[\n20 + 2h = 30\n\\]\n\\[\n2h = 10\n\\]\n\\[\nh = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, there are \\(\\boxed{5}\\) horses in the parade."
"Let's denote the weight of \\( B \\) as \\( b \\), the weight of \\( A \\) as \\( a \\), and the weight of \\( C \\) as \\( c \\).\n\nFirst, we know that the weight of \\( A \\) is \\( 40\\% \\) greater than the weight of \\( B \\). This can be expressed as:\n\\[\na = b + 0.4b = 1.4b\n\\]\n\nNext, we know that the weight of \\( A \\) is \\( 30\\% \\) less than the weight of \\( C \\). This can be expressed as:\n\\[\na = c - 0.3c = 0.7c\n\\]\n\nWe now have two equations:\n1. \\( a = 1.4b \\)\n2. \\( a = 0.7c \\)\n\nSince both expressions equal \\( a \\), we can set them equal to each other:\n\\[\n1.4b = 0.7c\n\\]\n\nTo find the ratio of the weight of \\( B \\) to the weight of \\( C \\), we solve for \\( \\frac{b}{c} \\):\n\\[\n1.4b = 0.7c \\implies b = \\frac{0.7}{1.4}c\n\\]\n\nSimplifying \\( \\frac{0.7}{1.4} \\):\n\\[\n\\frac{0.7}{1.4} = \\frac{7}{14} = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the ratio of the weight of \\( B \\) to the weight of \\( C \\) is:\n\\[\n\\frac{b}{c} = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the ratio of the weight of \\( B \\) to the weight of \\( C \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{2}}\\)."
'To find the sum of all numbers \\( a \\) for which the graphs of \\( y = x^2 + a \\) and \\( y = ax \\) intersect exactly once, we need to set the equations equal to each other and analyze the resulting equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + a = ax\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms, we get:\n\n\\[\nx^2 - ax + a = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in \\( x \\). For the graphs to intersect exactly once, the quadratic equation must have exactly one solution, which occurs when the discriminant is zero. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) of a quadratic equation \\(x^2 + bx + c = 0\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = b^2 - 4ac\n\\]\n\nIn our equation, \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = -a\\), and \\(c = a\\). Thus, the discriminant is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = (-a)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot a = a^2 - 4a\n\\]\n\nSetting the discriminant to zero for the quadratic to have exactly one solution:\n\n\\[\na^2 - 4a = 0\n\\]\n\nFactoring the equation:\n\n\\[\na(a - 4) = 0\n\\]\n\nThis gives the solutions:\n\n\\[\na = 0 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad a = 4\n\\]\n\nThe sum of all such \\( a \\) is:\n\n\\[\n0 + 4 = \\boxed{4}\n\\]'
'To solve the inequality \\((2x+10)(x+3) < (3x+9)(x+8)\\), we first expand both sides.\n\nExpanding the left side:\n\\[\n(2x+10)(x+3) = 2x(x) + 2x(3) + 10(x) + 10(3) = 2x^2 + 6x + 10x + 30 = 2x^2 + 16x + 30\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\\[\n(3x+9)(x+8) = 3x(x) + 3x(8) + 9(x) + 9(8) = 3x^2 + 24x + 9x + 72 = 3x^2 + 33x + 72\n\\]\n\nNow, we set up the inequality:\n\\[\n2x^2 + 16x + 30 < 3x^2 + 33x + 72\n\\]\n\nSubtract the left side from the right side to bring all terms to one side:\n\\[\n0 < 3x^2 + 33x + 72 - 2x^2 - 16x - 30\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\\[\n0 < x^2 + 17x + 42\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\\[\nx^2 + 17x + 42 > 0\n\\]\n\nTo solve this inequality, we first find the roots of the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + 17x + 42 = 0\\) using the quadratic formula:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\nwhere \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = 17\\), and \\(c = 42\\).\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = 17^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 42 = 289 - 168 = 121\n\\]\n\nThe square root of 121 is 11, so the roots are:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-17 \\pm 11}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-17 + 11}{2} = \\frac{-6}{2} = -3\n\\]\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-17 - 11}{2} = \\frac{-28}{2} = -14\n\\]\n\nThe roots of the quadratic are \\(x = -3\\) and \\(x = -14\\). The quadratic \\(x^2 + 17x + 42\\) is a parabola opening upwards (since the coefficient of \\(x^2\\) is positive). Therefore, the quadratic is positive outside the interval defined by its roots.\n\nThus, the solution to the inequality \\(x^2 + 17x + 42 > 0\\) is:\n\\[\nx \\in (-\\infty, -14) \\cup (-3, \\infty)\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the solution in interval notation is:\n\\[\n\\boxed{(-\\infty, -14) \\cup (-3, \\infty)}\n\\]'
"To solve this problem, we need to calculate the future value of an investment with compound interest. The investment is compounded bi-monthly at a rate of \\(1\\%\\). \n\nFirst, let's determine the number of compounding periods. Since the interest is compounded every two months, there are 6 compounding periods per year. Over 5 years, the total number of compounding periods is:\n\n\\[\n5 \\text{ years} \\times 6 \\text{ periods per year} = 30 \\text{ periods}\n\\]\n\nThe interest rate per period is \\(1\\%\\), or \\(0.01\\) as a decimal.\n\nThe formula for compound interest is:\n\n\\[\nA = P(1 + r)^n\n\\]\n\nwhere:\n- \\(A\\) is the amount of money accumulated after \\(n\\) periods, including interest.\n- \\(P\\) is the principal amount (initial investment), which is \\(\\$24,000\\).\n- \\(r\\) is the interest rate per period, which is \\(0.01\\).\n- \\(n\\) is the number of periods, which is \\(30\\).\n\nSubstituting the known values into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nA = 24000 \\times (1 + 0.01)^{30}\n\\]\n\nCalculating the expression inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\n1 + 0.01 = 1.01\n\\]\n\nNow, raise \\(1.01\\) to the power of 30:\n\n\\[\n1.01^{30} \\approx 1.347848\n\\]\n\nFinally, multiply this result by the principal amount:\n\n\\[\nA \\approx 24000 \\times 1.347848 \\approx 32348.352\n\\]\n\nRounding to the nearest whole number, the total amount in the investment at the end of five years is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{32348}\n\\]"
"To determine the real values of \\( x \\) that are not in the domain of the function \\( f(x) = \\frac{1}{|x^2 + 3x - 4| + |x^2 + 9x + 20|} \\), we need to find when the denominator is zero. This occurs when:\n\n\\[\n|x^2 + 3x - 4| + |x^2 + 9x + 20| = 0\n\\]\n\nSince the absolute value of any real number is non-negative, the sum of two absolute values is zero if and only if each absolute value is zero. Therefore, we need:\n\n\\[\n|x^2 + 3x - 4| = 0 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad |x^2 + 9x + 20| = 0\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 3x - 4 = 0 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x^2 + 9x + 20 = 0\n\\]\n\nLet's solve each quadratic equation separately.\n\n1. Solving \\( x^2 + 3x - 4 = 0 \\):\n\nUsing the quadratic formula \\( x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 3 \\), and \\( c = -4 \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{3^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-4)}}{2 \\cdot 1} = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{9 + 16}}{2} = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{25}}{2} = \\frac{-3 \\pm 5}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives the solutions:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-3 + 5}{2} = 1 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x = \\frac{-3 - 5}{2} = -4\n\\]\n\n2. Solving \\( x^2 + 9x + 20 = 0 \\):\n\nUsing the quadratic formula \\( x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 9 \\), and \\( c = 20 \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-9 \\pm \\sqrt{9^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 20}}{2 \\cdot 1} = \\frac{-9 \\pm \\sqrt{81 - 80}}{2} = \\frac{-9 \\pm \\sqrt{1}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives the solutions:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-9 + 1}{2} = -4 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x = \\frac{-9 - 1}{2} = -5\n\\]\n\nThe values of \\( x \\) that make the denominator zero are the common solutions of both equations. The common solution is \\( x = -4 \\).\n\nThus, the real value of \\( x \\) that is not in the domain of \\( f(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{-4}\\)."
'To find the value of \\( f(0) + f(-1) + f(-2) + f(-3) \\) for the function \\( f(x) = x^{(x+1)}(x+2)^{(x+3)} \\), we will evaluate each term separately.\n\n1. **Calculate \\( f(0) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(0) = 0^{(0+1)}(0+2)^{(0+3)} = 0^1 \\cdot 2^3 = 0 \\cdot 8 = 0\n   \\]\n\n2. **Calculate \\( f(-1) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-1) = (-1)^{(-1+1)}(-1+2)^{(-1+3)} = (-1)^0 \\cdot 1^2 = 1 \\cdot 1 = 1\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate \\( f(-2) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-2) = (-2)^{(-2+1)}(-2+2)^{(-2+3)} = (-2)^{-1} \\cdot 0^1\n   \\]\n\n   Since any non-zero number raised to a power multiplied by zero is zero, we have:\n\n   \\[\n   f(-2) = \\frac{1}{-2} \\cdot 0 = 0\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate \\( f(-3) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-3) = (-3)^{(-3+1)}(-3+2)^{(-3+3)} = (-3)^{-2} \\cdot (-1)^0\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   f(-3) = \\frac{1}{(-3)^2} \\cdot 1 = \\frac{1}{9} \\cdot 1 = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\nNow, we sum these results:\n\n\\[\nf(0) + f(-1) + f(-2) + f(-3) = 0 + 1 + 0 + \\frac{1}{9} = 1 + \\frac{1}{9} = \\frac{9}{9} + \\frac{1}{9} = \\frac{10}{9}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(0) + f(-1) + f(-2) + f(-3) \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{10}{9}}\\).'
'We are given three numbers \\( a \\), \\( b \\), and \\( c \\) such that their sum is:\n\n\\[\na + b + c = 88\n\\]\n\nWe also have the following conditions:\n\n1. If we decrease \\( a \\) by 5, we get \\( N \\):\n   \\[\n   a - 5 = N \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad a = N + 5\n   \\]\n\n2. If we increase \\( b \\) by 5, we get \\( N \\):\n   \\[\n   b + 5 = N \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad b = N - 5\n   \\]\n\n3. If we multiply \\( c \\) by 5, we get \\( N \\):\n   \\[\n   5c = N \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad c = \\frac{N}{5}\n   \\]\n\nSubstituting these expressions for \\( a \\), \\( b \\), and \\( c \\) into the sum equation:\n\n\\[\n(N + 5) + (N - 5) + \\frac{N}{5} = 88\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the left side:\n\n\\[\nN + 5 + N - 5 + \\frac{N}{5} = 88\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2N + \\frac{N}{5} = 88\n\\]\n\nTo eliminate the fraction, multiply the entire equation by 5:\n\n\\[\n5(2N) + 5\\left(\\frac{N}{5}\\right) = 5 \\times 88\n\\]\n\n\\[\n10N + N = 440\n\\]\n\n\\[\n11N = 440\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( N \\):\n\n\\[\nN = \\frac{440}{11} = 40\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( N \\) is \\(\\boxed{40}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to find the seventh term of a geometric sequence given the third term and the ninth term. Let's denote the first term of the sequence by \\( a \\) and the common ratio by \\( r \\).\n\nThe general formula for the \\( n \\)-th term of a geometric sequence is given by:\n\\[\na_n = a \\cdot r^{n-1}\n\\]\n\nGiven:\n- The third term \\( a_3 = a \\cdot r^2 = 1053 \\)\n- The ninth term \\( a_9 = a \\cdot r^8 = \\frac{13}{9} \\)\n\nWe need to find the seventh term \\( a_7 = a \\cdot r^6 \\).\n\nFirst, let's find the ratio \\( r \\) by dividing the ninth term by the third term:\n\\[\n\\frac{a \\cdot r^8}{a \\cdot r^2} = \\frac{\\frac{13}{9}}{1053}\n\\]\n\\[\nr^6 = \\frac{13}{9 \\times 1053}\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( 9 \\times 1053 \\):\n\\[\n9 \\times 1053 = 9477\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\\[\nr^6 = \\frac{13}{9477}\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\( a \\cdot r^6 \\), which is the seventh term:\n\\[\na \\cdot r^6 = (a \\cdot r^2) \\cdot r^4 = 1053 \\cdot r^4\n\\]\n\nWe know:\n\\[\nr^6 = \\frac{13}{9477}\n\\]\n\nTherefore:\n\\[\nr^4 = \\frac{r^6}{r^2} = \\frac{\\frac{13}{9477}}{r^2}\n\\]\n\nTo find \\( r^2 \\), we use:\n\\[\nr^2 = \\frac{a \\cdot r^2}{a} = \\frac{1053}{a}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back to find \\( a \\cdot r^6 \\):\n\\[\na \\cdot r^6 = 1053 \\cdot \\frac{13}{9477} \\cdot \\frac{9477}{1053}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying:\n\\[\na \\cdot r^6 = 13\n\\]\n\nThus, the seventh term is:\n\\[\n\\boxed{13}\n\\]"
'To evaluate \\(\\left(\\dfrac{-2i}{5}\\right)^2\\), we first square the fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\dfrac{-2i}{5}\\right)^2 = \\dfrac{(-2i)^2}{5^2}\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\((-2i)^2\\):\n\n\\[\n(-2i)^2 = (-2)^2 \\cdot i^2 = 4 \\cdot i^2\n\\]\n\nSince \\(i^2 = -1\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n4 \\cdot i^2 = 4 \\cdot (-1) = -4\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate \\(5^2\\):\n\n\\[\n5^2 = 25\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these results back into the fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\dfrac{(-2i)^2}{5^2} = \\dfrac{-4}{25}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\left(\\dfrac{-2i}{5}\\right)^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\dfrac{4}{25}}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( x^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} \\), we start with the given equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} = 7\n\\]\n\nWe want to find an expression for \\( x^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} \\). Notice that:\n\n\\[\n\\left( x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} \\right)^2 = x^4 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^4}\n\\]\n\nExpanding the left side, we have:\n\n\\[\n(x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2})^2 = x^4 + 2x^2 \\cdot \\frac{1}{x^2} + \\frac{1}{x^4} = x^4 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^4}\n\\]\n\nGiven that \\( x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} = 7 \\), we square both sides:\n\n\\[\n(7)^2 = x^4 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^4}\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n49 = x^4 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^4}\n\\]\n\nSubtract 2 from both sides to solve for \\( x^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} \\):\n\n\\[\nx^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} = 49 - 2 = 47\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} \\) is \\(\\boxed{47}\\).'

'To compute \\(32^2 - 18^2\\), we can use the difference of squares formula, which states:\n\n\\[\na^2 - b^2 = (a-b)(a+b)\n\\]\n\nIn this case, \\(a = 32\\) and \\(b = 18\\). Applying the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n32^2 - 18^2 = (32 - 18)(32 + 18)\n\\]\n\nCalculating each part:\n\n\\[\n32 - 18 = 14\n\\]\n\\[\n32 + 18 = 50\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these values back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n32^2 - 18^2 = 14 \\times 50\n\\]\n\nCalculate the product:\n\n\\[\n14 \\times 50 = 700\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(32^2 - 18^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{700}\\).'
'To find the fiftieth term of the arithmetic sequence, we first need to determine the common difference and the first term of the sequence.\n\nThe general formula for the \\( n \\)-th term of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\n\\[\na_n = a_1 + (n-1)d\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a_1 \\) is the first term and \\( d \\) is the common difference.\n\nWe know:\n- The second term \\( a_2 = 2 \\)\n- The ninth term \\( a_9 = 30 \\)\n\nUsing the formula for the second term:\n\n\\[\na_2 = a_1 + (2-1)d = a_1 + d = 2\n\\]\n\nUsing the formula for the ninth term:\n\n\\[\na_9 = a_1 + (9-1)d = a_1 + 8d = 30\n\\]\n\nWe now have the system of equations:\n\n1. \\( a_1 + d = 2 \\)\n2. \\( a_1 + 8d = 30 \\)\n\nSubtract the first equation from the second to eliminate \\( a_1 \\):\n\n\\[\n(a_1 + 8d) - (a_1 + d) = 30 - 2\n\\]\n\n\\[\n7d = 28\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = 4\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( d = 4 \\) back into the first equation to find \\( a_1 \\):\n\n\\[\na_1 + 4 = 2\n\\]\n\n\\[\na_1 = 2 - 4 = -2\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\( a_1 = -2 \\) and \\( d = 4 \\), we can find the fiftieth term \\( a_{50} \\):\n\n\\[\na_{50} = a_1 + (50-1)d = -2 + 49 \\times 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\na_{50} = -2 + 196\n\\]\n\n\\[\na_{50} = 194\n\\]\n\nThus, the fiftieth term of the sequence is \\(\\boxed{194}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to follow the transformations step by step and determine the new equation of the parabola after each transformation.\n\n1. **Original Equation:**\n   The original equation of the parabola is \\( y = -(x+1)^2 + 1 \\).\n\n2. **Shift 1 Unit to the Right:**\n   Shifting the parabola 1 unit to the right involves replacing \\( x \\) with \\( x-1 \\) in the equation:\n   \\[\n   y = -((x-1) + 1)^2 + 1 = -(x)^2 + 1 = -x^2 + 1.\n   \\]\n\n3. **Shift 5 Units Down:**\n   Shifting the parabola 5 units down involves subtracting 5 from the entire equation:\n   \\[\n   y = -x^2 + 1 - 5 = -x^2 - 4.\n   \\]\n\n4. **Rotate 180 Degrees About the Vertex:**\n   The vertex of the current parabola \\( y = -x^2 - 4 \\) is at \\( (0, -4) \\). Rotating the parabola 180 degrees about its vertex changes the sign of the \\( y \\)-term, effectively flipping the parabola:\n   \\[\n   y = x^2 - 4.\n   \\]\n\n5. **Find the Zeros of the Resulting Parabola:**\n   The equation of the resulting parabola is \\( y = x^2 - 4 \\). To find the zeros, set \\( y = 0 \\):\n   \\[\n   x^2 - 4 = 0.\n   \\]\n   Solving for \\( x \\), we have:\n   \\[\n   x^2 = 4 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = \\pm 2.\n   \\]\n   Thus, the zeros are \\( x = -2 \\) and \\( x = 2 \\).\n\n6. **Calculate \\( b-a \\):**\n   Here, \\( a = -2 \\) and \\( b = 2 \\). Therefore, \\( b-a = 2 - (-2) = 2 + 2 = 4 \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( b-a \\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To solve the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + 5x + 8 = 0\\) and express the solutions in the form \\(x = a + bi\\), we use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nFor the given equation, \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = 5\\), and \\(c = 8\\). Plugging these values into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{5^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 8}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\nCalculating the discriminant:\n\n\\[\n5^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 8 = 25 - 32 = -7\n\\]\n\nSince the discriminant is negative, the solutions will be complex. We continue with:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{-7}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten using imaginary numbers:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-5 \\pm i\\sqrt{7}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the solutions are:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{5}{2} + \\frac{\\sqrt{7}}{2}i \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x = -\\frac{5}{2} - \\frac{\\sqrt{7}}{2}i\n\\]\n\nIn the form \\(x = a + bi\\), we have \\(a = -\\frac{5}{2}\\) and \\(b = \\frac{\\sqrt{7}}{2}\\) for one of the solutions. We need to find \\(a + b^2\\):\n\n\\[\nb^2 = \\left(\\frac{\\sqrt{7}}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{7}{4}\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\(a + b^2\\):\n\n\\[\na + b^2 = -\\frac{5}{2} + \\frac{7}{4}\n\\]\n\nTo add these, convert \\(-\\frac{5}{2}\\) to a fraction with a denominator of 4:\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{5}{2} = -\\frac{10}{4}\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\na + b^2 = -\\frac{10}{4} + \\frac{7}{4} = -\\frac{3}{4}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(a + b^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{3}{4}}\\).'
'To find the total number of chimes the clock will strike in a twelve-hour period, we need to sum the number of chimes for each hour from 1 to 12.\n\nThe number of chimes at each hour is equal to the hour number itself. Therefore, the total number of chimes is the sum of the first 12 positive integers:\n\n\\[ 1 + 2 + 3 + \\cdots + 12. \\]\n\nThis is an arithmetic series where the first term \\( a = 1 \\), the last term \\( l = 12 \\), and the number of terms \\( n = 12 \\).\n\nThe formula for the sum of an arithmetic series is:\n\n\\[ S_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (a + l). \\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[ S_{12} = \\frac{12}{2} \\times (1 + 12) = 6 \\times 13 = 78. \\]\n\nTherefore, the total number of chimes the clock will strike in a twelve-hour period is \\(\\boxed{78}\\).'
"To determine the number of endpoints in Figure 5, we need to understand the pattern of how endpoints increase with each figure.\n\nLet's analyze the pattern:\n\n- **Figure 1**: The initial Y shape has 3 endpoints.\n- **Figure 2**: Each of the 3 endpoints from Figure 1 is replaced by a smaller Y, adding 2 new endpoints per original endpoint. Therefore, Figure 2 has \\(3 + 3 \\times 2 = 9\\) endpoints.\n- **Figure 3**: Each of the 9 endpoints from Figure 2 is replaced by a smaller Y, adding 2 new endpoints per original endpoint. Therefore, Figure 3 has \\(9 + 9 \\times 2 = 27\\) endpoints.\n\nWe can see a pattern forming: each figure has 3 times the number of endpoints as the previous figure. This is because each endpoint is replaced by a Y, which has 3 endpoints, effectively tripling the number of endpoints.\n\nThus, the number of endpoints in each figure follows a geometric sequence:\n- Figure 1: \\(3\\) endpoints\n- Figure 2: \\(3 \\times 3 = 9\\) endpoints\n- Figure 3: \\(9 \\times 3 = 27\\) endpoints\n- Figure 4: \\(27 \\times 3 = 81\\) endpoints\n- Figure 5: \\(81 \\times 3 = 243\\) endpoints\n\nTherefore, Figure 5 will have \\(\\boxed{243}\\) endpoints."
'To find the area of the circle, we first need to determine the radius. Since points \\(A(-1, -2)\\) and \\(B(3, 2)\\) are the endpoints of a diameter, we can find the length of the diameter using the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the coordinates of points \\(A\\) and \\(B\\):\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(3 - (-1))^2 + (2 - (-2))^2} = \\sqrt{(3 + 1)^2 + (2 + 2)^2} = \\sqrt{4^2 + 4^2} = \\sqrt{16 + 16} = \\sqrt{32} = 4\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThe diameter of the circle is \\(4\\sqrt{2}\\), so the radius \\(r\\) is half of the diameter:\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{4\\sqrt{2}}{2} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThe area \\(A\\) of the circle is given by the formula:\n\n\\[\nA = \\pi r^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the radius:\n\n\\[\nA = \\pi (2\\sqrt{2})^2 = \\pi \\times 4 \\times 2 = 8\\pi\n\\]\n\nThus, the area of the circle is \\(\\boxed{8\\pi}\\) square units.'

"To solve this problem, we need to find the number of non-congruent right triangles with integer side lengths where one of the legs is 162. Let's denote the sides of the triangle as \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\), where \\(c\\) is the hypotenuse and \\(a = 162\\).\n\nBy the Pythagorean theorem, we have:\n\n\\[\na^2 + b^2 = c^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(a = 162\\), we get:\n\n\\[\n162^2 + b^2 = c^2\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\nc^2 - b^2 = 162^2\n\\]\n\nThis is a difference of squares, which can be factored as:\n\n\\[\n(c-b)(c+b) = 162^2\n\\]\n\nCalculating \\(162^2\\):\n\n\\[\n162^2 = (160 + 2)^2 = 160^2 + 2 \\times 160 \\times 2 + 2^2 = 25600 + 640 + 4 = 26244\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n(c-b)(c+b) = 26244\n\\]\n\nTo find the number of solutions, we need to find the factor pairs of 26244. Let's start by finding the prime factorization of 26244.\n\nFirst, divide by 2:\n\n\\[\n26244 \\div 2 = 13122\n\\]\n\\[\n13122 \\div 2 = 6561\n\\]\n\nNext, divide by 3:\n\n\\[\n6561 \\div 3 = 2187\n\\]\n\\[\n2187 \\div 3 = 729\n\\]\n\\[\n729 \\div 3 = 243\n\\]\n\\[\n243 \\div 3 = 81\n\\]\n\\[\n81 \\div 3 = 27\n\\]\n\\[\n27 \\div 3 = 9\n\\]\n\\[\n9 \\div 3 = 3\n\\]\n\\[\n3 \\div 3 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the prime factorization of 26244 is:\n\n\\[\n26244 = 2^2 \\times 3^9\n\\]\n\nThe number of factor pairs is determined by the number of divisors. The number of divisors is given by:\n\n\\[\n(2+1)(9+1) = 3 \\times 10 = 30\n\\]\n\nEach factor pair \\((d_1, d_2)\\) corresponds to a solution \\((c-b, c+b)\\). For each pair, we solve for \\(c\\) and \\(b\\):\n\n\\[\nc = \\frac{d_1 + d_2}{2}, \\quad b = \\frac{d_2 - d_1}{2}\n\\]\n\nBoth \\(c\\) and \\(b\\) must be integers, which means \\(d_1\\) and \\(d_2\\) must have the same parity (both even or both odd). Since \\(26244\\) is even, all factor pairs will have the same parity, ensuring \\(c\\) and \\(b\\) are integers.\n\nThus, there are 15 valid factor pairs (since each pair \\((d_1, d_2)\\) is counted once, and \\((d_2, d_1)\\) is the same pair). Therefore, there are 15 non-congruent right triangles with one leg of length 162.\n\nThe answer is \\(\\boxed{15}\\)."

'To find the value of \\( x^3 - 2x + 1 \\) given that \\( x^2 - x - 1 = 0 \\), we can use the fact that \\( x \\) is a root of the quadratic equation.\n\nFirst, solve for \\( x^2 \\) from the equation \\( x^2 - x - 1 = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 = x + 1\n\\]\n\nNow, we want to find \\( x^3 - 2x + 1 \\). Start by expressing \\( x^3 \\) in terms of \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 = x \\cdot x^2 = x(x + 1) = x^2 + x\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( x^2 = x + 1 \\) into the expression for \\( x^3 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 = (x + 1) + x = 2x + 1\n\\]\n\nNow substitute this expression for \\( x^3 \\) into \\( x^3 - 2x + 1 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 - 2x + 1 = (2x + 1) - 2x + 1\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - 2x + 1 = 2x + 1 - 2x + 1 = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^3 - 2x + 1 \\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
