'To find the domain of the function \\( f(x) = \\sqrt{-6x^2 + 11x - 4} \\), we need to determine the values of \\( x \\) for which the expression under the square root is non-negative. This means we need to solve the inequality:\n\n\\[\n-6x^2 + 11x - 4 \\geq 0.\n\\]\n\nFirst, we find the roots of the quadratic equation \\( -6x^2 + 11x - 4 = 0 \\) using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a},\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = -6 \\), \\( b = 11 \\), and \\( c = -4 \\). Plugging in these values, we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-11 \\pm \\sqrt{11^2 - 4(-6)(-4)}}{2(-6)} = \\frac{-11 \\pm \\sqrt{121 - 96}}{-12}.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying under the square root:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-11 \\pm \\sqrt{25}}{-12} = \\frac{-11 \\pm 5}{-12}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives us the roots:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-11 + 5}{-12} = \\frac{-6}{-12} = \\frac{1}{2},\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-11 - 5}{-12} = \\frac{-16}{-12} = \\frac{4}{3}.\n\\]\n\nThe roots of the quadratic are \\( x = \\frac{1}{2} \\) and \\( x = \\frac{4}{3} \\).\n\nThe quadratic \\( -6x^2 + 11x - 4 \\) is a downward-opening parabola (since the coefficient of \\( x^2 \\) is negative). Therefore, the expression is non-negative between the roots. Thus, the solution to the inequality \\( -6x^2 + 11x - 4 \\geq 0 \\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2} \\leq x \\leq \\frac{4}{3}.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the domain of the function \\( f(x) \\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{\\left[\\frac{1}{2}, \\frac{4}{3}\\right]}.\n\\]'
'To find the value of \\( f(-2) + f(-1) + f(0) \\), we first need to evaluate each function value separately.\n\n1. **Calculate \\( f(-2) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-2) = \\frac{3(-2) - 2}{-2 - 2} = \\frac{-6 - 2}{-4} = \\frac{-8}{-4} = 2\n   \\]\n\n2. **Calculate \\( f(-1) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-1) = \\frac{3(-1) - 2}{-1 - 2} = \\frac{-3 - 2}{-3} = \\frac{-5}{-3} = \\frac{5}{3}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate \\( f(0) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(0) = \\frac{3(0) - 2}{0 - 2} = \\frac{-2}{-2} = 1\n   \\]\n\nNow, we sum these values:\n\n\\[\nf(-2) + f(-1) + f(0) = 2 + \\frac{5}{3} + 1\n\\]\n\nTo add these, we convert all terms to have a common denominator of 3:\n\n\\[\n2 = \\frac{6}{3}, \\quad 1 = \\frac{3}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{6}{3} + \\frac{5}{3} + \\frac{3}{3} = \\frac{6 + 5 + 3}{3} = \\frac{14}{3}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( f(-2) + f(-1) + f(0) \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{14}{3}}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( c \\) in the equation \\( y = x^2 + bx + c \\), we can use the fact that the parabola passes through the points \\( (2, 3) \\) and \\( (4, 3) \\).\n\nFirst, substitute the point \\( (2, 3) \\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\n3 = 2^2 + 2b + c\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n3 = 4 + 2b + c\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\n2b + c = -1 \\quad \\text{(Equation 1)}\n\\]\n\nNext, substitute the point \\( (4, 3) \\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\n3 = 4^2 + 4b + c\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n3 = 16 + 4b + c\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\n4b + c = -13 \\quad \\text{(Equation 2)}\n\\]\n\nNow, we have a system of two equations:\n\n1. \\( 2b + c = -1 \\)\n2. \\( 4b + c = -13 \\)\n\nSubtract Equation 1 from Equation 2 to eliminate \\( c \\):\n\n\\[\n(4b + c) - (2b + c) = -13 - (-1)\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n2b = -12\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( b \\) gives:\n\n\\[\nb = -6\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( b = -6 \\) back into Equation 1:\n\n\\[\n2(-6) + c = -1\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n-12 + c = -1\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( c \\) gives:\n\n\\[\nc = 11\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( c \\) is \\(\\boxed{11}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the coordinates of points \\( A \\) and \\( B \\) on the parabola \\( y = 3x^2 - 5x - 3 \\) such that the origin \\((0, 0)\\) is the midpoint of \\(\\overline{AB}\\).\n\nLet the coordinates of \\( A \\) be \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and the coordinates of \\( B \\) be \\((x_2, y_2)\\). Since the origin is the midpoint of \\(\\overline{AB}\\), we have:\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2}\\right) = (0, 0).\n\\]\nThis gives us the equations:\n\\[\nx_1 + x_2 = 0 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad y_1 + y_2 = 0.\n\\]\n\nFrom \\(x_1 + x_2 = 0\\), we have \\(x_2 = -x_1\\).\n\nSince both points lie on the parabola, we have:\n\\[\ny_1 = 3x_1^2 - 5x_1 - 3\n\\]\nand\n\\[\ny_2 = 3x_2^2 - 5x_2 - 3.\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(x_2 = -x_1\\) into the equation for \\(y_2\\), we get:\n\\[\ny_2 = 3(-x_1)^2 - 5(-x_1) - 3 = 3x_1^2 + 5x_1 - 3.\n\\]\n\nUsing the condition \\(y_1 + y_2 = 0\\), we have:\n\\[\n(3x_1^2 - 5x_1 - 3) + (3x_1^2 + 5x_1 - 3) = 0.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\\[\n6x_1^2 - 6 = 0.\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(x_1\\), we have:\n\\[\n6x_1^2 = 6 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x_1^2 = 1 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x_1 = \\pm 1.\n\\]\n\nThus, the possible coordinates for \\(A\\) and \\(B\\) are:\n- If \\(x_1 = 1\\), then \\(x_2 = -1\\).\n- If \\(x_1 = -1\\), then \\(x_2 = 1\\).\n\nFor \\(x_1 = 1\\), we find \\(y_1\\) and \\(y_2\\):\n\\[\ny_1 = 3(1)^2 - 5(1) - 3 = 3 - 5 - 3 = -5,\n\\]\n\\[\ny_2 = 3(-1)^2 + 5(-1) - 3 = 3 - 5 - 3 = -5.\n\\]\n\nThus, the points are \\(A(1, -5)\\) and \\(B(-1, -5)\\).\n\nThe length of \\(\\overline{AB}\\) is:\n\\[\nAB = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2} = \\sqrt{((-1) - 1)^2 + ((-5) - (-5))^2} = \\sqrt{(-2)^2 + 0^2} = \\sqrt{4} = 2.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the square of the length of \\(\\overline{AB}\\) is:\n\\[\n\\boxed{4}.\n\\]'
'To find a nonzero solution to the equation \\(\\sqrt{4c - 5c^2} = 0\\), we first set the expression inside the square root equal to zero:\n\n\\[\n4c - 5c^2 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe can factor out a \\(c\\) from the equation:\n\n\\[\nc(4 - 5c) = 0\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two possible solutions:\n\n1. \\(c = 0\\)\n2. \\(4 - 5c = 0\\)\n\nSince we are looking for a nonzero solution, we discard \\(c = 0\\) and solve the second equation:\n\n\\[\n4 - 5c = 0\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(c\\), we get:\n\n\\[\n5c = 4 \\\\\nc = \\frac{4}{5}\n\\]\n\nThus, the nonzero solution to the equation is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{4}{5}}\\).'

After the first doubling: \\(2.50 \\times 2 = 5.00\\)\n2. After the second doubling: \\(5.00 \\times 2 = 10.00\\)\n3. After the third doubling: \\(10.00 \\times 2 = 20.00\\)\n4. 'To find the value of \\( k \\), we need to ensure that points \\( A(9, 1) \\), \\( B(19, k) \\), and \\( C(7, 0) \\) are collinear, meaning they lie on the same line. We can do this by ensuring that the slopes between any two pairs of these points are equal.\n\nFirst, calculate the slope between points \\( A(9, 1) \\) and \\( C(7, 0) \\):\n\n\\[\n\\text{slope of } AC = \\frac{0 - 1}{7 - 9} = \\frac{-1}{-2} = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate the slope between points \\( A(9, 1) \\) and \\( B(19, k) \\):\n\n\\[\n\\text{slope of } AB = \\frac{k - 1}{19 - 9} = \\frac{k - 1}{10}\n\\]\n\nFor the points to be collinear, the slopes must be equal:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{k - 1}{10} = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\( k \\) by cross-multiplying:\n\n\\[\n2(k - 1) = 10\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2k - 2 = 10\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2k = 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\nk = 6\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( k \\) is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'

Therefore, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\nx \\cdot x^{3/2} = x^{1} \\cdot x^{3/2}\n\\]\n\nUsing the property of exponents that states \\(a^m \\cdot a^n = a^{m+n}\\), we combine the exponents:\n\n\\[\nx^{1 + 3/2} = x^{2/2 + 3/2} = x^{5/2}\n\\]\n\nNow, we raise this result to the power of 4:\n\n\\[\n(x^{5/2})^4\n\\]\n\nUsing the property of exponents \\((a^m)^n = a^{m \\cdot n}\\), we multiply the exponents:\n\n\\[\nx^{(5/2) \\cdot 4} = x^{20/2} = x^{10}\n\\]\n\nThus, the exponent of \\(x\\) in the simplified expression is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
'Since the pressure of a gas is inversely proportional to its volume at constant temperature, we can use the relationship \\( P_1 V_1 = P_2 V_2 \\), where \\( P_1 \\) and \\( V_1 \\) are the initial pressure and volume, and \\( P_2 \\) and \\( V_2 \\) are the final pressure and volume.\n\nGiven:\n- Initial volume \\( V_1 = 3.67 \\) liters\n- Initial pressure \\( P_1 = 4 \\) kPa\n- Final volume \\( V_2 = 1.835 \\) liters\n\nWe need to find the final pressure \\( P_2 \\).\n\nUsing the formula:\n\\[\nP_1 V_1 = P_2 V_2\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the known values:\n\\[\n4 \\times 3.67 = P_2 \\times 1.835\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( 4 \\times 3.67 \\):\n\\[\n4 \\times 3.67 = 14.68\n\\]\n\nNow solve for \\( P_2 \\):\n\\[\nP_2 = \\frac{14.68}{1.835}\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( \\frac{14.68}{1.835} \\):\n\\[\nP_2 \\approx 8.0\n\\]\n\nThus, the new pressure is approximately \\( \\boxed{8.0} \\) kPa.'

'To solve this problem, we need to find the smallest integer \\( b > 2011 \\) such that the difference between the \\((b+1)^{th}\\) and \\(b^{th}\\) triangular numbers is itself a triangular number.\n\nThe \\(n^{th}\\) triangular number is given by:\n\n\\[\nT(n) = \\frac{n(n+1)}{2}\n\\]\n\nThe difference between the \\((b+1)^{th}\\) and \\(b^{th}\\) triangular numbers is:\n\n\\[\nT(b+1) - T(b) = \\frac{(b+1)(b+2)}{2} - \\frac{b(b+1)}{2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying this expression, we have:\n\n\\[\nT(b+1) - T(b) = \\frac{(b+1)(b+2) - b(b+1)}{2} = \\frac{b^2 + 3b + 2 - b^2 - b}{2} = \\frac{2b + 2}{2} = b + 1\n\\]\n\nWe need \\(b + 1\\) to be a triangular number, say \\(T(x)\\). Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\nb + 1 = \\frac{x(x+1)}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{x(x+1)}{2} - 1\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the smallest \\(b > 2011\\). Thus, we solve:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x(x+1)}{2} - 1 > 2011\n\\]\n\nAdding 1 to both sides gives:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x(x+1)}{2} > 2012\n\\]\n\nMultiplying both sides by 2:\n\n\\[\nx(x+1) > 4024\n\\]\n\nTo find the smallest \\(x\\), we solve the quadratic inequality:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + x - 4024 > 0\n\\]\n\nUsing the quadratic formula to find the roots of the equation \\(x^2 + x - 4024 = 0\\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{1 + 4 \\times 4024}}{2} = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{16097}}{2}\n\\]\n\nApproximating \\(\\sqrt{16097}\\), we find:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{16097} \\approx 126.85\n\\]\n\nThus, the roots are approximately:\n\n\\[\nx \\approx \\frac{-1 + 126.85}{2} \\approx 62.925\n\\]\n\nSince \\(x\\) must be an integer, we take \\(x = 63\\).\n\nChecking \\(x = 63\\):\n\n\\[\nx(x+1) = 63 \\times 64 = 4032\n\\]\n\nSince \\(4032 > 4024\\), \\(x = 63\\) is valid. Therefore, the corresponding \\(b\\) is:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{63 \\times 64}{2} - 1 = 2015 - 1 = 2015\n\\]\n\nThus, the smallest integer \\(b > 2011\\) such that \\(T(b+1) - T(b) = T(x)\\) for some positive integer \\(x\\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{2015}\n\\]'
"To find the sixth term of the arithmetic sequence, we first need to determine the common difference of the sequence. Let's denote the first term of the sequence as \\( a \\) and the common difference as \\( d \\).\n\nThe formula for the \\( n \\)-th term of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\n\\[\na_n = a + (n-1)d\n\\]\n\nWe know the fourth term is 200, so:\n\n\\[\na_4 = a + 3d = 200\n\\]\n\nWe also know the eighth term is 500, so:\n\n\\[\na_8 = a + 7d = 500\n\\]\n\nWe have the following system of equations:\n\n1. \\( a + 3d = 200 \\)\n2. \\( a + 7d = 500 \\)\n\nTo find \\( d \\), we subtract the first equation from the second:\n\n\\[\n(a + 7d) - (a + 3d) = 500 - 200\n\\]\n\n\\[\n4d = 300\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = 75\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\( d = 75 \\), we can substitute it back into the first equation to find \\( a \\):\n\n\\[\na + 3(75) = 200\n\\]\n\n\\[\na + 225 = 200\n\\]\n\n\\[\na = 200 - 225 = -25\n\\]\n\nNow, we can find the sixth term using the formula for the \\( n \\)-th term:\n\n\\[\na_6 = a + 5d = -25 + 5(75)\n\\]\n\n\\[\na_6 = -25 + 375\n\\]\n\n\\[\na_6 = 350\n\\]\n\nThus, the sixth term of the sequence is \\(\\boxed{350}\\)."
'To solve the quadratic equation \\(0 = -21x^2 - 11x + 40\\), we can use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a = -21\\), \\(b = -11\\), and \\(c = 40\\).\n\nFirst, calculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = (-11)^2 - 4(-21)(40) = 121 + 3360 = 3481\n\\]\n\nNow, apply the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-(-11) \\pm \\sqrt{3481}}{2(-21)}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{11 \\pm \\sqrt{3481}}{-42}\n\\]\n\nNext, find \\(\\sqrt{3481}\\). Since \\(3481\\) is a perfect square, we find that:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{3481} = 59\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back into the formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{11 \\pm 59}{-42}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two possible solutions:\n\n1. \\(x = \\frac{11 + 59}{-42} = \\frac{70}{-42} = -\\frac{5}{3}\\)\n\n2. \\(x = \\frac{11 - 59}{-42} = \\frac{-48}{-42} = \\frac{48}{42} = \\frac{8}{7}\\)\n\nSince we are looking for the positive solution, we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{8}{7}\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(x = \\boxed{\\frac{8}{7}}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\left(\\frac{1}{9}\\right)^x = 3^{x+3}\\), we start by expressing \\(\\frac{1}{9}\\) as a power of 3. We know that:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{9} = 9^{-1} = (3^2)^{-1} = 3^{-2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n(3^{-2})^x = 3^{x+3}\n\\]\n\nUsing the property of exponents \\((a^m)^n = a^{mn}\\), we can rewrite the left side:\n\n\\[\n3^{-2x} = 3^{x+3}\n\\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we can equate the exponents:\n\n\\[\n-2x = x + 3\n\\]\n\nNow, solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n-2x - x = 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-3x = 3\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by \\(-3\\):\n\n\\[\nx = -1\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(x = \\boxed{-1}\\).'
"To find the value of \\( x \\) that satisfies both equations \\( 9x^2 - 18x - 16 = 0 \\) and \\( 15x^2 + 28x + 12 = 0 \\), we will solve the system of equations.\n\nFirst, let's solve the first equation:\n\n\\[ 9x^2 - 18x - 16 = 0. \\]\n\nWe can use the quadratic formula \\( x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 9 \\), \\( b = -18 \\), and \\( c = -16 \\).\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = (-18)^2 - 4 \\cdot 9 \\cdot (-16) = 324 + 576 = 900.\n\\]\n\nThe square root of 900 is 30. Thus, the solutions for \\( x \\) are:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-(-18) \\pm 30}{2 \\cdot 9} = \\frac{18 \\pm 30}{18}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{48}{18} = \\frac{8}{3} \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x = \\frac{-12}{18} = -\\frac{2}{3}.\n\\]\n\nNext, solve the second equation:\n\n\\[ 15x^2 + 28x + 12 = 0. \\]\n\nAgain, use the quadratic formula with \\( a = 15 \\), \\( b = 28 \\), and \\( c = 12 \\).\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = 28^2 - 4 \\cdot 15 \\cdot 12 = 784 - 720 = 64.\n\\]\n\nThe square root of 64 is 8. Thus, the solutions for \\( x \\) are:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-28 \\pm 8}{2 \\cdot 15} = \\frac{-28 \\pm 8}{30}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-20}{30} = -\\frac{2}{3} \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x = \\frac{-36}{30} = -\\frac{6}{5}.\n\\]\n\nThe common solution to both equations is \\( x = -\\frac{2}{3} \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{2}{3}}\\)."
"To find the value of the product \\( xy \\), we need to solve the system of equations:\n\n1. \\( 2x - 9y = 14 \\)\n2. \\( 6x = 42 + y \\)\n\nFirst, let's solve the second equation for \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\n6x = 42 + y \\implies y = 6x - 42\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( y = 6x - 42 \\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n2x - 9(6x - 42) = 14\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[\n2x - 54x + 378 = 14\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n-52x + 378 = 14\n\\]\n\nSubtract 378 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n-52x = 14 - 378\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-52x = -364\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by -52:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-364}{-52} = \\frac{364}{52} = \\frac{91}{13}\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x = \\frac{91}{13} \\) back into the expression for \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\ny = 6x - 42 = 6\\left(\\frac{91}{13}\\right) - 42\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( 6 \\times \\frac{91}{13} \\):\n\n\\[\n6 \\times \\frac{91}{13} = \\frac{546}{13} = 42\n\\]\n\nSo,\n\n\\[\ny = 42 - 42 = 0\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate the product \\( xy \\):\n\n\\[\nxy = \\left(\\frac{91}{13}\\right) \\times 0 = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the product \\( xy \\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\)."
'To determine the values of \\( c \\) for which the quadratic equation \\( 3x^2 + 7x + c = 0 \\) has two real roots, we need to ensure that the discriminant of the quadratic is positive. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) of a quadratic equation \\( ax^2 + bx + c = 0 \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = b^2 - 4ac\n\\]\n\nFor the quadratic \\( 3x^2 + 7x + c = 0 \\), we have \\( a = 3 \\), \\( b = 7 \\), and \\( c = c \\). Thus, the discriminant is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = 7^2 - 4 \\cdot 3 \\cdot c = 49 - 12c\n\\]\n\nWe require that the discriminant be positive for the quadratic to have two distinct real roots:\n\n\\[\n49 - 12c > 0\n\\]\n\nSolving this inequality for \\( c \\), we get:\n\n\\[\n49 > 12c\n\\]\n\n\\[\nc < \\frac{49}{12}\n\\]\n\nCalculating \\(\\frac{49}{12}\\), we find:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{49}{12} = 4.0833\\ldots\n\\]\n\nSince \\( c \\) must be a positive integer, the possible values for \\( c \\) are \\( 1, 2, 3, \\) and \\( 4 \\).\n\nNow, we find the product of these values:\n\n\\[\n1 \\times 2 \\times 3 \\times 4 = 24\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of all positive integer values of \\( c \\) such that the quadratic equation has two real roots is \\(\\boxed{24}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\frac{\\sqrt[3]{2x-4}}{\\sqrt[3]{x+4}} = 2\\), we start by letting \\(a = \\sqrt[3]{2x-4}\\) and \\(b = \\sqrt[3]{x+4}\\). The equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} = 2\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\na = 2b\n\\]\n\nSubstituting back the expressions for \\(a\\) and \\(b\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[3]{2x-4} = 2 \\cdot \\sqrt[3]{x+4}\n\\]\n\nCubing both sides to eliminate the cube roots, we get:\n\n\\[\n2x - 4 = (2 \\cdot \\sqrt[3]{x+4})^3\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the right side:\n\n\\[\n2x - 4 = 8(x+4)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\n\\[\n2x - 4 = 8x + 32\n\\]\n\nRearranging the terms to isolate \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n2x - 8x = 32 + 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-6x = 36\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by \\(-6\\):\n\n\\[\nx = -6\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(x = \\boxed{-6}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\sqrt{3x+6} = x+2\\), we start by squaring both sides to eliminate the square root:\n\n\\[\n(\\sqrt{3x+6})^2 = (x+2)^2\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n3x + 6 = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation to bring all terms to one side:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 - 3x - 6 = 0\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + x - 2 = 0\n\\]\n\nNext, we factor the quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + x - 2 = (x + 2)(x - 1) = 0\n\\]\n\nSetting each factor equal to zero gives the potential solutions:\n\n\\[\nx + 2 = 0 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = -2\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx - 1 = 0 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = 1\n\\]\n\nWe must check each solution in the original equation to ensure they are valid, as squaring both sides can introduce extraneous solutions.\n\n1. Check \\(x = -2\\):\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{3(-2) + 6} = \\sqrt{0} = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-2 + 2 = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a valid solution.\n\n2. Check \\(x = 1\\):\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{3(1) + 6} = \\sqrt{9} = 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1 + 2 = 3\n\\]\n\nThis is also a valid solution.\n\nBoth solutions are valid, so the solutions to the equation are:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{-2, 1}\n\\]'
"To find the distance between the original midpoint \\( M \\) and the new midpoint \\( M' \\), we first need to determine the coordinates of both midpoints.\n\nThe original midpoint \\( M \\) between points \\( A(a, b) \\) and \\( B(c, d) \\) is given by:\n\\[\nM = \\left( \\frac{a+c}{2}, \\frac{b+d}{2} \\right)\n\\]\n\nAfter moving point \\( A \\) vertically upwards by 20 units and horizontally to the right by 14 units, the new coordinates of \\( A \\) are:\n\\[\nA' = (a+14, b+20)\n\\]\n\nAfter moving point \\( B \\) vertically downwards by 4 units and horizontally to the left by 2 units, the new coordinates of \\( B \\) are:\n\\[\nB' = (c-2, d-4)\n\\]\n\nThe new midpoint \\( M' \\) between points \\( A' \\) and \\( B' \\) is:\n\\[\nM' = \\left( \\frac{(a+14) + (c-2)}{2}, \\frac{(b+20) + (d-4)}{2} \\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the coordinates of \\( M' \\):\n\\[\nM' = \\left( \\frac{a+c+12}{2}, \\frac{b+d+16}{2} \\right)\n\\]\n\nNow, we calculate the distance between \\( M \\) and \\( M' \\):\n\\[\n\\text{Distance} = \\sqrt{\\left( \\frac{a+c+12}{2} - \\frac{a+c}{2} \\right)^2 + \\left( \\frac{b+d+16}{2} - \\frac{b+d}{2} \\right)^2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expressions inside the square root:\n\\[\n\\frac{a+c+12}{2} - \\frac{a+c}{2} = \\frac{12}{2} = 6\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{b+d+16}{2} - \\frac{b+d}{2} = \\frac{16}{2} = 8\n\\]\n\nThus, the distance is:\n\\[\n\\text{Distance} = \\sqrt{6^2 + 8^2} = \\sqrt{36 + 64} = \\sqrt{100} = 10\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the distance between \\( M \\) and \\( M' \\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\)."
'To find out how many criminals Wonder Woman can capture in \\(4\\frac{1}{2}\\) hours, we first convert the mixed number to an improper fraction:\n\n\\[ 4\\frac{1}{2} = 4 + \\frac{1}{2} = \\frac{8}{2} + \\frac{1}{2} = \\frac{9}{2} \\]\n\nWonder Woman captures 6 criminals in 1 hour. Therefore, in \\(\\frac{9}{2}\\) hours, she can capture:\n\n\\[ 6 \\times \\frac{9}{2} = \\frac{54}{2} = 27 \\]\n\nThus, Wonder Woman can capture \\(\\boxed{27}\\) criminals in \\(4\\frac{1}{2}\\) hours.'
'To find the value of \\(3 \\ast 10\\) using the operation defined by \\(a \\ast b = 2a + 5b - ab\\), we substitute \\(a = 3\\) and \\(b = 10\\) into the expression:\n\n\\[\n3 \\ast 10 = 2(3) + 5(10) - (3)(10)\n\\]\n\nCalculating each term separately:\n\n- \\(2(3) = 6\\)\n- \\(5(10) = 50\\)\n- \\(3(10) = 30\\)\n\nSubstituting these values back into the expression, we have:\n\n\\[\n3 \\ast 10 = 6 + 50 - 30\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expression:\n\n\\[\n3 \\ast 10 = 56 - 30 = 26\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(3 \\ast 10\\) is \\(\\boxed{26}\\).'
'To determine the degree of the polynomial \\( f(x) \\), we need to analyze the given equation:\n\n\\[\n(x-1) \\cdot f(x) = 3x^4 + x^3 - 25x^2 + 38x - 17.\n\\]\n\nThe left-hand side of the equation is the product of \\( (x-1) \\) and \\( f(x) \\). The degree of a product of polynomials is the sum of the degrees of the factors. Therefore, if the degree of \\( f(x) \\) is \\( n \\), then the degree of \\( (x-1) \\cdot f(x) \\) is \\( n + 1 \\).\n\nThe right-hand side of the equation is a polynomial of degree 4, as the highest power of \\( x \\) is \\( x^4 \\).\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\nn + 1 = 4.\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( n \\), we find:\n\n\\[\nn = 4 - 1 = 3.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the degree of \\( f(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{3}\\).'
'To find \\(2x^2 + 2y^2\\), we start by using the given equations:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 3\n\\]\n\\[\nx - y = 4\n\\]\n\nWe can solve these equations simultaneously to find the values of \\(x\\) and \\(y\\). Adding the two equations, we have:\n\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 3 + 4\n\\]\n\\[\n2x = 7\n\\]\n\\[\nx = \\frac{7}{2}\n\\]\n\nNext, we substitute \\(x = \\frac{7}{2}\\) back into the equation \\(x + y = 3\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{7}{2} + y = 3\n\\]\n\\[\ny = 3 - \\frac{7}{2}\n\\]\n\\[\ny = \\frac{6}{2} - \\frac{7}{2}\n\\]\n\\[\ny = -\\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\(x = \\frac{7}{2}\\) and \\(y = -\\frac{1}{2}\\), we can calculate \\(2x^2 + 2y^2\\):\n\n\\[\n2x^2 + 2y^2 = 2\\left(\\left(\\frac{7}{2}\\right)^2\\right) + 2\\left(\\left(-\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2\\right)\n\\]\n\nCalculating each term separately:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{7}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{49}{4}\n\\]\n\\[\n\\left(-\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{1}{4}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting these into the expression:\n\n\\[\n2x^2 + 2y^2 = 2 \\times \\frac{49}{4} + 2 \\times \\frac{1}{4}\n\\]\n\\[\n= \\frac{98}{4} + \\frac{2}{4}\n\\]\n\\[\n= \\frac{100}{4}\n\\]\n\\[\n= 25\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(2x^2 + 2y^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{25}\\).'
'To find \\(\\text{D}(2,4,6)\\), we use the given formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{D}(a,b,c) = \\frac{abc}{a+b+c}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(a = 2\\), \\(b = 4\\), and \\(c = 6\\) into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\text{D}(2,4,6) = \\frac{2 \\cdot 4 \\cdot 6}{2 + 4 + 6}\n\\]\n\nFirst, calculate the product in the numerator:\n\n\\[\n2 \\cdot 4 \\cdot 6 = 48\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate the sum in the denominator:\n\n\\[\n2 + 4 + 6 = 12\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these values back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\text{D}(2,4,6) = \\frac{48}{12}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{48}{12} = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\text{D}(2,4,6)\\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To solve for \\( b \\) in the equation \\( 5^b + 5^b + 5^b + 5^b + 5^b = 625^{(b-1)} \\), we start by simplifying the left side of the equation. Notice that there are five terms of \\( 5^b \\), so we can factor this as:\n\n\\[\n5 \\times 5^b = 5^{b+1}\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n5^{b+1} = 625^{(b-1)}\n\\]\n\nNext, we express 625 as a power of 5. We know that:\n\n\\[\n625 = 5^4\n\\]\n\nTherefore, we can rewrite the right side of the equation as:\n\n\\[\n625^{(b-1)} = (5^4)^{(b-1)} = 5^{4(b-1)}\n\\]\n\nNow, the equation is:\n\n\\[\n5^{b+1} = 5^{4(b-1)}\n\\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we can equate the exponents:\n\n\\[\nb+1 = 4(b-1)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side gives:\n\n\\[\nb+1 = 4b - 4\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( b \\), we first move all terms involving \\( b \\) to one side:\n\n\\[\nb - 4b = -4 - 1\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n-3b = -5\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by \\(-3\\) gives:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{5}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( b \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{5}{3}}\\).'
'To find the common difference of the arithmetic series, we can use the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series:\n\n\\[\nS_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\left(2a + (n-1)d\\right)\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( S_n \\) is the sum of the series, \\( n \\) is the number of terms, \\( a \\) is the first term, and \\( d \\) is the common difference. We are given:\n\n- \\( S_n = -210 \\)\n- \\( n = 15 \\)\n- \\( a = 7 \\)\n\nSubstituting these values into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n-210 = \\frac{15}{2} \\left(2 \\cdot 7 + (15-1)d\\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n-210 = \\frac{15}{2} \\left(14 + 14d\\right)\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-210 = \\frac{15}{2} \\cdot (14 + 14d)\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-210 = \\frac{15}{2} \\cdot 14 + \\frac{15}{2} \\cdot 14d\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-210 = 105 + 105d\n\\]\n\nSubtract 105 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n-315 = 105d\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 105:\n\n\\[\nd = \\frac{-315}{105} = -3\n\\]\n\nThus, the common difference is \\(\\boxed{-3}\\).'
'To find the value of the expression \\(2x^2 + 3x + 4\\) given \\(x = -2\\), we substitute \\(-2\\) for \\(x\\) in the expression:\n\n\\[\n2(-2)^2 + 3(-2) + 4\n\\]\n\nFirst, calculate \\((-2)^2\\):\n\n\\[\n(-2)^2 = 4\n\\]\n\nNext, substitute this value back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n2 \\times 4 + 3(-2) + 4\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\(2 \\times 4\\):\n\n\\[\n2 \\times 4 = 8\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\(3 \\times (-2)\\):\n\n\\[\n3 \\times (-2) = -6\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these values back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n8 - 6 + 4\n\\]\n\nFinally, perform the addition and subtraction:\n\n\\[\n8 - 6 = 2\n\\]\n\\[\n2 + 4 = 6\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
'To find the sum of all the odd integers between 500 and 700, we first identify the smallest and largest odd integers in this range.\n\nThe smallest odd integer greater than 500 is 501, and the largest odd integer less than 700 is 699.\n\nThe sequence of odd integers from 501 to 699 is an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\( a = 501 \\), the last term \\( l = 699 \\), and the common difference \\( d = 2 \\).\n\nTo find the number of terms \\( n \\) in this sequence, we use the formula for the \\( n \\)-th term of an arithmetic sequence:\n\n\\[\nl = a + (n-1) \\cdot d\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[\n699 = 501 + (n-1) \\cdot 2\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( n \\):\n\n\\[\n699 = 501 + 2n - 2\n\\]\n\\[\n699 = 499 + 2n\n\\]\n\\[\n200 = 2n\n\\]\n\\[\nn = 100\n\\]\n\nThere are 100 terms in this sequence. The sum \\( S_n \\) of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\n\\[\nS_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\cdot (a + l)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[\nS_{100} = \\frac{100}{2} \\cdot (501 + 699)\n\\]\n\\[\nS_{100} = 50 \\cdot 1200\n\\]\n\\[\nS_{100} = 60000\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of all the odd integers between 500 and 700 is \\(\\boxed{60000}\\).'
"Let the two prime numbers be \\( p \\) and \\( q \\). Since they are roots of the quadratic equation \\( x^2 - 12x + k = 0 \\), by Vieta's formulas, we have:\n\n1. \\( p + q = 12 \\)\n2. \\( pq = k \\)\n\nWe need to find two prime numbers whose sum is 12. The possible pairs of prime numbers are:\n\n- \\( (5, 7) \\)\n\nChecking the sum:\n\n- \\( 5 + 7 = 12 \\)\n\nThis pair satisfies the condition. Now, we calculate \\( k \\):\n\n\\[\nk = pq = 5 \\times 7 = 35\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( k \\) is \\(\\boxed{35}\\)."
'To determine the value of \\( c \\) such that the quadratic \\( x^2 + cx + 9c \\) is the square of a binomial, we need to express it in the form \\( (x + a)^2 \\).\n\nExpanding \\( (x + a)^2 \\) gives:\n\\[\n(x + a)^2 = x^2 + 2ax + a^2\n\\]\n\nComparing this with \\( x^2 + cx + 9c \\), we equate the coefficients:\n1. The coefficient of \\( x \\) gives \\( 2a = c \\).\n2. The constant term gives \\( a^2 = 9c \\).\n\nFrom the first equation, we have \\( a = \\frac{c}{2} \\).\n\nSubstitute \\( a = \\frac{c}{2} \\) into the second equation:\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{c}{2}\\right)^2 = 9c\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{c^2}{4} = 9c\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 4 to clear the fraction:\n\\[\nc^2 = 36c\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation:\n\\[\nc^2 - 36c = 0\n\\]\n\nFactor out \\( c \\):\n\\[\nc(c - 36) = 0\n\\]\n\nThis gives two solutions:\n1. \\( c = 0 \\)\n2. \\( c = 36 \\)\n\nSince \\( c \\) is a nonzero constant, we discard \\( c = 0 \\) and are left with \\( c = 36 \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( c \\) is \\(\\boxed{36}\\).'
'To determine the fair representation of the two grades on the Student Council, we need to allocate the 18 representatives in proportion to the enrollments of the 7th and 8th grades.\n\nFirst, calculate the total enrollment of both grades:\n\n\\[\n520 + 650 = 1170\n\\]\n\nNext, find the proportion of the total enrollment that the 8th grade represents:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{650}{1170}\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate the number of representatives the 8th grade should have by multiplying this proportion by the total number of representatives:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{650}{1170} \\times 18\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{650}{1170} = \\frac{65}{117}\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{65}{117} \\times 18 = \\frac{65 \\times 18}{117} = \\frac{1170}{117} = 10\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the 8th grade should have \\(\\boxed{10}\\) representatives for fair representation.'
'Let \\( d \\) be the number of dimes and \\( n \\) be the number of nickels. We have two equations based on the problem statement:\n\n1. The total number of coins is 11:\n   \\[\n   d + n = 11\n   \\]\n\n2. The total value of the coins is 75 cents. Since dimes are worth 10 cents and nickels are worth 5 cents, we have:\n   \\[\n   10d + 5n = 75\n   \\]\n\nWe can simplify the second equation by dividing every term by 5:\n   \\[\n   2d + n = 15\n   \\]\n\nNow, we have the system of equations:\n\\[\n\\begin{align*}\nd + n &= 11 \\\\\n2d + n &= 15\n\\end{align*}\n\\]\n\nSubtract the first equation from the second equation to eliminate \\( n \\):\n\\[\n(2d + n) - (d + n) = 15 - 11\n\\]\n\\[\n2d + n - d - n = 4\n\\]\n\\[\nd = 4\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( d = 4 \\) back into the first equation:\n\\[\n4 + n = 11\n\\]\n\\[\nn = 7\n\\]\n\nTherefore, Hillary has \\(\\boxed{7}\\) nickels.'
'To find the value of \\( K \\), we first need to determine the slope of the line parallel to \\( 3x - 7y = 65 \\). The given line can be rewritten in slope-intercept form \\( y = mx + b \\).\n\nStarting with the equation:\n\\[ 3x - 7y = 65 \\]\n\nRearrange to solve for \\( y \\):\n\\[ -7y = -3x + 65 \\]\n\\[ y = \\frac{3}{7}x - \\frac{65}{7} \\]\n\nThe slope \\( m \\) of this line is \\( \\frac{3}{7} \\). Since parallel lines have the same slope, the line we are looking for also has a slope of \\( \\frac{3}{7} \\).\n\nNow, we use the point-slope form of a line to find the equation of the line passing through the point \\( (7, 4) \\) with slope \\( \\frac{3}{7} \\):\n\\[ y - y_1 = m(x - x_1) \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( m = \\frac{3}{7} \\), \\( x_1 = 7 \\), and \\( y_1 = 4 \\):\n\\[ y - 4 = \\frac{3}{7}(x - 7) \\]\n\nSimplify:\n\\[ y - 4 = \\frac{3}{7}x - 3 \\]\n\\[ y = \\frac{3}{7}x + 1 \\]\n\nThis is the equation of the line parallel to the given line and passing through \\( (7, 4) \\).\n\nTo find the y-intercept \\( K \\), substitute \\( x = 0 \\) into the equation:\n\\[ y = \\frac{3}{7}(0) + 1 \\]\n\\[ y = 1 \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( K \\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'To find the values of \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(m\\) for the line given by the equation \\(\\frac{x}{4} + \\frac{y}{12} = 1\\), we will first convert this equation into the slope-intercept form \\(y = mx + c\\).\n\nStarting with the given equation:\n\\[\n\\frac{x}{4} + \\frac{y}{12} = 1\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by 12 to eliminate the fractions:\n\\[\n3x + y = 12\n\\]\n\nRearrange to solve for \\(y\\):\n\\[\ny = -3x + 12\n\\]\n\nFrom this equation, we can identify the slope \\(m\\) as \\(-3\\).\n\nNext, we find the \\(x\\)-intercept \\(a\\) by setting \\(y = 0\\) in the original equation:\n\\[\n\\frac{x}{4} + \\frac{0}{12} = 1 \\implies \\frac{x}{4} = 1 \\implies x = 4\n\\]\nThus, the \\(x\\)-intercept \\(a = 4\\).\n\nNow, find the \\(y\\)-intercept \\(b\\) by setting \\(x = 0\\):\n\\[\n\\frac{0}{4} + \\frac{y}{12} = 1 \\implies \\frac{y}{12} = 1 \\implies y = 12\n\\]\nThus, the \\(y\\)-intercept \\(b = 12\\).\n\nFinally, we calculate \\(a + b + m\\):\n\\[\na + b + m = 4 + 12 - 3 = 13\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(a + b + m\\) is \\(\\boxed{13}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( c \\) for which the circle has a radius of length 1, we first need to rewrite the equation of the circle in standard form. The given equation is:\n\n\\[\nx^2 - 10x + y^2 + 6y + c = 0\n\\]\n\nWe will complete the square for both the \\( x \\) and \\( y \\) terms.\n\n**Completing the square for \\( x \\):**\n\nThe \\( x \\)-terms are \\( x^2 - 10x \\). To complete the square, we take half of the coefficient of \\( x \\), which is \\(-10\\), divide by 2 to get \\(-5\\), and then square it to get 25. Thus, we can rewrite:\n\n\\[\nx^2 - 10x = (x - 5)^2 - 25\n\\]\n\n**Completing the square for \\( y \\):**\n\nThe \\( y \\)-terms are \\( y^2 + 6y \\). To complete the square, we take half of the coefficient of \\( y \\), which is 6, divide by 2 to get 3, and then square it to get 9. Thus, we can rewrite:\n\n\\[\ny^2 + 6y = (y + 3)^2 - 9\n\\]\n\nSubstituting these completed squares back into the original equation, we have:\n\n\\[\n(x - 5)^2 - 25 + (y + 3)^2 - 9 + c = 0\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n(x - 5)^2 + (y + 3)^2 - 34 + c = 0\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\n(x - 5)^2 + (y + 3)^2 = 34 - c\n\\]\n\nThis is the standard form of a circle \\((x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2\\), where the radius \\( r \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nr^2 = 34 - c\n\\]\n\nWe want the radius to be 1, so:\n\n\\[\n1^2 = 34 - c\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( c \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n1 = 34 - c\n\\]\n\n\\[\nc = 34 - 1 = 33\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( c \\) that makes the radius of the circle 1 is \\(\\boxed{33}\\).'
'Let the weight of each of the two smaller dogs be \\( x \\) pounds. Then the weight of the largest dog is \\( x + 20 \\) pounds. The combined weight of the three dogs is given as 185 pounds. Therefore, we can set up the equation:\n\n\\[\nx + x + (x + 20) = 185\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the equation, we have:\n\n\\[\n3x + 20 = 185\n\\]\n\nSubtract 20 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n3x = 165\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 3:\n\n\\[\nx = 55\n\\]\n\nThus, the weight of the largest dog is:\n\n\\[\nx + 20 = 55 + 20 = 75\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the largest dog weighs \\(\\boxed{75}\\) pounds.'
'To find the function \\( k(x) \\) such that \\( f \\) is its own inverse, we need to ensure that \\( f(f(x)) = x \\) for all \\( x \\).\n\nGiven the piecewise function:\n\\[\nf(x) =\n\\begin{cases}\nk(x) & \\text{if } x > 2, \\\\\n2 + (x-2)^2 & \\text{if } x \\leq 2.\n\\end{cases}\n\\]\n\n### Step 1: Determine \\( f(f(x)) \\) when \\( x \\leq 2 \\)\n\nFor \\( x \\leq 2 \\), we have:\n\\[ f(x) = 2 + (x-2)^2. \\]\n\nSince \\( 2 + (x-2)^2 \\geq 2 \\), \\( f(x) \\) will be greater than or equal to 2. Therefore, we need to use the \\( k(x) \\) part of the function for \\( f(f(x)) \\).\n\nLet \\( y = f(x) = 2 + (x-2)^2 \\). Then:\n\\[ f(y) = k(y). \\]\n\nSince \\( f(f(x)) = x \\), we have:\n\\[ k(2 + (x-2)^2) = x. \\]\n\n### Step 2: Determine \\( f(f(x)) \\) when \\( x > 2 \\)\n\nFor \\( x > 2 \\), we have:\n\\[ f(x) = k(x). \\]\n\nSince \\( f \\) is its own inverse, we need:\n\\[ f(k(x)) = x. \\]\n\n### Step 3: Solve for \\( k(x) \\)\n\nFrom Step 1, we have:\n\\[ k(2 + (x-2)^2) = x. \\]\n\nTo find \\( k(x) \\), we need to express \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y = 2 + (x-2)^2 \\):\n\\[ y = 2 + (x-2)^2 \\]\n\\[ y - 2 = (x-2)^2 \\]\n\\[ x - 2 = \\pm \\sqrt{y - 2} \\]\n\\[ x = 2 \\pm \\sqrt{y - 2} \\]\n\nSince \\( x \\leq 2 \\) in this context, we choose the negative root:\n\\[ x = 2 - \\sqrt{y - 2} \\]\n\nThus, for \\( y > 2 \\), we have:\n\\[ k(y) = 2 - \\sqrt{y - 2}. \\]\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThe function \\( k(x) \\) such that \\( f \\) is its own inverse is:\n\\[ k(x) = 2 - \\sqrt{x - 2} \\]\nfor \\( x > 2 \\).\n\nTherefore, the complete function \\( f(x) \\) is:\n\\[\nf(x) =\n\\begin{cases}\n2 - \\sqrt{x - 2} & \\text{if } x > 2, \\\\\n2 + (x-2)^2 & \\text{if } x \\leq 2.\n\\end{cases}\n\\]'
'Let the two positive integers be \\( a \\) and \\( b \\). We are given that the sum of their product and their sum is 454:\n\n\\[\nab + (a + b) = 454\n\\]\n\nWe can rewrite this equation as:\n\n\\[\nab + a + b = 454\n\\]\n\nAdding 1 to both sides gives:\n\n\\[\nab + a + b + 1 = 455\n\\]\n\nThis can be factored as:\n\n\\[\n(a+1)(b+1) = 455\n\\]\n\nThe goal is to find the largest possible value of the product of their sum and their product, which is:\n\n\\[\n(a+b)(ab)\n\\]\n\nFirst, we need to find the factor pairs of 455. The prime factorization of 455 is:\n\n\\[\n455 = 5 \\times 7 \\times 13\n\\]\n\nThe factor pairs of 455 are:\n\n\\[\n(1, 455), (5, 91), (7, 65), (13, 35)\n\\]\n\nFor each factor pair \\((x, y)\\), we have:\n\n\\[\na+1 = x \\quad \\text{and} \\quad b+1 = y\n\\]\n\nor\n\n\\[\na+1 = y \\quad \\text{and} \\quad b+1 = x\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( a = x-1 \\) and \\( b = y-1 \\), or vice versa. We calculate \\( ab \\) and \\( a+b \\) for each pair:\n\n1. **Pair (1, 455):**\n   - \\( a = 0, b = 454 \\) or \\( a = 454, b = 0 \\)\n   - \\( ab = 0 \\), \\( a+b = 454 \\)\n   - Product: \\( (a+b)(ab) = 454 \\times 0 = 0 \\)\n\n2. **Pair (5, 91):**\n   - \\( a = 4, b = 90 \\) or \\( a = 90, b = 4 \\)\n   - \\( ab = 360 \\), \\( a+b = 94 \\)\n   - Product: \\( (a+b)(ab) = 94 \\times 360 = 33840 \\)\n\n3. **Pair (7, 65):**\n   - \\( a = 6, b = 64 \\) or \\( a = 64, b = 6 \\)\n   - \\( ab = 384 \\), \\( a+b = 70 \\)\n   - Product: \\( (a+b)(ab) = 70 \\times 384 = 26880 \\)\n\n4. **Pair (13, 35):**\n   - \\( a = 12, b = 34 \\) or \\( a = 34, b = 12 \\)\n   - \\( ab = 408 \\), \\( a+b = 46 \\)\n   - Product: \\( (a+b)(ab) = 46 \\times 408 = 18768 \\)\n\nThe largest product is obtained from the pair (5, 91), which gives:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{33840}\n\\]'
'To find the \\( y \\)-coordinate of the point where the line intersects the \\( y \\)-axis, we first need to determine the equation of the line passing through the points \\((-2, 6)\\) and \\((-4, -2)\\).\n\nFirst, calculate the slope \\( m \\) of the line using the formula for the slope between two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\):\n\n\\[\nm = \\frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1} = \\frac{-2 - 6}{-4 - (-2)} = \\frac{-8}{-2} = 4\n\\]\n\nNow that we have the slope \\( m = 4 \\), we can use the point-slope form of the equation of a line, which is:\n\n\\[\ny - y_1 = m(x - x_1)\n\\]\n\nUsing the point \\((-2, 6)\\), the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\ny - 6 = 4(x + 2)\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[\ny - 6 = 4x + 8\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 4x + 14\n\\]\n\nThe \\( y \\)-intercept occurs where \\( x = 0 \\). Substitute \\( x = 0 \\) into the equation to find the \\( y \\)-coordinate:\n\n\\[\ny = 4(0) + 14 = 14\n\\]\n\nThus, the \\( y \\)-coordinate of the point where the line intersects the \\( y \\)-axis is \\(\\boxed{14}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\( |x-3| + |3-x| - 1 = 3 \\), we first note that \\( |x-3| = |3-x| \\). Therefore, the equation simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n2|x-3| - 1 = 3\n\\]\n\nAdding 1 to both sides, we have:\n\n\\[\n2|x-3| = 4\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by 2, we get:\n\n\\[\n|x-3| = 2\n\\]\n\nThis absolute value equation gives us two cases to consider:\n\n1. \\( x-3 = 2 \\)\n2. \\( x-3 = -2 \\)\n\nSolving these equations:\n\n1. \\( x-3 = 2 \\) implies \\( x = 5 \\)\n2. \\( x-3 = -2 \\) implies \\( x = 1 \\)\n\nThus, the solutions for \\( x \\) are \\( x = 5 \\) and \\( x = 1 \\).\n\nThe sum of all values of \\( x \\) is:\n\n\\[\n5 + 1 = 6\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum of all values of \\( x \\) for which the equation holds is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
"To calculate the amount in Alan's bank account after 10 years with an annual compound interest rate of 3%, we use the formula for compound interest:\n\n\\[ A = P \\left(1 + \\frac{r}{n}\\right)^{nt} \\]\n\nwhere:\n- \\( A \\) is the amount of money accumulated after n years, including interest.\n- \\( P \\) is the principal amount (initial investment), which is $500.\n- \\( r \\) is the annual interest rate (decimal), which is 0.03.\n- \\( n \\) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year, which is 1 for annual compounding.\n- \\( t \\) is the time the money is invested for in years, which is 10.\n\nPlugging in the values, we get:\n\n\\[ A = 500 \\left(1 + \\frac{0.03}{1}\\right)^{1 \\times 10} \\]\n\\[ A = 500 \\left(1.03\\right)^{10} \\]\n\nNow, calculate \\( (1.03)^{10} \\):\n\n\\[ (1.03)^{10} \\approx 1.34391638 \\]\n\nNow, multiply this by the principal amount:\n\n\\[ A \\approx 500 \\times 1.34391638 \\]\n\\[ A \\approx 671.95819 \\]\n\nRounding to the nearest dollar, the amount in Alan's bank account after 10 years is approximately \\(\\boxed{672}\\) dollars."
'To solve for \\( A \\) and \\( B \\) in the given equation \\(\\frac{2}{5} = \\frac{A}{60} = \\frac{60}{B}\\), we will first find \\( A \\) and then \\( B\\).\n\n1. **Finding \\( A \\):**\n\n   We have the equation \\(\\frac{2}{5} = \\frac{A}{60}\\).\n\n   To solve for \\( A \\), we cross-multiply:\n\n   \\[\n   2 \\times 60 = 5 \\times A\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   120 = 5A\n   \\]\n\n   Divide both sides by 5:\n\n   \\[\n   A = \\frac{120}{5} = 24\n   \\]\n\n2. **Finding \\( B \\):**\n\n   We have the equation \\(\\frac{2}{5} = \\frac{60}{B}\\).\n\n   To solve for \\( B \\), we cross-multiply:\n\n   \\[\n   2B = 5 \\times 60\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   2B = 300\n   \\]\n\n   Divide both sides by 2:\n\n   \\[\n   B = \\frac{300}{2} = 150\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculating \\( A + B \\):**\n\n   Now that we have \\( A = 24 \\) and \\( B = 150 \\), we find \\( A + B \\):\n\n   \\[\n   A + B = 24 + 150 = 174\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( A + B \\) is \\(\\boxed{174}\\).'
"To determine how many different values are represented by the given quantities, we need to simplify each expression:\n\n1. \\(3^{-2}\\):\n   \\[\n   3^{-2} = \\frac{1}{3^2} = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\n2. \\(9^{-2}\\):\n   \\[\n   9^{-2} = \\left(3^2\\right)^{-2} = 3^{-4} = \\frac{1}{3^4} = \\frac{1}{81}\n   \\]\n\n3. \\(27^{-\\frac{2}{3}}\\):\n   \\[\n   27^{-\\frac{2}{3}} = \\left(3^3\\right)^{-\\frac{2}{3}} = 3^{-2} = \\frac{1}{3^2} = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\n4. \\(9 \\cdot 81^{-1}\\):\n   \\[\n   9 \\cdot 81^{-1} = 9 \\cdot \\frac{1}{81} = \\frac{9}{81} = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\n5. \\(243^{-\\frac{4}{5}}\\):\n   \\[\n   243^{-\\frac{4}{5}} = \\left(3^5\\right)^{-\\frac{4}{5}} = 3^{-4} = \\frac{1}{3^4} = \\frac{1}{81}\n   \\]\n\nNow, let's list the simplified values:\n- \\(3^{-2} = \\frac{1}{9}\\)\n- \\(9^{-2} = \\frac{1}{81}\\)\n- \\(27^{-\\frac{2}{3}} = \\frac{1}{9}\\)\n- \\(9 \\cdot 81^{-1} = \\frac{1}{9}\\)\n- \\(243^{-\\frac{4}{5}} = \\frac{1}{81}\\)\n\nThe distinct values are \\(\\frac{1}{9}\\) and \\(\\frac{1}{81}\\).\n\nThus, there are \\(\\boxed{2}\\) different values represented by the given quantities."

"Let's denote the first term of the arithmetic sequence as \\( a \\) and the common difference as \\( d \\). The terms of the sequence can be expressed as follows:\n\n- First term: \\( a \\)\n- Second term: \\( a + d \\)\n- Third term: \\( a + 2d \\)\n- Fourth term: \\( a + 3d \\)\n\nWe are given that the product of the first and third terms is 5:\n\n\\[\na(a + 2d) = 5\n\\]\n\nSince all terms are positive integers, we need to find integer solutions for \\( a \\) and \\( a + 2d \\) such that their product is 5. The possible pairs \\((a, a + 2d)\\) that satisfy this condition are:\n\n- \\( (1, 5) \\)\n- \\( (5, 1) \\)\n\nLet's consider each case:\n\n1. **Case 1: \\( a = 1 \\) and \\( a + 2d = 5 \\)**\n\n   Solving for \\( d \\):\n\n   \\[\n   1 + 2d = 5 \\implies 2d = 4 \\implies d = 2\n   \\]\n\n   The fourth term is:\n\n   \\[\n   a + 3d = 1 + 3 \\times 2 = 1 + 6 = 7\n   \\]\n\n2. **Case 2: \\( a = 5 \\) and \\( a + 2d = 1 \\)**\n\n   Solving for \\( d \\):\n\n   \\[\n   5 + 2d = 1 \\implies 2d = -4 \\implies d = -2\n   \\]\n\n   The fourth term is:\n\n   \\[\n   a + 3d = 5 + 3 \\times (-2) = 5 - 6 = -1\n   \\]\n\n   However, this is not a positive integer, so this case is not valid.\n\nThus, the only valid solution is from Case 1, where the fourth term is \\(\\boxed{7}\\)."
'To find the height of the plant two weeks ago, we need to determine its height 14 days ago, given that it grows by 5% each day. Let \\( h \\) be the height of the plant 14 days ago. The height of the plant today is 452 cm, and it grows by 5% each day, which means it multiplies by 1.05 each day.\n\nThe relationship between the height 14 days ago and today is given by:\n\n\\[\nh \\times (1.05)^{14} = 452\n\\]\n\nTo find \\( h \\), we solve for it by dividing both sides by \\( (1.05)^{14} \\):\n\n\\[\nh = \\frac{452}{(1.05)^{14}}\n\\]\n\nNow, we calculate \\( (1.05)^{14} \\):\n\n\\[\n(1.05)^{14} \\approx 1.979\n\\]\n\nUsing this approximation, we find \\( h \\):\n\n\\[\nh \\approx \\frac{452}{1.979} \\approx 228.4\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the height of the plant two weeks ago was approximately \\( \\boxed{228.4} \\) centimeters.'
'To find the value of \\( x \\) that gives the minimum value for the quadratic expression \\( 9x^2 + 18x + 7 \\), we can use the formula for the vertex of a parabola. The expression is in the form \\( ax^2 + bx + c \\), where \\( a = 9 \\), \\( b = 18 \\), and \\( c = 7 \\).\n\nThe \\( x \\)-coordinate of the vertex, which gives the minimum value for a parabola that opens upwards (since \\( a > 0 \\)), is given by:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{b}{2a}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values of \\( a \\) and \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{18}{2 \\times 9} = -\\frac{18}{18} = -1\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( x \\) that gives the minimum value for the expression \\( 9x^2 + 18x + 7 \\) is \\( \\boxed{-1} \\).'
"Let the two-digit integer be represented as \\(10a + b\\), where \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) are the digits of the integer, and \\(a\\) is the tens digit while \\(b\\) is the units digit. We are given that the product of the digits is one-half of the integer:\n\n\\[\nab = \\frac{1}{2}(10a + b)\n\\]\n\nMultiplying both sides by 2 to eliminate the fraction, we have:\n\n\\[\n2ab = 10a + b\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms, we get:\n\n\\[\n2ab - b = 10a\n\\]\n\nFactoring out \\(b\\) from the left side, we have:\n\n\\[\nb(2a - 1) = 10a\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(b\\), we get:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{10a}{2a - 1}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(b\\) is a digit, it must be an integer between 0 and 9. We need to find the smallest integer \\(a\\) such that \\(\\frac{10a}{2a - 1}\\) is an integer.\n\nLet's test values of \\(a\\) starting from the smallest possible value for a two-digit number, which is 1:\n\n- For \\(a = 1\\):\n  \\[\n  b = \\frac{10 \\times 1}{2 \\times 1 - 1} = \\frac{10}{1} = 10 \\quad (\\text{not a valid digit})\n  \\]\n\n- For \\(a = 2\\):\n  \\[\n  b = \\frac{10 \\times 2}{2 \\times 2 - 1} = \\frac{20}{3} \\quad (\\text{not an integer})\n  \\]\n\n- For \\(a = 3\\):\n  \\[\n  b = \\frac{10 \\times 3}{2 \\times 3 - 1} = \\frac{30}{5} = 6 \\quad (\\text{valid digit})\n  \\]\n\nThus, when \\(a = 3\\), \\(b = 6\\), and the integer is \\(10a + b = 10 \\times 3 + 6 = 36\\).\n\nLet's verify:\n\nThe product of the digits is \\(3 \\times 6 = 18\\), and one-half of the integer is \\(\\frac{36}{2} = 18\\).\n\nTherefore, the smallest two-digit positive integer such that the product of its two digits is one-half the integer is \\(\\boxed{36}\\)."
'To find the point of intersection \\( A \\) of the lines \\( 3y = x \\) and \\( 2x + 5y = 11 \\), we first express the equations in terms of \\( y \\).\n\nThe first equation is:\n\\[\n3y = x \\implies y = \\frac{x}{3}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( y = \\frac{x}{3} \\) into the second equation:\n\\[\n2x + 5\\left(\\frac{x}{3}\\right) = 11\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( x \\):\n\\[\n2x + \\frac{5x}{3} = 11\n\\]\n\nTo eliminate the fraction, multiply the entire equation by 3:\n\\[\n3(2x) + 3\\left(\\frac{5x}{3}\\right) = 3 \\times 11\n\\]\n\\[\n6x + 5x = 33\n\\]\n\\[\n11x = 33\n\\]\n\\[\nx = 3\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\( x = 3 \\) back into the equation \\( y = \\frac{x}{3} \\) to find \\( y \\):\n\\[\ny = \\frac{3}{3} = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the coordinates of point \\( A \\) are \\( (3, 1) \\).\n\nThe sum of the coordinates of point \\( A \\) is:\n\\[\n3 + 1 = 4\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum of the coordinates of point \\( A \\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
"To solve the given problem, we need to simplify the expression \\(\\frac{x^{r-2}\\cdot y^{2s}\\cdot z^{3t+1}}{x^{2r}\\cdot y^{s-4}\\cdot z^{2t-3}}\\) and set it equal to \\(xyz\\).\n\nFirst, let's simplify the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^{r-2}\\cdot y^{2s}\\cdot z^{3t+1}}{x^{2r}\\cdot y^{s-4}\\cdot z^{2t-3}} = x^{(r-2) - 2r} \\cdot y^{2s - (s-4)} \\cdot z^{(3t+1) - (2t-3)}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying each exponent:\n\n- For \\(x\\): \\((r-2) - 2r = r - 2 - 2r = -r - 2\\)\n- For \\(y\\): \\(2s - (s-4) = 2s - s + 4 = s + 4\\)\n- For \\(z\\): \\((3t+1) - (2t-3) = 3t + 1 - 2t + 3 = t + 4\\)\n\nThus, the expression simplifies to:\n\n\\[\nx^{-r-2} \\cdot y^{s+4} \\cdot z^{t+4}\n\\]\n\nWe are given that this equals \\(xyz\\), which can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\nx^1 \\cdot y^1 \\cdot z^1\n\\]\n\nEquating the exponents of corresponding variables, we have:\n\n1. For \\(x\\): \\(-r - 2 = 1\\)\n2. For \\(y\\): \\(s + 4 = 1\\)\n3. For \\(z\\): \\(t + 4 = 1\\)\n\nSolving these equations:\n\n1. \\(-r - 2 = 1 \\implies -r = 3 \\implies r = -3\\)\n2. \\(s + 4 = 1 \\implies s = -3\\)\n3. \\(t + 4 = 1 \\implies t = -3\\)\n\nNow, we need to find \\(r^s \\cdot t\\):\n\n\\[\nr^s \\cdot t = (-3)^{-3} \\cdot (-3)\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\((-3)^{-3}\\):\n\n\\[\n(-3)^{-3} = \\frac{1}{(-3)^3} = \\frac{1}{-27} = -\\frac{1}{27}\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\nr^s \\cdot t = -\\frac{1}{27} \\cdot (-3) = \\frac{3}{27} = \\frac{1}{9}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{9}}\\)."
'To solve for \\( x \\) in the equation \\((2^{x+1})^3 \\cdot 4^x = 8192\\), we start by simplifying the expression.\n\nFirst, note that \\( 4^x = (2^2)^x = 2^{2x} \\). Therefore, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n(2^{x+1})^3 \\cdot 2^{2x} = 8192\n\\]\n\nSimplify \\((2^{x+1})^3\\):\n\n\\[\n(2^{x+1})^3 = 2^{3(x+1)} = 2^{3x+3}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back into the equation:\n\n\\[\n2^{3x+3} \\cdot 2^{2x} = 8192\n\\]\n\nCombine the exponents on the left side:\n\n\\[\n2^{3x+3 + 2x} = 8192\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n2^{5x+3} = 8192\n\\]\n\nNext, express 8192 as a power of 2. We find that:\n\n\\[\n8192 = 2^{13}\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n2^{5x+3} = 2^{13}\n\\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we equate the exponents:\n\n\\[\n5x + 3 = 13\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\n5x = 13 - 3\n\\]\n\\[\n5x = 10\n\\]\n\\[\nx = \\frac{10}{5}\n\\]\n\\[\nx = 2\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the solution is \\( x = \\boxed{2} \\).'
"To solve the given expression, we first need to simplify it. The expression is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^1 \\cdot x^2 \\cdot x^3 \\cdots x^9}{x^2 \\cdot x^4 \\cdot x^6 \\cdots x^{12}}\n\\]\n\nFirst, let's determine the exponents in the numerator and the denominator.\n\n**Numerator:**\n\nThe numerator is the product of powers of \\(x\\) from \\(x^1\\) to \\(x^9\\). The sum of the exponents in the numerator is:\n\n\\[\n1 + 2 + 3 + \\cdots + 9\n\\]\n\nThis is an arithmetic series with the first term \\(a = 1\\), the last term \\(l = 9\\), and the number of terms \\(n = 9\\). The sum of an arithmetic series is given by:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (a + l) = \\frac{9}{2} \\times (1 + 9) = \\frac{9}{2} \\times 10 = 45\n\\]\n\nSo, the exponent of \\(x\\) in the numerator is 45.\n\n**Denominator:**\n\nThe denominator is the product of powers of \\(x\\) from \\(x^2\\) to \\(x^{12}\\) with a step of 2. The sum of the exponents in the denominator is:\n\n\\[\n2 + 4 + 6 + 8 + 10 + 12\n\\]\n\nThis is also an arithmetic series with the first term \\(a = 2\\), the last term \\(l = 12\\), and the number of terms \\(n = 6\\). The sum of this series is:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (a + l) = \\frac{6}{2} \\times (2 + 12) = 3 \\times 14 = 42\n\\]\n\nSo, the exponent of \\(x\\) in the denominator is 42.\n\n**Simplifying the Expression:**\n\nNow, we simplify the original expression by subtracting the exponents:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^{45}}{x^{42}} = x^{45 - 42} = x^3\n\\]\n\nGiven that \\(x = 5\\), we substitute to find the value:\n\n\\[\nx^3 = 5^3 = 125\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{125}\\)."
'To solve this problem, we need to find the coordinates of the point \\((x, y)\\) that satisfy the given conditions and then determine the distance from the origin.\n\n1. **Distance from the \\(x\\)-axis:**\n   Since the point is 6 units from the \\(x\\)-axis and both coordinates are negative, the \\(y\\)-coordinate must be \\(-6\\). Thus, \\(y = -6\\).\n\n2. **Distance from the point \\((8, 3)\\):**\n   The distance formula gives us:\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{(x - 8)^2 + (y - 3)^2} = 15\n   \\]\n   Substituting \\(y = -6\\) into the equation:\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{(x - 8)^2 + (-6 - 3)^2} = 15\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{(x - 8)^2 + 81} = 15\n   \\]\n   Squaring both sides:\n   \\[\n   (x - 8)^2 + 81 = 225\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   (x - 8)^2 = 144\n   \\]\n   Solving for \\(x\\):\n   \\[\n   x - 8 = \\pm 12\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = 20 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad x = -4\n   \\]\n   Since \\(x\\) must be negative, we have \\(x = -4\\).\n\n3. **Distance from the origin:**\n   The distance from the origin \\((0, 0)\\) to the point \\((-4, -6)\\) is:\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{(-4)^2 + (-6)^2} = \\sqrt{16 + 36} = \\sqrt{52}\n   \\]\n\nThus, \\(n = 52\\). Therefore, the value of \\(n\\) is \\(\\boxed{52}\\).'
'To solve for \\( a + b \\), we start with the given equations:\n\n1. \\( a^2b^3 = \\frac{32}{27} \\)\n2. \\( \\frac{a}{b^3} = \\frac{27}{4} \\)\n\nFrom the second equation, we can express \\( a \\) in terms of \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{27}{4}b^3\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( a \\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{27}{4}b^3\\right)^2 b^3 = \\frac{32}{27}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the left side:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{729}{16}b^6 \\cdot b^3 = \\frac{32}{27}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{729}{16}b^9 = \\frac{32}{27}\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( b^9 \\), multiply both sides by \\(\\frac{16}{729}\\):\n\n\\[\nb^9 = \\frac{32}{27} \\cdot \\frac{16}{729}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the right side:\n\n\\[\nb^9 = \\frac{32 \\times 16}{27 \\times 729} = \\frac{512}{19683}\n\\]\n\nRecognize that \\( 512 = 2^9 \\) and \\( 19683 = 3^9 \\), so:\n\n\\[\nb^9 = \\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right)^9\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( b = \\frac{2}{3} \\).\n\nSubstitute \\( b = \\frac{2}{3} \\) back into the expression for \\( a \\):\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{27}{4} \\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right)^3\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( \\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right)^3 \\):\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right)^3 = \\frac{8}{27}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back:\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{27}{4} \\cdot \\frac{8}{27} = \\frac{8}{4} = 2\n\\]\n\nNow, find \\( a + b \\):\n\n\\[\na + b = 2 + \\frac{2}{3} = \\frac{6}{3} + \\frac{2}{3} = \\frac{8}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( a + b \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{8}{3}}\\).'
'To find the perimeter of the square, we first need to determine the length of one side of the square. The points \\((1, -2)\\) and \\((-4, 10)\\) are adjacent vertices of the square, so the distance between these two points is the length of one side of the square.\n\nThe distance \\(d\\) between two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is given by the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given points \\((1, -2)\\) and \\((-4, 10)\\) into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{((-4) - 1)^2 + (10 - (-2))^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(-5)^2 + (12)^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{25 + 144}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{169}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = 13\n\\]\n\nSince the distance between the two adjacent vertices is 13, this is the length of one side of the square. The perimeter \\(P\\) of a square is given by four times the length of one side:\n\n\\[\nP = 4 \\times 13 = 52\n\\]\n\nThus, the perimeter of the square is \\(\\boxed{52}\\).'
'Let the vertices of the triangle be \\( A(x_1, y_1) \\), \\( B(x_2, y_2) \\), and \\( C(x_3, y_3) \\). The sum of the \\( x \\)-coordinates of the vertices is given by:\n\n\\[\nx_1 + x_2 + x_3 = \\sqrt{13}\n\\]\n\nThe midpoints of the sides of the triangle are:\n\n- Midpoint of \\( AB \\): \\( \\left( \\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2} \\right) \\)\n- Midpoint of \\( BC \\): \\( \\left( \\frac{x_2 + x_3}{2}, \\frac{y_2 + y_3}{2} \\right) \\)\n- Midpoint of \\( CA \\): \\( \\left( \\frac{x_3 + x_1}{2}, \\frac{y_3 + y_1}{2} \\right) \\)\n\nThe sum of the \\( x \\)-coordinates of these midpoints is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2} + \\frac{x_2 + x_3}{2} + \\frac{x_3 + x_1}{2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying this expression, we have:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{x_1 + x_2 + x_2 + x_3 + x_3 + x_1}{2}\n= \\frac{2x_1 + 2x_2 + 2x_3}{2}\n= x_1 + x_2 + x_3\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x_1 + x_2 + x_3 = \\sqrt{13} \\), the sum of the \\( x \\)-coordinates of the midpoints is also \\( \\sqrt{13} \\).\n\nThus, \\( S = \\sqrt{13} \\).\n\nFinally, we need to find \\( S^2 \\):\n\n\\[\nS^2 = (\\sqrt{13})^2 = 13\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( S^2 \\) is \\(\\boxed{13}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( C \\), we start by setting up equations based on the given information.\n\n1. The arithmetic mean of \\( A \\), \\( B \\), and \\( C \\) is 10:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{A + B + C}{3} = 10\n   \\]\n   Multiplying both sides by 3 gives:\n   \\[\n   A + B + C = 30\n   \\]\n\n2. The value of \\( A \\) is six less than the value of \\( B \\):\n   \\[\n   A = B - 6\n   \\]\n\n3. The value of \\( C \\) is three more than the value of \\( B \\):\n   \\[\n   C = B + 3\n   \\]\n\nSubstitute the expressions for \\( A \\) and \\( C \\) from equations 2 and 3 into equation 1:\n\\[\n(B - 6) + B + (B + 3) = 30\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( B \\):\n\\[\nB - 6 + B + B + 3 = 30\n\\]\n\\[\n3B - 3 = 30\n\\]\n\\[\n3B = 33\n\\]\n\\[\nB = 11\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( B = 11 \\) back into the expression for \\( C \\):\n\\[\nC = B + 3 = 11 + 3 = 14\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( C \\) is \\(\\boxed{14}\\).'
"To find the \\(x\\)-intercepts of the lines, we set \\(y = 0\\) in each equation and solve for \\(x\\).\n\nFor the line \\(y = \\frac{1}{3}x + 7\\):\n\n\\[\n0 = \\frac{1}{3}x + 7\n\\]\n\nSubtract 7 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{1}{3}x = -7\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by \\(-3\\) to solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nx = 21\n\\]\n\nSo, the \\(x\\)-intercept of the first line is \\(x = 21\\).\n\nFor the line \\(y = 2x + 5\\):\n\n\\[\n0 = 2x + 5\n\\]\n\nSubtract 5 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2x = -5\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 2:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{5}{2} = -2.5\n\\]\n\nSo, the \\(x\\)-intercept of the second line is \\(x = -2.5\\).\n\nThe sum of the \\(x\\)-coordinates of the two lines' \\(x\\)-intercepts is:\n\n\\[\n21 + (-2.5) = 21 - 2.5 = 18.5\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of the \\(x\\)-coordinates of the \\(x\\)-intercepts is \\(\\boxed{18.5}\\)."
'To determine how many sticks of butter Walter and Gretel need, we first calculate the number of pans of cookies required to make 216 cookies. Each pan makes 15 cookies, so the number of pans needed is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{216}{15} = 14.4\n\\]\n\nSince they can only make full recipes, they need to make 15 pans of cookies (rounding up from 14.4).\n\nNext, we calculate the total amount of butter needed for 15 pans. The recipe requires 3 tablespoons of butter per pan, so for 15 pans, they need:\n\n\\[\n15 \\times 3 = 45 \\text{ tablespoons of butter}\n\\]\n\nThere are 8 tablespoons in a stick of butter, so the number of sticks needed is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{45}{8} = 5.625\n\\]\n\nSince they can only use whole sticks of butter, they will need to use 6 sticks of butter. Therefore, the number of sticks of butter needed is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
'To find the positive difference between \\(120\\%\\) of 30 and \\(130\\%\\) of 20, we first calculate each percentage.\n\nFirst, calculate \\(120\\%\\) of 30:\n\\[\n120\\% \\text{ of } 30 = \\frac{120}{100} \\times 30 = 1.2 \\times 30 = 36\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate \\(130\\%\\) of 20:\n\\[\n130\\% \\text{ of } 20 = \\frac{130}{100} \\times 20 = 1.3 \\times 20 = 26\n\\]\n\nNow, find the positive difference between these two results:\n\\[\n|36 - 26| = 10\n\\]\n\nThus, the positive difference is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
'To solve the problem, we need to evaluate the expression \\(3 \\ast (6 \\ast 8)\\) using the operation defined as \\(P \\ast Q = \\frac{P+Q}{2}\\).\n\nFirst, we calculate \\(6 \\ast 8\\):\n\n\\[\n6 \\ast 8 = \\frac{6 + 8}{2} = \\frac{14}{2} = 7\n\\]\n\nNext, we use the result from the first calculation to find \\(3 \\ast 7\\):\n\n\\[\n3 \\ast 7 = \\frac{3 + 7}{2} = \\frac{10}{2} = 5\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(3 \\ast (6 \\ast 8)\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to find the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) of the function \\( f(x) = ax + b \\), and then use the given relationship \\( g(x) = 2f^{-1}(x) \\).\n\nFirst, let's find the inverse of \\( f(x) = ax + b \\). To find \\( f^{-1}(x) \\), we set \\( y = ax + b \\) and solve for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\ny = ax + b \\implies ax = y - b \\implies x = \\frac{y - b}{a}\n\\]\n\nThus, the inverse function is:\n\n\\[\nf^{-1}(x) = \\frac{x - b}{a}\n\\]\n\nAccording to the problem, \\( g(x) = 2f^{-1}(x) \\). Substituting the expression for \\( f^{-1}(x) \\), we have:\n\n\\[\ng(x) = 2 \\left( \\frac{x - b}{a} \\right) = \\frac{2(x - b)}{a}\n\\]\n\nWe are also given that \\( g(x) = 3x + 2 \\). Therefore, we equate the two expressions for \\( g(x) \\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2(x - b)}{a} = 3x + 2\n\\]\n\nTo eliminate the fraction, multiply both sides by \\( a \\):\n\n\\[\n2(x - b) = a(3x + 2)\n\\]\n\nExpanding both sides, we get:\n\n\\[\n2x - 2b = 3ax + 2a\n\\]\n\nRearrange the terms to isolate the terms involving \\( x \\) on one side:\n\n\\[\n2x - 3ax = 2a + 2b\n\\]\n\nFactor out \\( x \\) on the left side:\n\n\\[\nx(2 - 3a) = 2a + 2b\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( x \\), divide both sides by \\( 2 - 3a \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{2a + 2b}{2 - 3a}\n\\]\n\nSince this equation must hold for all \\( x \\), the coefficients of \\( x \\) must be equal on both sides. Therefore, the coefficient of \\( x \\) on the left side must be zero:\n\n\\[\n2 - 3a = 0 \\implies 3a = 2 \\implies a = \\frac{2}{3}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( a = \\frac{2}{3} \\) back into the equation for the constant terms:\n\n\\[\n2a + 2b = 0 \\implies 2\\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right) + 2b = 0 \\implies \\frac{4}{3} + 2b = 0\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\n2b = -\\frac{4}{3} \\implies b = -\\frac{2}{3}\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\( \\frac{a+b}{2} \\):\n\n\\[\na + b = \\frac{2}{3} - \\frac{2}{3} = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, \n\n\\[\n\\frac{a+b}{2} = \\frac{0}{2} = 0\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{0}\\)."
"To find the sum of \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\), we start with the given equations:\n\n\\[\na^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 13\n\\]\n\n\\[\nab + bc + ca = 6\n\\]\n\nWe want to find \\(a + b + c\\). Let's denote \\(s = a + b + c\\). We know the identity:\n\n\\[\n(a + b + c)^2 = a^2 + b^2 + c^2 + 2(ab + bc + ca)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values into this identity, we have:\n\n\\[\ns^2 = 13 + 2 \\times 6\n\\]\n\n\\[\ns^2 = 13 + 12 = 25\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we find:\n\n\\[\ns = \\sqrt{25} = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\)."
'Let the two numbers be \\( x \\) and \\( y \\). We are given the following system of equations:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 25\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx - y = 9\n\\]\n\nTo find \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), we can add these two equations:\n\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 25 + 9\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2x = 34\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 17\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x = 17 \\) back into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n17 + y = 25\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 25 - 17\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 8\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\( x = 17 \\) and \\( y = 8 \\), we can find their product:\n\n\\[\nx \\cdot y = 17 \\cdot 8 = 136\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the two numbers is \\(\\boxed{136}\\).'
'To determine the domain of the function \\( q(x) = \\frac{\\sqrt{x}}{\\sqrt{1-x^2}} \\), we need to consider the restrictions imposed by the square roots and the denominator.\n\n1. **Square Root in the Numerator:**\n   - The expression \\(\\sqrt{x}\\) is defined for \\(x \\geq 0\\).\n\n2. **Square Root in the Denominator:**\n   - The expression \\(\\sqrt{1-x^2}\\) is defined for \\(1-x^2 \\geq 0\\), which simplifies to \\(-1 \\leq x \\leq 1\\).\n   - Additionally, since the square root is in the denominator, it cannot be zero. Therefore, \\(1-x^2 > 0\\), which simplifies to \\(-1 < x < 1\\).\n\nCombining these conditions:\n- From \\(\\sqrt{x}\\), we have \\(x \\geq 0\\).\n- From \\(\\sqrt{1-x^2}\\), we have \\(-1 < x < 1\\).\n\nThe intersection of these conditions is \\(0 \\leq x < 1\\).\n\nThus, the domain of the function \\( q(x) \\) is \\([0, 1)\\).\n\nThe answer is \\([0, 1)\\).'
'To find the value of \\(\\frac{2x+y}{3x-2y}\\) given that \\(4x = 3y\\), we start by expressing \\(y\\) in terms of \\(x\\). From the equation \\(4x = 3y\\), we can solve for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{4x}{3}\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\(y = \\frac{4x}{3}\\) into the expression \\(\\frac{2x+y}{3x-2y}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2x + y}{3x - 2y} = \\frac{2x + \\frac{4x}{3}}{3x - 2\\left(\\frac{4x}{3}\\right)}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the numerator:\n\n\\[\n2x + \\frac{4x}{3} = \\frac{6x}{3} + \\frac{4x}{3} = \\frac{10x}{3}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the denominator:\n\n\\[\n3x - 2\\left(\\frac{4x}{3}\\right) = 3x - \\frac{8x}{3} = \\frac{9x}{3} - \\frac{8x}{3} = \\frac{x}{3}\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these simplified expressions back into the fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\frac{10x}{3}}{\\frac{x}{3}} = \\frac{10x}{3} \\times \\frac{3}{x} = 10\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{2x+y}{3x-2y}\\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\left(\\frac{i}{2}\\right)^2\\), we start by squaring the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{i}{2}\\right)^2 = \\left(\\frac{i}{2}\\right) \\times \\left(\\frac{i}{2}\\right)\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{i \\times i}{2 \\times 2} = \\frac{i^2}{4}\n\\]\n\nWe know that \\(i^2 = -1\\). Therefore, substituting this into the expression gives:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{-1}{4} = -\\frac{1}{4}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\left(\\frac{i}{2}\\right)^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{1}{4}}\\).'
"To find the radius of the cookie, we need to rewrite the given equation of the circle in standard form. The given equation is:\n\n\\[ x^2 + y^2 - 6 = 6x + 2y. \\]\n\nFirst, let's rearrange the terms:\n\n\\[ x^2 - 6x + y^2 - 2y = 6. \\]\n\nNext, we complete the square for both the \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) terms.\n\nFor the \\(x\\) terms: \\(x^2 - 6x\\).\n\n1. Take half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), which is \\(-6\\), giving \\(-3\\).\n2. Square \\(-3\\) to get \\(9\\).\n3. Add and subtract \\(9\\) inside the equation.\n\nFor the \\(y\\) terms: \\(y^2 - 2y\\).\n\n1. Take half of the coefficient of \\(y\\), which is \\(-2\\), giving \\(-1\\).\n2. Square \\(-1\\) to get \\(1\\).\n3. Add and subtract \\(1\\) inside the equation.\n\nNow, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[ (x^2 - 6x + 9) + (y^2 - 2y + 1) = 6 + 9 + 1. \\]\n\nSimplify the left side by writing it as perfect squares:\n\n\\[ (x - 3)^2 + (y - 1)^2 = 16. \\]\n\nThis is the standard form of a circle's equation \\((x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2\\), where \\((h, k)\\) is the center and \\(r\\) is the radius.\n\nFrom the equation \\((x - 3)^2 + (y - 1)^2 = 16\\), we see that the center of the circle is \\((3, 1)\\) and the radius \\(r\\) is \\(\\sqrt{16} = 4\\).\n\nTherefore, the radius of the cookie is \\(\\boxed{4}\\)."
"Let \\( r \\) be the number of red marbles, \\( y \\) be the number of yellow marbles, \\( o \\) be the number of orange marbles, and \\( w \\) be the number of white marbles. We are given the following relationships:\n\n1. \\( r + y + o + w = 35 \\)\n2. \\( \\frac{r}{2} = y - 2 \\)\n3. \\( \\frac{r}{2} = \\frac{o}{3} \\)\n4. \\( \\frac{r}{2} = \\frac{w + 3}{3} \\)\n\nLet's denote \\( \\frac{r}{2} = k \\). Then we have:\n\n- \\( y = k + 2 \\)\n- \\( o = 3k \\)\n- \\( w = 3k - 3 \\)\n\nSubstitute these expressions into the total equation:\n\n\\[\nr + y + o + w = 35\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the expressions for \\( y \\), \\( o \\), and \\( w \\):\n\n\\[\nr + (k + 2) + 3k + (3k - 3) = 35\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\nr + k + 2 + 3k + 3k - 3 = 35\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\nr + 7k - 1 = 35\n\\]\n\nSince \\( r = 2k \\), substitute \\( r = 2k \\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\n2k + 7k - 1 = 35\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n9k - 1 = 35\n\\]\n\nAdd 1 to both sides:\n\n\\[\n9k = 36\n\\]\n\nDivide by 9:\n\n\\[\nk = 4\n\\]\n\nSince \\( r = 2k \\), we have:\n\n\\[\nr = 2 \\times 4 = 8\n\\]\n\nThus, the number of red marbles is \\(\\boxed{8}\\)."
'The roots of the quadratic equation \\(4x^2 + 7x + k = 0\\) are given as \\(\\frac{-7 \\pm i\\sqrt{15}}{8}\\). These roots are in the form \\(\\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\\), where \\(a = 4\\), \\(b = 7\\), and \\(c = k\\).\n\nThe given roots are complex, indicating that the discriminant \\(b^2 - 4ac\\) is negative. The imaginary part of the roots is \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{15}}{8}\\), which corresponds to \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{-(b^2 - 4ac)}}{2a}\\).\n\nFirst, equate the imaginary part:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{15}}{8} = \\frac{\\sqrt{-(b^2 - 4ac)}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(a = 4\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{15}}{8} = \\frac{\\sqrt{-(7^2 - 4 \\cdot 4 \\cdot k)}}{8}\n\\]\n\nSquaring both sides, we get:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{15}{64} = \\frac{-(49 - 16k)}{64}\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 64:\n\n\\[\n15 = -(49 - 16k)\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\(k\\):\n\n\\[\n15 = -49 + 16k\n\\]\n\n\\[\n64 = 16k\n\\]\n\n\\[\nk = \\frac{64}{16} = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(k\\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To solve the problem, we need to calculate the values of \\(\\lfloor 10N \\rfloor\\), \\(\\lfloor 100N \\rfloor\\), \\(\\lfloor 1000N \\rfloor\\), and \\(\\lfloor 10,000N \\rfloor\\) where \\(N = \\frac{1}{3}\\).\n\n1. **Calculate \\(\\lfloor 10N \\rfloor\\):**\n\n   \\[\n   10N = 10 \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{10}{3} \\approx 3.3333\n   \\]\n\n   The greatest integer less than or equal to \\(\\frac{10}{3}\\) is 3. Therefore, \\(\\lfloor 10N \\rfloor = 3\\).\n\n2. **Calculate \\(\\lfloor 100N \\rfloor\\):**\n\n   \\[\n   100N = 100 \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{100}{3} \\approx 33.3333\n   \\]\n\n   The greatest integer less than or equal to \\(\\frac{100}{3}\\) is 33. Therefore, \\(\\lfloor 100N \\rfloor = 33\\).\n\n3. **Calculate \\(\\lfloor 1000N \\rfloor\\):**\n\n   \\[\n   1000N = 1000 \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{1000}{3} \\approx 333.3333\n   \\]\n\n   The greatest integer less than or equal to \\(\\frac{1000}{3}\\) is 333. Therefore, \\(\\lfloor 1000N \\rfloor = 333\\).\n\n4. **Calculate \\(\\lfloor 10,000N \\rfloor\\):**\n\n   \\[\n   10,000N = 10,000 \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{10,000}{3} \\approx 3333.3333\n   \\]\n\n   The greatest integer less than or equal to \\(\\frac{10,000}{3}\\) is 3333. Therefore, \\(\\lfloor 10,000N \\rfloor = 3333\\).\n\nNow, we sum these values:\n\n\\[\n\\lfloor 10N \\rfloor + \\lfloor 100N \\rfloor + \\lfloor 1000N \\rfloor + \\lfloor 10,000N \\rfloor = 3 + 33 + 333 + 3333 = 3702\n\\]\n\nThus, the value is \\(\\boxed{3702}\\).'
'To find a value for \\( x \\) such that \\( f^{-1}(x) = f(x+1) \\), we first need to determine the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) for the given function \\( f(x) = 5x - 12 \\).\n\n1. **Find the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\):**\n\n   Start by setting \\( y = f(x) = 5x - 12 \\).\n\n   Solve for \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y \\):\n   \\[\n   y = 5x - 12 \\implies 5x = y + 12 \\implies x = \\frac{y + 12}{5}\n   \\]\n\n   Thus, the inverse function is:\n   \\[\n   f^{-1}(x) = \\frac{x + 12}{5}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Set up the equation \\( f^{-1}(x) = f(x+1) \\):**\n\n   We have:\n   \\[\n   f^{-1}(x) = \\frac{x + 12}{5}\n   \\]\n\n   Calculate \\( f(x+1) \\):\n   \\[\n   f(x+1) = 5(x+1) - 12 = 5x + 5 - 12 = 5x - 7\n   \\]\n\n   Set the two expressions equal:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{x + 12}{5} = 5x - 7\n   \\]\n\n3. **Solve the equation:**\n\n   Multiply both sides by 5 to eliminate the fraction:\n   \\[\n   x + 12 = 25x - 35\n   \\]\n\n   Rearrange the terms:\n   \\[\n   12 + 35 = 25x - x\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   47 = 24x\n   \\]\n\n   Solve for \\( x \\):\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{47}{24}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x \\) that satisfies the equation \\( f^{-1}(x) = f(x+1) \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{47}{24}}\\).'

Therefore, the expression becomes:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{8} \\times 2^{12}.\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\(2^{12}\\):\n\\[\n2^{12} = 4096.\n\\]\n\nThus, the denominator becomes:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{8} \\times 4096 = \\frac{4096}{8}.\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\(\\frac{4096}{8}\\):\n\\[\n\\frac{4096}{8} = 512.\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute back into the original expression:\n\\[\n\\frac{512}{512}.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\\[\n1.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the simplified expression is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'

'To find the number of teams \\( n \\) in a round-robin tournament where 55 games are played, we use the formula for the number of games:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{n^2 - n}{2} = 55\n\\]\n\nFirst, multiply both sides by 2 to eliminate the fraction:\n\n\\[\nn^2 - n = 110\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation to form a standard quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\nn^2 - n - 110 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe can solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -1 \\), and \\( c = -110 \\). Plug these values into the formula:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-(-1) \\pm \\sqrt{(-1)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-110)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 \\pm \\sqrt{1 + 440}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 \\pm \\sqrt{441}}{2}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(\\sqrt{441} = 21\\), we have:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 \\pm 21}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two possible solutions:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 + 21}{2} = \\frac{22}{2} = 11\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 - 21}{2} = \\frac{-20}{2} = -10\n\\]\n\nSince the number of teams cannot be negative, the number of teams is:\n\n\\[\nn = 11\n\\]\n\nThus, there are \\(\\boxed{11}\\) teams in the tournament.'
"To solve the equation \\(\\lceil x \\rceil + \\lfloor x \\rfloor + x = 4.8\\), we start by understanding the properties of the ceiling and floor functions. For any real number \\(x\\), the floor function \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor\\) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(x\\), and the ceiling function \\(\\lceil x \\rceil\\) is the smallest integer greater than or equal to \\(x\\).\n\nLet's denote:\n- \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor = n\\), where \\(n\\) is an integer.\n- Then, \\(n \\leq x < n+1\\).\n\nThe ceiling function \\(\\lceil x \\rceil\\) can be expressed as:\n- \\(\\lceil x \\rceil = n\\) if \\(x = n\\),\n- \\(\\lceil x \\rceil = n+1\\) if \\(x > n\\).\n\nGiven the equation:\n\\[\n\\lceil x \\rceil + \\lfloor x \\rfloor + x = 4.8\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor = n\\), we have:\n\\[\n\\lceil x \\rceil + n + x = 4.8\n\\]\n\nConsider the two cases for \\(\\lceil x \\rceil\\):\n\n**Case 1:** \\(x = n\\)\n\nIn this case, \\(\\lceil x \\rceil = n\\), so the equation becomes:\n\\[\nn + n + n = 4.8 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad 3n = 4.8 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad n = \\frac{4.8}{3} = 1.6\n\\]\n\nSince \\(n\\) must be an integer, this case is not possible.\n\n**Case 2:** \\(n < x < n+1\\)\n\nHere, \\(\\lceil x \\rceil = n+1\\), so the equation becomes:\n\\[\n(n+1) + n + x = 4.8 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad 2n + 1 + x = 4.8\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(x\\), we have:\n\\[\nx = 4.8 - 2n - 1 = 3.8 - 2n\n\\]\n\nSince \\(n < x < n+1\\), we substitute \\(x = 3.8 - 2n\\) into the inequality:\n\\[\nn < 3.8 - 2n < n+1\n\\]\n\nBreaking it into two inequalities:\n1. \\(n < 3.8 - 2n\\)\n   \\[\n   3n < 3.8 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad n < \\frac{3.8}{3} \\approx 1.2667\n   \\]\n\n2. \\(3.8 - 2n < n+1\\)\n   \\[\n   3.8 - 1 < 3n \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad 2.8 < 3n \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad n > \\frac{2.8}{3} \\approx 0.9333\n   \\]\n\nSince \\(n\\) is an integer, the only possible value for \\(n\\) is \\(n = 1\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(n = 1\\) back into \\(x = 3.8 - 2n\\):\n\\[\nx = 3.8 - 2 \\times 1 = 3.8 - 2 = 1.8\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(x = \\boxed{1.8}\\)."
'To solve the expression \\(49x^2 + 14x(19-7x) + (19-7x)^2\\), we start by expanding each term.\n\nFirst, expand the middle term:\n\\[\n14x(19 - 7x) = 14x \\cdot 19 - 14x \\cdot 7x = 266x - 98x^2.\n\\]\n\nNext, expand the last term:\n\\[\n(19 - 7x)^2 = 19^2 - 2 \\cdot 19 \\cdot 7x + (7x)^2 = 361 - 266x + 49x^2.\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these expanded terms back into the original expression:\n\\[\n49x^2 + (266x - 98x^2) + (361 - 266x + 49x^2).\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n- The \\(x^2\\) terms: \\(49x^2 - 98x^2 + 49x^2 = 0\\).\n- The \\(x\\) terms: \\(266x - 266x = 0\\).\n- The constant term: \\(361\\).\n\nThus, the expression simplifies to:\n\\[\n0 + 0 + 361 = 361.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{361}\\).'
"Let \\( L \\) represent the amount of money Larry has, and let \\( N \\) represent the amount of money Lenny has. According to the problem, we have the following two equations:\n\n1. \\( L + N = 35 \\)\n2. \\( L = \\frac{2}{5}N \\)\n\nWe can substitute the expression for \\( L \\) from the second equation into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2}{5}N + N = 35\n\\]\n\nCombine the terms on the left side:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2}{5}N + \\frac{5}{5}N = 35\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{7}{5}N = 35\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( N \\), multiply both sides by \\(\\frac{5}{7}\\):\n\n\\[\nN = 35 \\times \\frac{5}{7} = 25\n\\]\n\nNow that we know \\( N = 25 \\), we can find \\( L \\) using the equation \\( L = \\frac{2}{5}N \\):\n\n\\[\nL = \\frac{2}{5} \\times 25 = 10\n\\]\n\nLenny has \\( N = 25 \\) dollars, and Larry has \\( L = 10 \\) dollars. The difference between Lenny's and Larry's amounts is:\n\n\\[\nN - L = 25 - 10 = 15\n\\]\n\nThus, Lenny has \\(\\boxed{15}\\) more dollars than Larry."
