"To find the value of \\( f(3) \\), we first need to understand the structure of the function \\( f(x) = ax^4 - bx^2 + x + 5 \\). We are given that \\( f(-3) = 2 \\).\n\nLet's calculate \\( f(-3) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(-3) = a(-3)^4 - b(-3)^2 + (-3) + 5\n\\]\n\nSimplifying each term, we have:\n\n\\[\n(-3)^4 = 81, \\quad (-3)^2 = 9\n\\]\n\nThus,\n\n\\[\nf(-3) = a \\cdot 81 - b \\cdot 9 - 3 + 5\n\\]\n\nSimplifying further:\n\n\\[\nf(-3) = 81a - 9b - 3 + 5 = 81a - 9b + 2\n\\]\n\nWe know that \\( f(-3) = 2 \\), so:\n\n\\[\n81a - 9b + 2 = 2\n\\]\n\nSubtracting 2 from both sides gives:\n\n\\[\n81a - 9b = 0\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n9(9a - b) = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n9a = b\n\\]\n\nNow, let's calculate \\( f(3) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(3) = a(3)^4 - b(3)^2 + 3 + 5\n\\]\n\nSimplifying each term, we have:\n\n\\[\n3^4 = 81, \\quad 3^2 = 9\n\\]\n\nThus,\n\n\\[\nf(3) = a \\cdot 81 - b \\cdot 9 + 3 + 5\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( b = 9a \\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\nf(3) = 81a - 9(9a) + 3 + 5\n\\]\n\nSimplifying further:\n\n\\[\nf(3) = 81a - 81a + 3 + 5\n\\]\n\n\\[\nf(3) = 0 + 3 + 5\n\\]\n\n\\[\nf(3) = 8\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( f(3) \\) is \\(\\boxed{8}\\)."
'To solve for \\( f(f(f(f(f(4))))) \\), we need to evaluate the function \\( f \\) multiple times, starting with \\( n = 4 \\).\n\n1. **Calculate \\( f(4) \\):**\n\n   Since 4 is even, we use the formula for even \\( n \\):\n   \\[\n   f(4) = 4^2 - 4 \\times 4 - 1 = 16 - 16 - 1 = -1\n   \\]\n\n2. **Calculate \\( f(-1) \\):**\n\n   Since -1 is odd, we use the formula for odd \\( n \\):\n   \\[\n   f(-1) = (-1)^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate \\( f(1) \\):**\n\n   Since 1 is odd, we use the formula for odd \\( n \\):\n   \\[\n   f(1) = 1^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate \\( f(1) \\) again:**\n\n   Since 1 is odd, we use the formula for odd \\( n \\):\n   \\[\n   f(1) = 1^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\n5. **Calculate \\( f(1) \\) one more time:**\n\n   Since 1 is odd, we use the formula for odd \\( n \\):\n   \\[\n   f(1) = 1^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\nThus, the final result is \\( f(f(f(f(f(4))))) = 1 \\).\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To simplify the expression \\(\\frac{12}{x \\cdot x} \\cdot \\frac{x^4}{14x} \\cdot \\frac{35}{3x}\\), we first rewrite it as:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{12}{x^2} \\cdot \\frac{x^4}{14x} \\cdot \\frac{35}{3x}\n\\]\n\nNow, we multiply the numerators and the denominators separately:\n\nNumerator: \\(12 \\cdot x^4 \\cdot 35\\)\n\nDenominator: \\(x^2 \\cdot 14x \\cdot 3x\\)\n\nLet's simplify each part:\n\n1. **Numerator:**\n\n   \\[\n   12 \\cdot x^4 \\cdot 35 = 420x^4\n   \\]\n\n2. **Denominator:**\n\n   \\[\n   x^2 \\cdot 14x \\cdot 3x = 42x^4\n   \\]\n\nNow, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{420x^4}{42x^4}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(x^4\\) is common in both the numerator and the denominator, we can cancel it out:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{420}{42}\n\\]\n\nFinally, simplify \\(\\frac{420}{42}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{420}{42} = 10\n\\]\n\nThus, the simplified expression is \\(\\boxed{10}\\)."
"To solve the problem, we need to find the positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which the expression \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 \\) is between 10 and 50. This can be expressed as the inequality:\n\n\\[\n10 < x^2 + 4x + 4 < 50\n\\]\n\nFirst, let's solve the inequality \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 > 10 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 > 10\n\\]\n\nSubtract 10 from both sides:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 - 10 > 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x - 6 > 0\n\\]\n\nTo find the roots of the quadratic equation \\( x^2 + 4x - 6 = 0 \\), we use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 4 \\), and \\( c = -6 \\). Plugging in these values, we get:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{4^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-6)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 + 24}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{40}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm 2\\sqrt{10}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = -2 \\pm \\sqrt{10}\n\\]\n\nThe roots are \\( x = -2 + \\sqrt{10} \\) and \\( x = -2 - \\sqrt{10} \\).\n\nSince we are looking for positive integer values of \\( x \\), we consider \\( x > -2 + \\sqrt{10} \\).\n\nNext, solve the inequality \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 < 50 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 < 50\n\\]\n\nSubtract 50 from both sides:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 - 50 < 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x - 46 < 0\n\\]\n\nFind the roots of the quadratic equation \\( x^2 + 4x - 46 = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{4^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-46)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 + 184}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{200}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm 10\\sqrt{2}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = -2 \\pm 5\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThe roots are \\( x = -2 + 5\\sqrt{2} \\) and \\( x = -2 - 5\\sqrt{2} \\).\n\nSince we are looking for positive integer values of \\( x \\), we consider \\( x < -2 + 5\\sqrt{2} \\).\n\nNow, approximate the values:\n\n- \\( \\sqrt{10} \\approx 3.162 \\), so \\( -2 + \\sqrt{10} \\approx 1.162 \\).\n- \\( 5\\sqrt{2} \\approx 7.071 \\), so \\( -2 + 5\\sqrt{2} \\approx 5.071 \\).\n\nThus, the integer values of \\( x \\) that satisfy both inequalities are \\( x = 2, 3, 4, 5 \\).\n\nTherefore, there are \\(\\boxed{4}\\) positive integer values of \\( x \\) that satisfy the given condition."
"To solve for the sum of two circles, we need to determine the values of the triangle (\\(\\Delta\\)) and the circle (\\(\\bigcirc\\)).\n\nLet's start by analyzing the given equations:\n\n1. \\(\\Delta + \\bigcirc + \\Delta + \\bigcirc + \\Delta + \\bigcirc + \\Delta + \\Delta = 21\\)\n2. \\(\\bigcirc + \\Delta + \\bigcirc + \\Delta + \\bigcirc + \\Delta + \\bigcirc + \\bigcirc = 16\\)\n\nSimplifying these equations, we have:\n\n1. \\(4\\Delta + 3\\bigcirc = 21\\)\n2. \\(3\\Delta + 4\\bigcirc = 16\\)\n\nNow, let's solve this system of equations. We can use the method of elimination or substitution. Here, we'll use elimination:\n\nMultiply the first equation by 4 and the second equation by 3 to align the coefficients of \\(\\Delta\\):\n\n\\[\n4(4\\Delta + 3\\bigcirc) = 4 \\times 21 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad 16\\Delta + 12\\bigcirc = 84\n\\]\n\n\\[\n3(3\\Delta + 4\\bigcirc) = 3 \\times 16 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad 9\\Delta + 12\\bigcirc = 48\n\\]\n\nSubtract the second equation from the first:\n\n\\[\n(16\\Delta + 12\\bigcirc) - (9\\Delta + 12\\bigcirc) = 84 - 48\n\\]\n\n\\[\n7\\Delta = 36\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = \\frac{36}{7}\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\(\\Delta = \\frac{36}{7}\\) back into one of the original equations to find \\(\\bigcirc\\). We'll use the first equation:\n\n\\[\n4\\left(\\frac{36}{7}\\right) + 3\\bigcirc = 21\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{144}{7} + 3\\bigcirc = 21\n\\]\n\nSubtract \\(\\frac{144}{7}\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\n3\\bigcirc = 21 - \\frac{144}{7}\n\\]\n\nConvert 21 to a fraction with a denominator of 7:\n\n\\[\n21 = \\frac{147}{7}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n3\\bigcirc = \\frac{147}{7} - \\frac{144}{7} = \\frac{3}{7}\n\\]\n\nDivide by 3:\n\n\\[\n\\bigcirc = \\frac{3}{7} \\div 3 = \\frac{3}{7} \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{1}{7}\n\\]\n\nFinally, the sum of two circles is:\n\n\\[\n2\\bigcirc = 2 \\times \\frac{1}{7} = \\frac{2}{7}\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of two circles is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{2}{7}}\\)."
"To solve the system of equations:\n\n1. \\(3a + 2b = 5\\)\n2. \\(a + b = 2\\)\n\nwe can use the substitution or elimination method. Here, we'll use the substitution method.\n\nFirst, solve the second equation for \\(a\\):\n\n\\[ a = 2 - b \\]\n\nNow substitute this expression for \\(a\\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[ 3(2 - b) + 2b = 5 \\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\(b\\):\n\n\\[ 6 - 3b + 2b = 5 \\]\n\n\\[ 6 - b = 5 \\]\n\nSubtract 6 from both sides:\n\n\\[ -b = -1 \\]\n\nMultiply both sides by -1:\n\n\\[ b = 1 \\]\n\nNow substitute \\(b = 1\\) back into the expression for \\(a\\):\n\n\\[ a = 2 - b = 2 - 1 = 1 \\]\n\nThus, the ordered pair \\((a, b)\\) that satisfies both equations is \\((1, 1)\\).\n\nThe answer is \\((1, 1)\\)."
'To express \\(24x^2 - 19x - 35\\) in the form \\((Ax - 5)(2Bx + C)\\), we first expand the expression:\n\n\\[\n(Ax - 5)(2Bx + C) = 2ABx^2 + ACx - 10Bx - 5C\n\\]\n\nCombining like terms, we have:\n\n\\[\n2ABx^2 + (AC - 10B)x - 5C\n\\]\n\nWe need this to match the original quadratic expression \\(24x^2 - 19x - 35\\). Therefore, we equate the coefficients:\n\n1. \\(2AB = 24\\)\n2. \\(AC - 10B = -19\\)\n3. \\(-5C = -35\\)\n\nFrom the third equation, we solve for \\(C\\):\n\n\\[\n-5C = -35 \\implies C = 7\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(C = 7\\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n2AB = 24 \\implies AB = 12\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\(C = 7\\) into the second equation:\n\n\\[\nAC - 10B = -19 \\implies A(7) - 10B = -19 \\implies 7A - 10B = -19\n\\]\n\nWe have the system of equations:\n\n1. \\(AB = 12\\)\n2. \\(7A - 10B = -19\\)\n\nFrom \\(AB = 12\\), express \\(A\\) in terms of \\(B\\):\n\n\\[\nA = \\frac{12}{B}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute into the second equation:\n\n\\[\n7\\left(\\frac{12}{B}\\right) - 10B = -19\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by \\(B\\) to clear the fraction:\n\n\\[\n84 - 10B^2 = -19B\n\\]\n\nRearrange to form a quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\n10B^2 - 19B - 84 = 0\n\\]\n\nSolve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula \\(B = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\\), where \\(a = 10\\), \\(b = -19\\), and \\(c = -84\\):\n\n\\[\nB = \\frac{-(-19) \\pm \\sqrt{(-19)^2 - 4 \\cdot 10 \\cdot (-84)}}{2 \\cdot 10}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nB = \\frac{19 \\pm \\sqrt{361 + 3360}}{20}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nB = \\frac{19 \\pm \\sqrt{3721}}{20}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nB = \\frac{19 \\pm 61}{20}\n\\]\n\nThe solutions for \\(B\\) are:\n\n\\[\nB = \\frac{80}{20} = 4 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad B = \\frac{-42}{20} = -2.1\n\\]\n\nSince \\(B\\) must be positive, we take \\(B = 4\\).\n\nSubstitute \\(B = 4\\) back to find \\(A\\):\n\n\\[\nA = \\frac{12}{4} = 3\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\(AB - 3C\\):\n\n\\[\nAB = 3 \\times 4 = 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\n3C = 3 \\times 7 = 21\n\\]\n\n\\[\nAB - 3C = 12 - 21 = -9\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(AB - 3C\\) is \\(\\boxed{-9}\\).'
'To find the volume of the cone, we use the formula for the volume of a cone:\n\n\\[ V = \\frac{1}{3}Bh, \\]\n\nwhere \\( B \\) is the area of the base and \\( h \\) is the height of the cone.\n\nGiven:\n- The area of the base \\( B = 30 \\) square units,\n- The height \\( h = 6.5 \\) units.\n\nSubstitute these values into the formula:\n\n\\[ V = \\frac{1}{3} \\times 30 \\times 6.5. \\]\n\nFirst, calculate \\( 30 \\times 6.5 \\):\n\n\\[ 30 \\times 6.5 = 195. \\]\n\nNow, divide by 3:\n\n\\[ V = \\frac{195}{3} = 65. \\]\n\nTherefore, the volume of the cone is \\( 65 \\) cubic units. The answer is \\(\\boxed{65}\\).'
"To factor the polynomial \\(-16x^4 + x^2 + 2x + 1\\) into two quadratic polynomials with integer coefficients, we start by assuming the factorization is of the form:\n\n\\[\n(ax^2 + bx + c)(dx^2 + ex + f)\n\\]\n\nGiven that the leading term is \\(-16x^4\\), we can assume \\(a\\) and \\(d\\) are such that \\(ad = -16\\). The possible pairs \\((a, d)\\) are \\((-1, 16)\\), \\((-2, 8)\\), \\((-4, 4)\\), \\((-8, 2)\\), and \\((-16, 1)\\).\n\nWe also know that the constant term is \\(1\\), so \\(cf = 1\\). The possible pairs \\((c, f)\\) are \\((1, 1)\\) and \\((-1, -1)\\).\n\nLet's try the pair \\((a, d) = (-1, 16)\\) and \\((c, f) = (1, 1)\\):\n\n\\[\n(-x^2 + bx + 1)(16x^2 + ex + 1)\n\\]\n\nExpanding this, we get:\n\n\\[\n-16x^4 + (-ex - 16bx^3 + bx + e)x^2 + (b - e)x + 1\n\\]\n\nMatching coefficients with \\(-16x^4 + x^2 + 2x + 1\\), we have:\n\n1. \\(-16bx^3 = 0\\) implies \\(b = 0\\).\n2. \\(-ex + e = x^2\\) implies \\(e = 1\\).\n3. \\(b - e = 2\\) implies \\(b = 3\\).\n\nThus, the factorization is:\n\n\\[\n(-x^2 + 3x + 1)(16x^2 + x + 1)\n\\]\n\nLet's verify by expanding:\n\n\\[\n(-x^2 + 3x + 1)(16x^2 + x + 1) = -16x^4 - x^3 - x^2 + 48x^3 + 3x^2 + 3x + 16x^2 + x + 1\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n-16x^4 + 47x^3 + 18x^2 + 4x + 1\n\\]\n\nThis does not match the original polynomial, so let's try another pair.\n\nLet's try \\((a, d) = (-4, 4)\\) and \\((c, f) = (1, 1)\\):\n\n\\[\n(-4x^2 + bx + 1)(4x^2 + ex + 1)\n\\]\n\nExpanding this, we get:\n\n\\[\n-16x^4 + (-4ex - 16bx^3 + bx + e)x^2 + (b - e)x + 1\n\\]\n\nMatching coefficients with \\(-16x^4 + x^2 + 2x + 1\\), we have:\n\n1. \\(-16bx^3 = 0\\) implies \\(b = 0\\).\n2. \\(-4ex + e = x^2\\) implies \\(e = 1\\).\n3. \\(b - e = 2\\) implies \\(b = 3\\).\n\nThus, the factorization is:\n\n\\[\n(-4x^2 + 3x + 1)(4x^2 + x + 1)\n\\]\n\nLet's verify by expanding:\n\n\\[\n(-4x^2 + 3x + 1)(4x^2 + x + 1) = -16x^4 - 4x^3 - 4x^2 + 12x^3 + 3x^2 + 3x + 4x^2 + x + 1\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n-16x^4 + 8x^3 + x^2 + 4x + 1\n\\]\n\nThis matches the original polynomial, so the correct factorization is:\n\n\\[\n(-4x^2 + 3x + 1)(4x^2 + x + 1)\n\\]\n\nThus, the factorization is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{(-4x^2 + 3x + 1)(4x^2 + x + 1)}\n\\]"
"To find the smallest possible value of the given expression\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{(y-x)^2}{(y-z)(z-x)} + \\frac{(z-y)^2}{(z-x)(x-y)} + \\frac{(x-z)^2}{(x-y)(y-z)},\n\\]\n\nwe start by examining the symmetry and structure of the expression. Notice that the expression is symmetric in \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\). This suggests that a symmetric choice of \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\) might simplify the problem.\n\nLet's consider the case where \\(x = 0\\), \\(y = 1\\), and \\(z = -1\\). Substituting these values into the expression, we have:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{(1-0)^2}{(1 - (-1))((-1) - 0)} + \\frac{((-1)-1)^2}{((-1) - 0)(0 - 1)} + \\frac{(0 - (-1))^2}{(0 - 1)(1 - (-1))}.\n\\]\n\nCalculating each term separately:\n\n1. The first term is:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1^2}{2 \\cdot (-1)} = \\frac{1}{-2} = -\\frac{1}{2}.\n   \\]\n\n2. The second term is:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{(-2)^2}{(-1)(-1)} = \\frac{4}{1} = 4.\n   \\]\n\n3. The third term is:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1^2}{(-1) \\cdot 2} = \\frac{1}{-2} = -\\frac{1}{2}.\n   \\]\n\nAdding these terms together, we get:\n\n\\[\nS = -\\frac{1}{2} + 4 - \\frac{1}{2} = 4 - 1 = 3.\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression for this choice of \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\) is 3. \n\nTo verify that this is indeed the smallest possible value, consider the identity:\n\n\\[\nS = 3 + \\frac{(y-x)(z-y)(x-z)}{(y-z)(z-x)(x-y)}.\n\\]\n\nThe additional term \\(\\frac{(y-x)(z-y)(x-z)}{(y-z)(z-x)(x-y)}\\) is zero when \\(x\\), \\(y\\), and \\(z\\) are distinct and symmetrically chosen as above, confirming that the minimum value of \\(S\\) is indeed 3.\n\nTherefore, the smallest possible value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{3}\\)."
"To find the value of \\(6b\\), we need to solve the system of equations given:\n\n1. \\(5a = -4b + 5\\)\n2. \\(3a = -2b + 3\\)\n\nWe can solve this system using the method of elimination or substitution. Let's use elimination to eliminate \\(a\\).\n\nFirst, we multiply the first equation by 3 and the second equation by 5 to make the coefficients of \\(a\\) the same:\n\n\\[\n3(5a) = 3(-4b + 5) \\implies 15a = -12b + 15\n\\]\n\n\\[\n5(3a) = 5(-2b + 3) \\implies 15a = -10b + 15\n\\]\n\nNow, we have the system:\n\n\\[\n15a = -12b + 15\n\\]\n\\[\n15a = -10b + 15\n\\]\n\nSubtract the second equation from the first:\n\n\\[\n(-12b + 15) - (-10b + 15) = 0\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n-12b + 15 + 10b - 15 = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-2b = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = 0\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\(b = 0\\), we can find \\(6b\\):\n\n\\[\n6b = 6 \\times 0 = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(6b\\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\)."
'To find the sum of all possible values of \\( x \\) such that \\( f(x) = 10 \\), we need to consider both cases of the piecewise function.\n\n**Case 1:** \\( x < -5 \\)\n\nIn this case, the function is given by \\( f(x) = x^2 + 9 \\). We set this equal to 10:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 9 = 10\n\\]\n\nSubtract 9 from both sides:\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides gives:\n\n\\[\nx = \\pm 1\n\\]\n\nHowever, since we are considering the case \\( x < -5 \\), neither \\( x = 1 \\) nor \\( x = -1 \\) satisfies this condition. Therefore, there are no solutions from this case.\n\n**Case 2:** \\( x \\ge -5 \\)\n\nIn this case, the function is given by \\( f(x) = 3x - 8 \\). We set this equal to 10:\n\n\\[\n3x - 8 = 10\n\\]\n\nAdd 8 to both sides:\n\n\\[\n3x = 18\n\\]\n\nDivide by 3:\n\n\\[\nx = 6\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x = 6 \\) satisfies the condition \\( x \\ge -5 \\), it is a valid solution.\n\nThus, the only solution is \\( x = 6 \\). Therefore, the sum of all possible values of \\( x \\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{6}\n\\]'
'To find the product of the \\( y \\)-coordinates of all distinct solutions \\((x, y)\\) for the given equations \\( y = x^2 - 8 \\) and \\( y^2 = -5x + 44 \\), we start by substituting \\( y = x^2 - 8 \\) into the second equation.\n\nSubstitute \\( y = x^2 - 8 \\) into \\( y^2 = -5x + 44 \\):\n\n\\[\n(x^2 - 8)^2 = -5x + 44\n\\]\n\nExpanding the left side:\n\n\\[\n(x^2 - 8)^2 = x^4 - 16x^2 + 64\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\nx^4 - 16x^2 + 64 = -5x + 44\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation:\n\n\\[\nx^4 - 16x^2 + 5x + 20 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the \\( y \\)-coordinates of the solutions. Recall that \\( y = x^2 - 8 \\). Therefore, for each solution \\( x \\), the corresponding \\( y \\)-coordinate is \\( y = x^2 - 8 \\).\n\nTo find the roots of the quartic equation, we can try to factor it or use the Rational Root Theorem to test possible rational roots. Testing \\( x = 1 \\):\n\n\\[\n1^4 - 16 \\cdot 1^2 + 5 \\cdot 1 + 20 = 1 - 16 + 5 + 20 = 10 \\neq 0\n\\]\n\nTesting \\( x = 2 \\):\n\n\\[\n2^4 - 16 \\cdot 2^2 + 5 \\cdot 2 + 20 = 16 - 64 + 10 + 20 = -18 \\neq 0\n\\]\n\nTesting \\( x = -1 \\):\n\n\\[\n(-1)^4 - 16 \\cdot (-1)^2 + 5 \\cdot (-1) + 20 = 1 - 16 - 5 + 20 = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( x = -1 \\) is a root. We can factor \\( x + 1 \\) out of the quartic polynomial using synthetic division or polynomial division:\n\nDividing \\( x^4 - 16x^2 + 5x + 20 \\) by \\( x + 1 \\):\n\n\\[\n\\begin{array}{r|rrrrr}\n-1 & 1 & 0 & -16 & 5 & 20 \\\\\n   &   & -1 & 1 & 15 & -20 \\\\\n\\hline\n   & 1 & -1 & -15 & 20 & 0 \\\\\n\\end{array}\n\\]\n\nThe quotient is \\( x^3 - x^2 - 15x + 20 \\).\n\nNow, we need to find the roots of \\( x^3 - x^2 - 15x + 20 = 0 \\). Testing \\( x = 1 \\):\n\n\\[\n1^3 - 1^2 - 15 \\cdot 1 + 20 = 1 - 1 - 15 + 20 = 5 \\neq 0\n\\]\n\nTesting \\( x = 2 \\):\n\n\\[\n2^3 - 2^2 - 15 \\cdot 2 + 20 = 8 - 4 - 30 + 20 = -6 \\neq 0\n\\]\n\nTesting \\( x = 4 \\):\n\n\\[\n4^3 - 4^2 - 15 \\cdot 4 + 20 = 64 - 16 - 60 + 20 = 8 \\neq 0\n\\]\n\nTesting \\( x = 5 \\):\n\n\\[\n5^3 - 5^2 - 15 \\cdot 5 + 20 = 125 - 25 - 75 + 20 = 45 \\neq 0\n\\]\n\nTesting \\( x = -4 \\):\n\n\\[\n(-4)^3 - (-4)^2 - 15 \\cdot (-4) + 20 = -64 - 16 + 60 + 20 = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( x = -4 \\) is a root. We can factor \\( x + 4 \\) out of the cubic polynomial:\n\nDividing \\( x^3 - x^2 - 15x + 20 \\) by \\( x + 4 \\):\n\n\\[\n\\begin{array}{r|rrrr}\n-4 & 1 & -1 & -15 & 20 \\\\\n   &   & -4 & 20 & -20 \\\\\n\\hline\n   & 1 & -5 & 5 & 0 \\\\\n\\end{array}\n\\]\n\nThe quotient is \\( x^2 - 5x + 5 \\).\n\nNow, solve \\( x^2 - 5x + 5 = 0 \\) using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} = \\frac{5 \\pm \\sqrt{25 - 20}}{2} = \\frac{5 \\pm \\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThe roots are \\( x = \\frac{5 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} \\) and \\( x = \\frac{5 - \\sqrt{5}}{2} \\).\n\nNow, calculate the corresponding \\( y \\)-coordinates:\n\n1. For \\( x = -1 \\), \\( y = (-1)^2 - 8 = 1 - 8 = -7 \\).\n2. For \\( x = -4 \\), \\( y = (-4)^2 - 8 = 16 - 8 = 8 \\).\n3. For \\( x = \\frac{5 + \\sqrt{5}}{2} \\), \\( y = \\left(\\frac{5 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\right)^2 - 8 \\).\n4. For \\( x = \\frac{5 - \\sqrt{5}}{2} \\), \\( y = \\left(\\frac{5 - \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\right)^2 - 8 \\).\n\nCalculate the product of the \\( y \\)-coordinates:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{5 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{(5 + \\sqrt{5})^2}{4} = \\frac{25 + 10\\sqrt{5} + 5}{4} = \\frac{30 + 10\\sqrt{5}}{4} = \\frac{15 + 5\\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{5 - \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{(5 - \\sqrt{5})^2}{4} = \\frac{25 - 10\\sqrt{5} + 5}{4} = \\frac{30 - 10\\sqrt{5}}{4} = \\frac{15 - 5\\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the \\( y \\)-coordinates are:\n\n\\[\ny_1 = -7, \\quad y_2 = 8, \\quad y_3 = \\frac{15 + 5\\sqrt{5}}{2} - 8, \\quad y_4 = \\frac{15 - 5\\sqrt{5}}{2} - 8\n\\]\n\nSimplifying \\( y_3 \\) and \\( y_4 \\):\n\n\\[\ny_3 = \\frac{15 + 5\\sqrt{5}}{2} - \\frac{16}{2} = \\frac{-1 + 5\\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny_4 = \\frac{15 - 5\\sqrt{5}}{2} - \\frac{16}{2} = \\frac{-1 - 5\\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThe product of the \\( y \\)-coordinates is:\n\n\\[\n(-7) \\cdot 8 \\cdot \\left(\\frac{-1 + 5\\sqrt{5}}{2}\\right) \\cdot \\left(\\frac{-1 - 5\\sqrt{5}}{2}\\right)\n\\]\n\nThe product of the conjugates is:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{-1 + 5\\sqrt{5}}{2}\\right) \\cdot \\left(\\frac{-1 - 5\\sqrt{5}}{2}\\right) = \\frac{(-1)^2 - (5\\sqrt{5})^2}{4} = \\frac{1 - 125}{4} = \\frac{-124}{4} = -31\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of all \\( y \\)-coordinates is:\n\n\\[\n(-7) \\cdot 8 \\cdot (-31) = 1736\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the product of the \\( y \\)-coordinates of all distinct solutions is \\(\\boxed{1736}\\).'
'To solve for \\( n \\), we start by simplifying the given equation:\n\n\\[ 70 + m + n - 20 = 80. \\]\n\nSimplify the left side:\n\n\\[ 70 - 20 = 50, \\]\n\nso the equation becomes:\n\n\\[ 50 + m + n = 80. \\]\n\nSubtract 50 from both sides:\n\n\\[ m + n = 30. \\]\n\nWe are also given that \\( m = 2n \\). Substitute \\( m = 2n \\) into the equation \\( m + n = 30 \\):\n\n\\[ 2n + n = 30. \\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[ 3n = 30. \\]\n\nDivide both sides by 3:\n\n\\[ n = 10. \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( n \\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
"To solve the inequality \\( x^{-1} > x \\), we first rewrite it in a more manageable form. The inequality can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{x} > x\n\\]\n\nMultiplying both sides by \\( x \\) (assuming \\( x \\neq 0 \\)), we obtain:\n\n\\[\n1 > x^2\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nx^2 < 1\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x \\) is a positive integer, the only possible value for \\( x \\) that satisfies \\( x^2 < 1 \\) is \\( x = 1 \\).\n\nLet's verify:\n\n- If \\( x = 1 \\), then \\( x^{-1} = 1^{-1} = 1 \\) and \\( x = 1 \\). The inequality \\( 1 > 1 \\) is false.\n\nThus, there are no positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which \\( x^{-1} > x \\).\n\nTherefore, the number of positive integer values of \\( x \\) that satisfy the inequality is \\(\\boxed{0}\\)."
'To solve for \\( a + b \\), we need to use the given conditions for the function \\( f(x) \\).\n\nFirst, consider the condition \\( f(-4) = -\\frac{60}{13} \\). Since \\( x = -4 \\) falls under the case \\( x \\le -4 \\), we use the expression \\( f(x) = \\frac{a}{b}x \\). Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\nf(-4) = \\frac{a}{b}(-4) = -\\frac{4a}{b} = -\\frac{60}{13}\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( \\frac{a}{b} \\), we get:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{4a}{b} = \\frac{60}{13} \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad \\frac{a}{b} = \\frac{15}{13}\n\\]\n\nNext, consider the condition \\( f(4) = 3120 \\). Since \\( x = 4 \\) falls under the case \\( x > -4 \\), we use the expression \\( f(x) = abx^2 \\). Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\nf(4) = ab(4)^2 = 16ab = 3120\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( ab \\), we get:\n\n\\[\nab = \\frac{3120}{16} = 195\n\\]\n\nNow, we have the system of equations:\n\n1. \\(\\frac{a}{b} = \\frac{15}{13}\\)\n2. \\(ab = 195\\)\n\nFrom the first equation, express \\( a \\) in terms of \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{15}{13}b\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( a \\) into the second equation:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{15}{13}b\\right)b = 195\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{15}{13}b^2 = 195\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 13 to clear the fraction:\n\n\\[\n15b^2 = 195 \\times 13\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( 195 \\times 13 \\):\n\n\\[\n195 \\times 13 = 2535\n\\]\n\nSo, we have:\n\n\\[\n15b^2 = 2535\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 15:\n\n\\[\nb^2 = \\frac{2535}{15} = 169\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we find:\n\n\\[\nb = \\sqrt{169} = 13\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( b = 13 \\) back into the expression for \\( a \\):\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{15}{13} \\times 13 = 15\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( a + b = 15 + 13 = \\boxed{28} \\).'
'To find when the ball hits the ground, we need to determine when the height \\( y \\) is equal to 0. We set the equation \\( y = -16t^2 - 60t + 54 \\) equal to 0 and solve for \\( t \\):\n\n\\[\n-16t^2 - 60t + 54 = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation of the form \\( at^2 + bt + c = 0 \\), where \\( a = -16 \\), \\( b = -60 \\), and \\( c = 54 \\). We can use the quadratic formula to solve for \\( t \\):\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values of \\( a \\), \\( b \\), and \\( c \\) into the formula:\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{-(-60) \\pm \\sqrt{(-60)^2 - 4(-16)(54)}}{2(-16)}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{60 \\pm \\sqrt{3600 + 3456}}{-32}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{60 \\pm \\sqrt{7056}}{-32}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the square root of 7056:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{7056} = 84\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back into the equation:\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{60 \\pm 84}{-32}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two possible solutions for \\( t \\):\n\n1. \\( t = \\frac{60 + 84}{-32} = \\frac{144}{-32} = -4.5 \\)\n2. \\( t = \\frac{60 - 84}{-32} = \\frac{-24}{-32} = 0.75 \\)\n\nSince time cannot be negative, we discard \\( t = -4.5 \\). Therefore, the ball hits the ground at \\( t = 0.75 \\) seconds.\n\nThe answer is \\(\\boxed{0.75}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\lfloor 14.6 \\rfloor - \\lceil -14.6 \\rceil\\), we need to understand the floor and ceiling functions.\n\n1. **Floor Function**: \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor\\) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(x\\).\n   - For \\(14.6\\), the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(14.6\\) is \\(14\\).\n   - Therefore, \\(\\lfloor 14.6 \\rfloor = 14\\).\n\n2. **Ceiling Function**: \\(\\lceil x \\rceil\\) is the smallest integer greater than or equal to \\(x\\).\n   - For \\(-14.6\\), the smallest integer greater than or equal to \\(-14.6\\) is \\(-14\\).\n   - Therefore, \\(\\lceil -14.6 \\rceil = -14\\).\n\nNow, we substitute these values into the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\lfloor 14.6 \\rfloor - \\lceil -14.6 \\rceil = 14 - (-14) = 14 + 14 = 28\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{28}\\).'
'The original dimensions of the TV screen are 24 inches by 16 inches. The original area is:\n\n\\[ \n\\text{Original Area} = 24 \\times 16 = 384 \\text{ square inches}.\n\\]\n\nEach dimension is increased by 20%. Therefore, the new dimensions are:\n\n\\[\n\\text{New Length} = 24 + 0.2 \\times 24 = 24 \\times 1.2 = 28.8 \\text{ inches},\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\text{New Width} = 16 + 0.2 \\times 16 = 16 \\times 1.2 = 19.2 \\text{ inches}.\n\\]\n\nThe new area is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{New Area} = 28.8 \\times 19.2.\n\\]\n\nCalculating the new area:\n\n\\[\n28.8 \\times 19.2 = 552.96 \\text{ square inches}.\n\\]\n\nThe increase in area is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Increase in Area} = 552.96 - 384 = 168.96 \\text{ square inches}.\n\\]\n\nThe percent increase in area is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Percent Increase} = \\left(\\frac{168.96}{384}\\right) \\times 100\\%.\n\\]\n\nCalculating the percent increase:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{168.96}{384} \\approx 0.44.\n\\]\n\n\\[\n0.44 \\times 100\\% = 44\\%.\n\\]\n\nThus, the area is increased by \\(\\boxed{44\\%}\\).'
'To expand the expression \\((q-5)(3r+6)\\), we use the distributive property, also known as the FOIL method for binomials. This involves multiplying each term in the first binomial by each term in the second binomial:\n\n1. Multiply \\(q\\) by \\(3r\\): \n   \\[\n   q \\cdot 3r = 3qr\n   \\]\n\n2. Multiply \\(q\\) by \\(6\\): \n   \\[\n   q \\cdot 6 = 6q\n   \\]\n\n3. Multiply \\(-5\\) by \\(3r\\): \n   \\[\n   -5 \\cdot 3r = -15r\n   \\]\n\n4. Multiply \\(-5\\) by \\(6\\): \n   \\[\n   -5 \\cdot 6 = -30\n   \\]\n\nNow, combine all these results to get the expanded expression:\n\\[\n3qr + 6q - 15r - 30\n\\]\n\nThus, the expanded form of \\((q-5)(3r+6)\\) is:\n\\[\n3qr + 6q - 15r - 30\n\\]'
'To solve this problem, we need to calculate the total distance the ball travels after being dropped and bouncing back multiple times.\n\n1. **Initial Drop:**\n   - The ball is dropped from a height of 16 feet. This is the first distance it travels.\n\n2. **Bounces:**\n   - After the first drop, the ball bounces back to half the height it fell from. So, after the first bounce, it reaches a height of \\( \\frac{16}{2} = 8 \\) feet.\n   - It then falls again from 8 feet, bounces back to \\( \\frac{8}{2} = 4 \\) feet, and so on.\n\n3. **Calculating Total Distance:**\n   - The ball hits the floor for the first time after falling 16 feet.\n   - It then travels up 8 feet and falls 8 feet, totaling 16 feet for the first bounce.\n   - It travels up 4 feet and falls 4 feet, totaling 8 feet for the second bounce.\n   - It travels up 2 feet and falls 2 feet, totaling 4 feet for the third bounce.\n   - It travels up 1 foot and falls 1 foot, totaling 2 feet for the fourth bounce.\n   - It travels up 0.5 feet and falls 0.5 feet, totaling 1 foot for the fifth bounce.\n\n4. **Summing the Distances:**\n   - Initial drop: 16 feet\n   - First bounce: 8 + 8 = 16 feet\n   - Second bounce: 4 + 4 = 8 feet\n   - Third bounce: 2 + 2 = 4 feet\n   - Fourth bounce: 1 + 1 = 2 feet\n   - Fifth bounce: 0.5 + 0.5 = 1 foot\n\nAdding these distances gives the total distance traveled by the ball:\n\n\\[\n16 + 16 + 8 + 4 + 2 + 1 = 47 \\text{ feet}\n\\]\n\nThus, the ball will have traveled a total of 47 feet when it hits the floor for the sixth time. The answer is \\(\\boxed{47}\\) feet.'
"To solve this problem, we start by using the equation of the circle centered at \\((5, 15)\\) with radius \\(\\sqrt{130}\\). The equation of the circle is:\n\n\\[\n(x - 5)^2 + (y - 15)^2 = 130\n\\]\n\nWe are given that the point \\(Q = (x, y)\\) is on the circle and that the \\(x\\)-coordinate is twice the \\(y\\)-coordinate, i.e., \\(x = 2y\\). We substitute \\(x = 2y\\) into the circle's equation:\n\n\\[\n(2y - 5)^2 + (y - 15)^2 = 130\n\\]\n\nExpanding both squares, we have:\n\n\\[\n(4y^2 - 20y + 25) + (y^2 - 30y + 225) = 130\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n4y^2 + y^2 - 20y - 30y + 25 + 225 = 130\n\\]\n\n\\[\n5y^2 - 50y + 250 = 130\n\\]\n\nSubtract 130 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n5y^2 - 50y + 120 = 0\n\\]\n\nDivide the entire equation by 5 to simplify:\n\n\\[\ny^2 - 10y + 24 = 0\n\\]\n\nNow, we solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = -10\\), and \\(c = 24\\). Plug these values into the formula:\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{-(-10) \\pm \\sqrt{(-10)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 24}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{10 \\pm \\sqrt{100 - 96}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{10 \\pm \\sqrt{4}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{10 \\pm 2}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two possible values for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{12}{2} = 6 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad y = \\frac{8}{2} = 4\n\\]\n\nSince \\(x = 2y\\), we find the corresponding \\(x\\)-values:\n\n- If \\(y = 6\\), then \\(x = 2 \\times 6 = 12\\).\n- If \\(y = 4\\), then \\(x = 2 \\times 4 = 8\\).\n\nThe maximum possible value for \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{12}\\)."
'To find the integer that lies between \\(\\sqrt[3]{-45}\\) and \\(\\sqrt[3]{-101}\\), we first need to approximate these cube roots.\n\n1. **Estimate \\(\\sqrt[3]{-45}\\):**\n\n   We know that \\(-3^3 = -27\\) and \\(-4^3 = -64\\). Since \\(-45\\) is between \\(-27\\) and \\(-64\\), \\(\\sqrt[3]{-45}\\) is between \\(-3\\) and \\(-4\\).\n\n   To get a better approximation, we can check:\n   \\[\n   (-3.5)^3 = -3.5 \\times -3.5 \\times -3.5 = -12.25 \\times -3.5 = -42.875\n   \\]\n   Since \\(-42.875\\) is close to \\(-45\\), \\(\\sqrt[3]{-45}\\) is slightly less than \\(-3.5\\).\n\n2. **Estimate \\(\\sqrt[3]{-101}\\):**\n\n   We know that \\(-4^3 = -64\\) and \\(-5^3 = -125\\). Since \\(-101\\) is between \\(-64\\) and \\(-125\\), \\(\\sqrt[3]{-101}\\) is between \\(-4\\) and \\(-5\\).\n\n   To get a better approximation, we can check:\n   \\[\n   (-4.5)^3 = -4.5 \\times -4.5 \\times -4.5 = -20.25 \\times -4.5 = -91.125\n   \\]\n   Since \\(-91.125\\) is less than \\(-101\\), \\(\\sqrt[3]{-101}\\) is slightly less than \\(-4.5\\).\n\n3. **Determine the integer between the two cube roots:**\n\n   From the approximations, \\(\\sqrt[3]{-45}\\) is slightly less than \\(-3.5\\) and \\(\\sqrt[3]{-101}\\) is slightly less than \\(-4.5\\). Therefore, the integer that lies between these two values is \\(-4\\).\n\nThus, the integer that lies between \\(\\sqrt[3]{-45}\\) and \\(\\sqrt[3]{-101}\\) is \\(\\boxed{-4}\\).'
'To find the length of a segment with endpoints \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\), we use the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nFor the points \\((1, 2)\\) and \\((-4, -10)\\), we have:\n\n- \\(x_1 = 1\\), \\(y_1 = 2\\)\n- \\(x_2 = -4\\), \\(y_2 = -10\\)\n\nSubstituting these values into the distance formula gives:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{((-4) - 1)^2 + ((-10) - 2)^2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(-5)^2 + (-12)^2}\n\\]\n\nCalculating the squares:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{25 + 144}\n\\]\n\nAdding the results:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{169}\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root:\n\n\\[\nd = 13\n\\]\n\nThus, the length of the segment is \\(\\boxed{13}\\) units.'
'To find the value of \\( x \\) for which \\( f(g(x)) = g(f(x)) \\), we first need to compute each composition.\n\nFirst, compute \\( f(g(x)) \\):\n\\[\ng(x) = x^2 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad f(g(x)) = f(x^2) = x^2 + 2\n\\]\n\nNext, compute \\( g(f(x)) \\):\n\\[\nf(x) = x + 2 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad g(f(x)) = g(x + 2) = (x + 2)^2 = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nNow, set the two expressions equal to each other:\n\\[\nx^2 + 2 = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nSubtract \\( x^2 \\) from both sides:\n\\[\n2 = 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nSubtract 4 from both sides:\n\\[\n-2 = 4x\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 4:\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x \\) for which \\( f(g(x)) = g(f(x)) \\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{1}{2}}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\log_{5^2}5^4\\), we start by using the change of base formula for logarithms. The expression can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{5^2}5^4 = \\frac{\\log_{5}5^4}{\\log_{5}5^2}\n\\]\n\nWe know that \\(\\log_{5}5^4 = 4\\) because \\(5^4\\) is the power of 5 that gives 5 raised to the fourth power. Similarly, \\(\\log_{5}5^2 = 2\\) because \\(5^2\\) is the power of 5 that gives 5 squared.\n\nSubstituting these values into the expression, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\log_{5}5^4}{\\log_{5}5^2} = \\frac{4}{2} = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\log_{5^2}5^4\\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'

We can solve it using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -4 \\), and \\( c = -1 \\). Plugging these values into the formula gives:\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{-(-4) \\pm \\sqrt{(-4)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-1)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 + 4}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{20}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{4 \\cdot 5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{4 \\pm 2\\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 2 \\pm \\sqrt{5}\n\\]\n\nThus, there are two solutions for \\( y \\): \\( y = 2 + \\sqrt{5} \\) and \\( y = 2 - \\sqrt{5} \\). Therefore, the graph of the parabola has two \\( y \\)-intercepts.\n\nThe number of \\( y \\)-intercepts is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
'To rewrite the expression \\(6y^2 - y - 51\\) in the form \\((3Ay + B)(y - C)\\), we first expand the expression:\n\n\\[\n(3Ay + B)(y - C) = 3Ay^2 - 3ACy + By - BC\n\\]\n\nThis must be equal to the original expression:\n\n\\[\n6y^2 - y - 51\n\\]\n\nBy comparing coefficients, we have:\n\n1. \\(3A = 6\\)\n2. \\(-3AC + B = -1\\)\n3. \\(-BC = -51\\)\n\nFrom the first equation, we solve for \\(A\\):\n\n\\[\n3A = 6 \\implies A = 2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(A = 2\\) into the third equation:\n\n\\[\n-BC = -51 \\implies BC = 51\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\(A = 2\\) into the second equation:\n\n\\[\n-3(2)C + B = -1 \\implies -6C + B = -1 \\implies B = 6C - 1\n\\]\n\nWe have two equations:\n\n1. \\(BC = 51\\)\n2. \\(B = 6C - 1\\)\n\nSubstitute \\(B = 6C - 1\\) into \\(BC = 51\\):\n\n\\[\n(6C - 1)C = 51\n\\]\n\nExpanding and rearranging gives:\n\n\\[\n6C^2 - C = 51 \\implies 6C^2 - C - 51 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nC = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a = 6\\), \\(b = -1\\), and \\(c = -51\\). Calculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = (-1)^2 - 4 \\cdot 6 \\cdot (-51) = 1 + 1224 = 1225\n\\]\n\nThe square root of 1225 is 35. Thus, the solutions for \\(C\\) are:\n\n\\[\nC = \\frac{1 \\pm 35}{12}\n\\]\n\nCalculating the two possible values for \\(C\\):\n\n\\[\nC = \\frac{1 + 35}{12} = \\frac{36}{12} = 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\nC = \\frac{1 - 35}{12} = \\frac{-34}{12} = -\\frac{17}{6} \\quad (\\text{not an integer})\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(C = 3\\). Substitute \\(C = 3\\) back to find \\(B\\):\n\n\\[\nB = 6C - 1 = 6 \\times 3 - 1 = 18 - 1 = 17\n\\]\n\nNow, we have \\(A = 2\\), \\(B = 17\\), and \\(C = 3\\). We need to find \\((AC)^2 - B\\):\n\n\\[\nAC = 2 \\times 3 = 6\n\\]\n\n\\[\n(AC)^2 = 6^2 = 36\n\\]\n\n\\[\n(AC)^2 - B = 36 - 17 = 19\n\\]\n\nThus, the answer is \\(\\boxed{19}\\).'
'To rewrite the expression \\(5x - |x - 5|\\) without using absolute value signs, we need to consider the condition given: \\(x < 5\\).\n\nThe absolute value expression \\(|x - 5|\\) can be rewritten based on the value of \\(x\\) relative to 5. Specifically:\n\n- If \\(x \\geq 5\\), then \\(|x - 5| = x - 5\\).\n- If \\(x < 5\\), then \\(|x - 5| = -(x - 5) = 5 - x\\).\n\nSince we are given that \\(x < 5\\), we use the second case:\n\n\\[\n|x - 5| = 5 - x\n\\]\n\nSubstituting this into the original expression, we have:\n\n\\[\n5x - |x - 5| = 5x - (5 - x)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expression:\n\n\\[\n5x - 5 + x = 6x - 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression \\(5x - |x - 5|\\) can be rewritten as \\(6x - 5\\) when \\(x < 5\\). Therefore, the expression without absolute value signs is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{6x - 5}\n\\]'
'To solve the equation \\(2^{x + 2} = 32\\), we first express 32 as a power of 2. We know that:\n\n\\[ 32 = 2^5. \\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[ 2^{x + 2} = 2^5. \\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we can equate the exponents:\n\n\\[ x + 2 = 5. \\]\n\nSolving for \\(x\\), we subtract 2 from both sides:\n\n\\[ x = 5 - 2 = 3. \\]\n\nTherefore, the integer \\(x\\) that satisfies the equation is \\(\\boxed{3}\\).'
'Given that \\( a < b \\), we need to find the value of \\( |a-b| + a + b \\).\n\nFirst, we evaluate the absolute value expression. Since \\( a < b \\), it follows that \\( a - b < 0 \\). Therefore, the absolute value \\( |a-b| \\) is equal to \\( -(a-b) \\), which simplifies to \\( b-a \\).\n\nNow, substitute this into the expression:\n\n\\[\n|a-b| + a + b = (b-a) + a + b\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression by combining like terms:\n\n\\[\nb - a + a + b = b + b = 2b\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( |a-b| + a + b \\) is \\(\\boxed{2b}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to establish the relationships between the costs of cookies, brownies, and cupcakes.\n\n1. **Cookies and Brownies:**\n   - Six cookies cost the same as 2 brownies.\n   - Therefore, the cost of 1 brownie is equivalent to the cost of 3 cookies.\n\n2. **Brownies and Cupcakes:**\n   - Four brownies cost the same as 10 cupcakes.\n   - Therefore, the cost of 1 brownie is equivalent to the cost of \\( \\frac{10}{4} = 2.5 \\) cupcakes.\n\nNow, let's find out how many cupcakes Bob can buy for the price of eighteen cookies:\n\n- Since 1 brownie costs the same as 3 cookies, the cost of 18 cookies is equivalent to the cost of \\( \\frac{18}{3} = 6 \\) brownies.\n\n- Since 1 brownie costs the same as 2.5 cupcakes, the cost of 6 brownies is equivalent to the cost of \\( 6 \\times 2.5 = 15 \\) cupcakes.\n\nTherefore, Bob can buy \\(\\boxed{15}\\) cupcakes for the price of eighteen cookies."
'To find the maximum value of the quadratic function \\( f(x) = -x^2 - 8x + 12 \\), we can use the vertex formula for a parabola. The function is in the form \\( ax^2 + bx + c \\), where \\( a = -1 \\), \\( b = -8 \\), and \\( c = 12 \\).\n\nThe vertex of a parabola given by \\( ax^2 + bx + c \\) is at \\( x = -\\frac{b}{2a} \\). Substituting the values of \\( a \\) and \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{-8}{2 \\times -1} = \\frac{8}{-2} = -4\n\\]\n\nNow, we substitute \\( x = -4 \\) back into the function to find the maximum value:\n\n\\[\nf(-4) = -(-4)^2 - 8(-4) + 12\n\\]\n\nCalculating each term:\n\n\\[\n(-4)^2 = 16 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad -(-4)^2 = -16\n\\]\n\\[\n-8(-4) = 32\n\\]\n\nThus, the function value is:\n\n\\[\nf(-4) = -16 + 32 + 12 = 28\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the maximum value of the function \\( -x^2 - 8x + 12 \\) is \\(\\boxed{28}\\).'
'To find the value of \\(\\frac{d}{c}\\), we start by solving the system of equations:\n\n\\[\nd - 6c = 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2d - 9c = 20\n\\]\n\nFirst, we can express \\(d\\) in terms of \\(c\\) from the first equation:\n\n\\[\nd = 6c + 4\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\(d\\) into the second equation:\n\n\\[\n2(6c + 4) - 9c = 20\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\(c\\):\n\n\\[\n12c + 8 - 9c = 20\n\\]\n\n\\[\n3c + 8 = 20\n\\]\n\n\\[\n3c = 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\nc = 4\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\(c = 4\\), substitute back to find \\(d\\):\n\n\\[\nd = 6c + 4 = 6(4) + 4 = 24 + 4 = 28\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\(\\frac{d}{c}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{d}{c} = \\frac{28}{4} = 7\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{d}{c}\\) is \\(\\boxed{7}\\).'
'To solve the problem, we need to find the values of \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\) that satisfy the given equations:\n\n1. \\(a + \\frac{1}{b} = \\frac{22}{7}\\)\n2. \\(b + \\frac{1}{c} = 8\\)\n3. \\(abc = 21\\)\n\nWe are tasked with finding \\(c + \\frac{1}{a}\\).\n\n**Step 1: Solve for \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) using the first equation.**\n\nFrom the first equation, we have:\n\\[\na + \\frac{1}{b} = \\frac{22}{7}\n\\]\nRewriting, we get:\n\\[\na = \\frac{22}{7} - \\frac{1}{b}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(a\\) is an integer, \\(\\frac{22}{7} - \\frac{1}{b}\\) must also be an integer. Let \\(a = 3\\) (since \\(\\frac{22}{7} \\approx 3.14\\)), then:\n\\[\n3 = \\frac{22}{7} - \\frac{1}{b}\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{b} = \\frac{22}{7} - 3 = \\frac{22}{7} - \\frac{21}{7} = \\frac{1}{7}\n\\]\nThus, \\(b = 7\\).\n\n**Step 2: Solve for \\(c\\) using the second equation.**\n\nFrom the second equation, we have:\n\\[\nb + \\frac{1}{c} = 8\n\\]\nSubstituting \\(b = 7\\), we get:\n\\[\n7 + \\frac{1}{c} = 8\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{c} = 1\n\\]\nThus, \\(c = 1\\).\n\n**Step 3: Verify the product \\(abc = 21\\).**\n\nWe have found \\(a = 3\\), \\(b = 7\\), and \\(c = 1\\). Check the product:\n\\[\nabc = 3 \\times 7 \\times 1 = 21\n\\]\nThis satisfies the third condition.\n\n**Step 4: Calculate \\(c + \\frac{1}{a}\\).**\n\nNow, we need to find:\n\\[\nc + \\frac{1}{a} = 1 + \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{3}{3} + \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{4}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the answer is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{4}{3}}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the greatest three-digit number "abc" such that the digits \\(4, a, b\\) form a geometric sequence and the digits \\(b, c, 5\\) form an arithmetic sequence.\n\n### Step 1: Analyze the geometric sequence \\(4, a, b\\)\n\nIn a geometric sequence, the ratio between consecutive terms is constant. Let the common ratio be \\(r\\). Then:\n\n\\[\na = 4r \\quad \\text{and} \\quad b = 4r^2\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Analyze the arithmetic sequence \\(b, c, 5\\)\n\nIn an arithmetic sequence, the difference between consecutive terms is constant. Let the common difference be \\(d\\). Then:\n\n\\[\nc = b + d \\quad \\text{and} \\quad 5 = c + d\n\\]\n\nFrom the second equation, we have:\n\n\\[\n5 = (b + d) + d = b + 2d \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad 2d = 5 - b \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad d = \\frac{5 - b}{2}\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Combine the conditions\n\nSince \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\) are digits (0 through 9), we have:\n\n1. \\(a = 4r\\) must be a digit, so \\(0 \\leq 4r \\leq 9\\).\n2. \\(b = 4r^2\\) must be a digit, so \\(0 \\leq 4r^2 \\leq 9\\).\n3. \\(c = b + d\\) must be a digit, so \\(0 \\leq b + \\frac{5 - b}{2} \\leq 9\\).\n\n### Step 4: Solve for \\(r\\) and find the greatest \\(abc\\)\n\nSince \\(b = 4r^2\\) and \\(b\\) is a digit, we test integer values of \\(r\\) to maximize \\(b\\).\n\n- If \\(r = 1\\), then \\(a = 4 \\times 1 = 4\\) and \\(b = 4 \\times 1^2 = 4\\).\n- If \\(r = \\frac{3}{2}\\), then \\(a = 4 \\times \\frac{3}{2} = 6\\) and \\(b = 4 \\times \\left(\\frac{3}{2}\\right)^2 = 9\\).\n\nFor \\(r = \\frac{3}{2}\\), we have \\(b = 9\\).\n\n### Step 5: Check the arithmetic sequence for \\(b = 9\\)\n\nIf \\(b = 9\\), then:\n\n\\[\nd = \\frac{5 - 9}{2} = -2\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(c = b + d = 9 - 2 = 7\\).\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThe digits \\(a = 6\\), \\(b = 9\\), and \\(c = 7\\) satisfy both the geometric and arithmetic sequence conditions. Therefore, the greatest three-digit number "abc" is \\(\\boxed{697}\\).'
'To rewrite the quadratic \\(x^2 - 6x + 66\\) in the form \\((x+b)^2 + c\\), we need to complete the square.\n\nStart with the quadratic expression:\n\\[ x^2 - 6x + 66. \\]\n\nTo complete the square, focus on the \\(x^2 - 6x\\) part. Take half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), which is \\(-6\\), and square it:\n\\[ \\left(\\frac{-6}{2}\\right)^2 = 9. \\]\n\nAdd and subtract this square inside the expression:\n\\[ x^2 - 6x + 9 - 9 + 66. \\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\\[ (x - 3)^2 - 9 + 66. \\]\n\nSimplify the constant terms:\n\\[ (x - 3)^2 + 57. \\]\n\nThus, the quadratic can be expressed in the form \\((x+b)^2 + c\\) where \\(b = -3\\) and \\(c = 57\\).\n\nTherefore, \\(b + c = -3 + 57 = 54\\).\n\nThe value of \\(b+c\\) is \\(\\boxed{54}\\).'
"To determine which letters could be portions of the graph of a function, we need to consider the vertical line test. A graph represents a function if and only if no vertical line intersects the graph at more than one point.\n\nLet's analyze each letter:\n\n- **A**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **B**: Fails the vertical line test (vertical line can intersect at two points).\n- **C**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **D**: Fails the vertical line test (vertical line can intersect at two points).\n- **E**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **F**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **G**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **H**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **I**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **J**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **K**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **L**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **M**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **N**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **O**: Fails the vertical line test (vertical line can intersect at two points).\n- **P**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **Q**: Fails the vertical line test (vertical line can intersect at two points).\n- **R**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **S**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **T**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **U**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **V**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **W**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **X**: Fails the vertical line test (vertical line can intersect at two points).\n- **Y**: Passes the vertical line test.\n- **Z**: Passes the vertical line test.\n\nThe letters that could be portions of the graph of a function, in alphabetical order, are:\n\n\\[\n\\textsf{ACEFGHIJKLMNPQRSTUVWYZ}\n\\]"
'To solve the inequality \\(x^2 - 5x - 4 \\le 10\\), we first rewrite it as:\n\n\\[ x^2 - 5x - 4 - 10 \\le 0 \\]\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n\\[ x^2 - 5x - 14 \\le 0. \\]\n\nNext, we solve the corresponding equation:\n\n\\[ x^2 - 5x - 14 = 0. \\]\n\nWe use the quadratic formula \\(x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\\), where \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = -5\\), and \\(c = -14\\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-(-5) \\pm \\sqrt{(-5)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-14)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{5 \\pm \\sqrt{25 + 56}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{5 \\pm \\sqrt{81}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{5 \\pm 9}{2}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives the solutions:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{5 + 9}{2} = 7 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x = \\frac{5 - 9}{2} = -2.\n\\]\n\nThe solutions to the equation are \\(x = 7\\) and \\(x = -2\\). These are the points where the quadratic expression changes sign. We need to determine the intervals where the inequality \\(x^2 - 5x - 14 \\le 0\\) holds.\n\nWe test intervals determined by the roots \\(-2\\) and \\(7\\):\n\n1. For \\(x < -2\\), choose \\(x = -3\\):\n   \\[\n   (-3)^2 - 5(-3) - 14 = 9 + 15 - 14 = 10 > 0.\n   \\]\n\n2. For \\(-2 \\le x \\le 7\\), choose \\(x = 0\\):\n   \\[\n   0^2 - 5(0) - 14 = -14 \\le 0.\n   \\]\n\n3. For \\(x > 7\\), choose \\(x = 8\\):\n   \\[\n   8^2 - 5(8) - 14 = 64 - 40 - 14 = 10 > 0.\n   \\]\n\nThe inequality \\(x^2 - 5x - 14 \\le 0\\) holds for \\(-2 \\le x \\le 7\\).\n\nThus, the solution in interval notation is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{[-2, 7]}\n\\]'
"To solve for \\( A + M + C \\), we start by expressing the two numbers \\( AMC10 \\) and \\( AMC12 \\) in terms of their digits:\n\n\\[\nAMC10 = 10000A + 1000M + 100C + 10 \\times 1 + 0 = 10000A + 1000M + 100C + 10\n\\]\n\n\\[\nAMC12 = 10000A + 1000M + 100C + 10 \\times 1 + 2 = 10000A + 1000M + 100C + 12\n\\]\n\nThe sum of these two numbers is given as:\n\n\\[\nAMC10 + AMC12 = 123422\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the expressions for \\( AMC10 \\) and \\( AMC12 \\):\n\n\\[\n(10000A + 1000M + 100C + 10) + (10000A + 1000M + 100C + 12) = 123422\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the left side:\n\n\\[\n20000A + 2000M + 200C + 22 = 123422\n\\]\n\nSubtract 22 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n20000A + 2000M + 200C = 123400\n\\]\n\nDivide the entire equation by 200:\n\n\\[\n100A + 10M + C = 617\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find digits \\( A \\), \\( M \\), and \\( C \\) such that the equation holds. We know that \\( A \\), \\( M \\), and \\( C \\) are digits (0 through 9).\n\nLet's solve for \\( A \\), \\( M \\), and \\( C \\):\n\n1. **Estimate \\( A \\):** Since \\( 100A \\) is the largest term, start by estimating \\( A \\). The largest possible value for \\( 100A \\) that is less than or equal to 617 is 600, which implies \\( A = 6 \\).\n\n2. **Substitute \\( A = 6 \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   100 \\times 6 + 10M + C = 617\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   600 + 10M + C = 617\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   10M + C = 17\n   \\]\n\n3. **Solve for \\( M \\) and \\( C \\):** We need \\( 10M + C = 17 \\). Since \\( M \\) and \\( C \\) are digits, try possible values for \\( M \\):\n\n   - If \\( M = 1 \\), then \\( 10 \\times 1 + C = 17 \\) gives \\( C = 7 \\).\n\nThus, \\( A = 6 \\), \\( M = 1 \\), and \\( C = 7 \\).\n\nFinally, calculate \\( A + M + C \\):\n\n\\[\nA + M + C = 6 + 1 + 7 = 14\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( A + M + C \\) is \\(\\boxed{14}\\)."
'To solve this problem, we first determine the total amount of work required to mow the lawn in terms of person-hours. If 5 people can mow the lawn in 12 hours, the total work is:\n\n\\[ 5 \\text{ people} \\times 12 \\text{ hours} = 60 \\text{ person-hours}. \\]\n\nNow, we want to find out how many people are needed to complete the same amount of work in just 3 hours. Let \\( n \\) be the number of people needed. The equation for the total work is:\n\n\\[ n \\text{ people} \\times 3 \\text{ hours} = 60 \\text{ person-hours}. \\]\n\nSolving for \\( n \\), we have:\n\n\\[ n \\times 3 = 60 \\]\n\n\\[ n = \\frac{60}{3} = 20. \\]\n\nTherefore, 20 people are needed to mow the lawn in 3 hours. Since we already have 5 people, the number of additional people needed is:\n\n\\[ 20 - 5 = 15. \\]\n\nThus, 15 more people are needed. The answer is \\(\\boxed{15}\\).'
'To find \\( x^3 - y^3 \\), we can use the identity:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = (x-y)(x^2 + xy + y^2)\n\\]\n\nWe are given \\( x-y = 6 \\) and \\( x^2 + y^2 = 24 \\). To use the identity, we need to find \\( xy \\).\n\nWe start by squaring the equation \\( x-y = 6 \\):\n\n\\[\n(x-y)^2 = x^2 - 2xy + y^2 = 36\n\\]\n\nWe know \\( x^2 + y^2 = 24 \\). Using these two equations, we can solve for \\( xy \\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 = 24\n\\]\n\\[\nx^2 - 2xy + y^2 = 36\n\\]\n\nSubtract the first equation from the second:\n\n\\[\n(x^2 - 2xy + y^2) - (x^2 + y^2) = 36 - 24\n\\]\n\\[\n-2xy = 12\n\\]\n\\[\nxy = -6\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x-y = 6 \\), \\( x^2 + y^2 = 24 \\), and \\( xy = -6 \\) into the identity:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = (x-y)(x^2 + xy + y^2)\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( x^2 + xy + y^2 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 + xy + y^2 = x^2 + y^2 + xy = 24 + (-6) = 18\n\\]\n\nNow substitute back into the identity:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = 6 \\times 18 = 108\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^3 - y^3 \\) is \\(\\boxed{108}\\).'
'To evaluate the expression \\(\\sqrt[3]{12} \\times \\sqrt[3]{20} \\times \\sqrt[3]{15} \\times \\sqrt[3]{60}\\), we can use the property of cube roots that states \\(\\sqrt[3]{a} \\times \\sqrt[3]{b} = \\sqrt[3]{a \\times b}\\). Applying this property, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[3]{12} \\times \\sqrt[3]{20} \\times \\sqrt[3]{15} \\times \\sqrt[3]{60} = \\sqrt[3]{12 \\times 20 \\times 15 \\times 60}\n\\]\n\nFirst, we calculate the product inside the cube root:\n\n\\[\n12 \\times 20 \\times 15 \\times 60\n\\]\n\nWe can break down each number into its prime factors:\n\n- \\(12 = 2^2 \\times 3\\)\n- \\(20 = 2^2 \\times 5\\)\n- \\(15 = 3 \\times 5\\)\n- \\(60 = 2^2 \\times 3 \\times 5\\)\n\nNow, multiply these factorizations together:\n\n\\[\n(2^2 \\times 3) \\times (2^2 \\times 5) \\times (3 \\times 5) \\times (2^2 \\times 3 \\times 5)\n\\]\n\nCombine all the factors:\n\n\\[\n2^{2+2+2} \\times 3^{1+1+1} \\times 5^{1+1+1} = 2^6 \\times 3^3 \\times 5^3\n\\]\n\nNow, take the cube root of the product:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[3]{2^6 \\times 3^3 \\times 5^3} = \\sqrt[3]{2^6} \\times \\sqrt[3]{3^3} \\times \\sqrt[3]{5^3}\n\\]\n\nCalculate each cube root:\n\n- \\(\\sqrt[3]{2^6} = 2^{6/3} = 2^2 = 4\\)\n- \\(\\sqrt[3]{3^3} = 3^{3/3} = 3\\)\n- \\(\\sqrt[3]{5^3} = 5^{3/3} = 5\\)\n\nMultiply these results together:\n\n\\[\n4 \\times 3 \\times 5 = 12 \\times 5 = 60\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the original expression is \\(\\boxed{60}\\).'
"Bob's rate of travel is \\(\\frac{m}{h}\\) miles per hour. To find out how many hours it would take him to travel \\(h\\) miles, we set up the equation:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Time} = \\frac{\\text{Distance}}{\\text{Rate}} = \\frac{h}{\\frac{m}{h}} = \\frac{h \\cdot h}{m} = \\frac{h^2}{m}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, it would take him \\(\\frac{h^2}{m}\\) hours to travel \\(h\\) miles. The answer is \\(\\frac{h^2}{m}\\)."
"To find Cal O'Ree's expected weight at the end of ten weeks, we need to calculate his weight after each week, considering a 1% weight loss from the previous week's weight.\n\nInitially, Cal's weight is 244 pounds. Each week, he loses 1% of his weight from the previous week, which means he retains 99% of his weight. Therefore, his weight at the end of each week can be calculated using the formula:\n\n\\[ \\text{Weight after } n \\text{ weeks} = 244 \\times (0.99)^n \\]\n\nWe need to find his weight after 10 weeks:\n\n\\[ \\text{Weight after 10 weeks} = 244 \\times (0.99)^{10} \\]\n\nFirst, calculate \\( (0.99)^{10} \\):\n\n\\[ (0.99)^{10} \\approx 0.904382075 \\]\n\nNow, multiply this by 244:\n\n\\[ 244 \\times 0.904382075 \\approx 220.668 \\]\n\nRounding to the nearest whole number, Cal's expected weight at the end of the ten weeks is:\n\n\\[ \\boxed{221} \\]"
